Principles of Payment Allocation in Multiple Divorces
Establishes the principle for allocating payment when two divorces are mentioned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle for allocating payment in multiple divorces, identifying when the payment is for both divorces or only the second, and explain the usul principle of later speech abrogating earlier.

Core Idea
If payment is mentioned after two divorces, it is for both unless the first has a description incompatible with payment.

In this lesson, we delve into a nuanced rule from the Hanafi school regarding the allocation of payment when a husband pronounces two divorces and mentions a sum of money. The rule, derived from al-Fath and al-Dhakhira, provides a clear method for determining which divorce(s) the payment corresponds to. Understanding this principle is crucial for correctly characterizing the divorces as raj'iy or ba'in.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two divorces and their descriptions
List the two divorces and any attributes attached to each (e.g., 'I own the return', 'ba'in', 'without anything').
2
Check for contradiction with payment
Determine if the description of the first divorce is incompatible with the obligation of payment (e.g., 'raj'iy' inherently means no immediate payment; 'ba'in without anything' also negates payment).
3
Apply the allocation rule
If the first description is incompatible, the payment is exclusively for the second divorce. If compatible or no contradictory description, payment is for both equally.
4
Consider the effect of remarriage before the second divorce
If the husband remarries before the second divorce's time, the second may still occur with a portion of the payment.
5
Understand the underlying usul principle
The principle that later speech abrogates earlier (al-nasikh) is invoked: the later mention of payment overrides the earlier contradictory description.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فالألف مقابل بهما مخالف للمسألة الآتية قريباً) فإنه جعل فيها المال في مقابلة الثانية فقط وهذا هو الموافق للقاعدة الآتية عن الفتح عند قول المتن أنت كذا بألف من قوله الأصل أنه متى ذكر طلاقين وذكر عقيبهما مالاً يكون مقابلاً بهما إلا إذا وصف الأول بما ينافي وجوب المال فيكون مقابلاً بالثاني فقط، وقدم تفاريع هذه المسألة في باب إضافة الطلاق وأنها على وجوه عشرة قوله : وغداً أخرى (بالألف أي إن تزوجها قبل مجيء الغد وإلا تقع غداً أخرى بغير شيء لأنه شرط المال في الثانية لم يوجد وهو زوال الملك عنها بها لزوال الملك بالأولى لكونها بائنة ذخيرة قوله : (فقبلت انصرف البدل إليهما) قال في النهر : وفي الزيادات والذخيرة نص في أنهما بائنتان قوله : (فالبدل ينصرف إليهما) فيكون كل تطليقة بخمسمائة فيكونان بائنتين فتقع في بنصف الألف وغداً أخرى مجاناً إلا أن يتزوجها قبل مجيء الغد فتقع الثانية غداً بنصف الألف. وإنما انصرف البدل إليهما لأنه لا بد من إلغاء الوصف أو البدل وإلغاء المنافي أولى لأنه ذكر أولاً وذكر البدل آخراً والآخر يكون ناسخاً للأول . ولو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة أملك الرجعة أو بائنة بغير شيء وغداً أخرى بألف ينصرف البدل إلى الثانية لأنه قرن بالأولى وصفاً منافياً للبدل، ولو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة وغداً أخرى أملك الرجعة بألف ينصرف إليهما لأنه قرن بالثانية وصفاً منافياً للبدل فينصرف البدل إلى التطليقتين؛ كذا في الذخيرة من الفصل السادس في إضافة الطلاق قوله : (قید به احترازاً عن التأخير أي قيد بالمال وكان الأنسب كما فعل في النهر أن يذكره عند قول المصنف سابقاً والواقع به وبالطلاق على مال بائن قوله : والطلاق رجعي على كل حال) أي سواء كان للتأخير غاية معلومة أو لم يكن .
His statement: 'So the thousand is in exchange for both, contrary to the upcoming issue shortly' – for therein he made the money in exchange for the second only, and this is in agreement with the upcoming rule from al-Fath when the text says 'You are such with a thousand'. The principle: whenever two divorces are mentioned and after them comes money, it is in exchange for both, unless the first is described with something that negates the obligation of money, in which case it is in exchange for the second only. The branches of this issue have been presented in the chapter on addition of divorce, and they are on ten faces. His statement: 'and tomorrow another (with a thousand)' – i.e., if he marries her before the arrival of tomorrow, otherwise tomorrow another occurs with nothing, because the condition of money for the second did not exist, which is the departure of marital authority from her due to the departure of authority by the first since it is ba'in. al-Dhakhira. His statement: 'so she accepted, the payment is allocated to both' – al-Nahr said: In al-Ziyadat and al-Dhakhira there is a text that both are ba'in. His statement: 'the payment is allocated to both' – so each divorce is for five hundred, so both are ba'in. So the first occurs with half a thousand and tomorrow another for free, unless he marries her before the arrival of tomorrow, then the second occurs tomorrow with half a thousand. The payment is allocated to both because it is necessary to cancel either the description or the payment, and cancelling the contradictory is better because it was mentioned first, and the payment was mentioned later, and the later abrogates the earlier. And if he says 'You are divorced now one, I own the return or ba'in with nothing, and tomorrow another with a thousand' – the payment is allocated to the second because he connected to the first a description contradictory to payment. And if he says 'You are divorced now one, and tomorrow another, I own the return, with a thousand' – it is allocated to both because he connected to the second a description contradictory to payment, so the payment is allocated to the two divorces; thus in al-Dhakhira, from the sixth chapter on addition of divorce. His statement: 'He restricted it to avoid deferment' – i.e., he restricted it to money, and it is more appropriate, as done in al-Nahr, to mention it at the statement of the author previously 'and what occurs by it and by divorce for money is ba'in'. His statement: 'and the divorce is raj'iy in all cases' – i.e., whether the deferment has a known term or not.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage provides the underlying principle for allocating payment in multiple divorces, as derived from al-Fath and al-Dhakhira. The rule is: when a husband pronounces two divorces and then mentions money (e.g., 'with a thousand'), the payment is generally for both, unless the first divorce is described in a way that is incompatible with payment (such as being described as 'I own the return' or 'ba'in with nothing'). In such cases, the payment goes exclusively to the second. The commentator explains that if the first divorce is described with a characteristic that contradicts payment (like being free), then that description takes precedence, and the money is only for the second. If the second divorce has a contradictory description, then the money is allocated to both because the contradictory description on the second cannot override both. The passage also discusses the detail of the first case: if the first divorce is ba'in (e.g., by saying 'without anything'), then it occurs immediately without payment, and the second takes the full payment. If the husband remarries before the second divorce's time, the second may still occur with a portion of the payment. The final part reiterates the earlier ruling about deferment: the author restricted the condition to 'money' to exclude deferment, and if deferment is the consideration, the divorce remains raj'iy in all cases, regardless of whether the term is known or not, because deferment is not valid as property.

Key Terms
المنافي (al-munafi): A description that contradicts or is incompatible with the obligation of payment.
الناسخ (al-nasikh): Abrogating; here, the later mention of payment abrogates the earlier description if they conflict.
التفاريع (al-tafari'): Branches or derivative cases from a principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle stated, if a husband says 'أنت طالق الساعة واحدة أملك الرجعة وغداً أخرى بألف', how is the payment allocated?
A) Both divorces get half each
B) The first gets nothing, the second gets the full thousand
C) Both get the full thousand
D) The first gets the full thousand, the second nothing

Key Takeaway
The allocation of payment in multiple divorces follows a clear rule: payment is for both unless the first divorce has a description incompatible with payment, in which case it is only for the second.

The Condition of Mal in Khul' and Multiple Talaq Allocations
Explaining that khul' compensation must be mal and addressing multiple talaqs and deferment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that khul' compensation must be mal, explain why deferment does not qualify, and apply the allocation rule when multiple talaqs are pronounced with a single sum.

Core Idea
In khul', compensation must be actual property; deferment of a debt is not mal, so the divorce remains revocable.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key requirement for khul': the compensation offered by the wife must be genuine property (mal). Mere deferment of an existing debt does not count as mal, so the husband cannot claim compensation, and the divorce remains revocable. The text also shows how compensation is allocated when multiple divorces are pronounced with a single sum, ensuring each divorce receives a portion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage discusses khul' (divorce initiated by wife in exchange for compensation). The ruling is that khul' is valid only if the compensation is mal in the Hanafi sense.
Khul' is mubah (permissible) when needed, but the compensation condition is crucial.
2
Understand the examples of multiple talaqs
The text gives examples where a husband says multiple divorces together with a single sum of compensation. The key is that the compensation is allocated to all divorces mentioned, and each becomes ba'in (irrevocable) even if the wording suggests one is revocable.
For instance, 'You are divorced now one, and tomorrow another, for a thousand' makes both ba'in.
3
Analyze the condition of mal
The passage specifies that compensation must be mal. Deferment (ta'khir) of a debt is not mal—it is merely delaying the claim. Therefore, if a wife offers to defer a debt, it is not valid compensation; the divorce remains raj'iy (revocable).
Hanafi mal includes tangible assets and debts, but not usufruct or mere delay.
4
Apply the rule to deferment scenarios
If a wife says 'Divorce me on condition that I defer what I owe you' and the husband agrees, if the deferment has a known term, it is valid as a separate agreement but does not make the divorce ba'in. If no known term, the deferment itself is invalid, but the divorce is still raj'iy.
The divorce's nature (raj'iy vs ba'in) depends on the compensation being mal, not on the separate deferment agreement.
5
Recognize the authority
The passage cites al-Bazzaziyya for the rulings, indicating that these are well-established positions within the Hanafi school, part of the relied-upon (mufta bihi) views.
The author (Ibn Nujaym) in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is expanding on Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طالق واحدة وأنت طالق أخرى بألف فقبلت وقعتا بألف ولو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة أملك الزجعة وغداً أخرى أملك الرجعة بألف فقبلت انصرف البدل إليهما، وكذا لو قال أنت طالق الساعة ثلاثاً وغداً أخرى بائنة بألف وأنت طالق الساعة واحدة بغير شيء وغداً أخرى بغير شيء بالألف فالبدل ينصرف إليهما اهـ.
قوله : (ولزمها المال) أي في المسألتين لأنه ما رضي بخروج بعضها عن ملكه إلا به فلزمها المال بالقبول. ولو قال وكان المسمى له لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا قبله غيرها وسيأتي آخر الباب بيان خلع الفضولي إن شاء الله وليشمل الابراء حتى لو قالت له أبرأتك عما لي عليك على طلاقي ففعل جازت البراءة وكان الطلاق بائناً، وكذا لو طلقها على أن تبرئه من الألف التي كفل بها للمرأة . فلان من والطلاق بائن كما في البزازية. وقيد به احترازاً عن التأخير فإنه ليس بمال وأنما تتأخر فيه المطالبة كما لو قالت له طلقني على أن أؤخر مالي عليك فطلقها، فإن كان للتأخير غاية معلومة صح التأخير، وإن يكن له غاية معلومة لا يصح والطلاق رجعي على كل حال كما في البزازية أيضاً.
One divorce and you are divorced another with a thousand, and she accepted: both fall with a thousand. And if he said: 'You are divorced now one, I have the right to take back, and tomorrow another, I have the right to take back, for a thousand,' and she accepted, the compensation is allocated to both. Similarly, if he said: 'You are divorced now three, and tomorrow another irrevocably, for a thousand; and you are divorced now one for nothing, and tomorrow another for nothing, for a thousand,' the compensation is allocated to both. End.
His saying: 'And the money is binding on her' means in both cases because he was not satisfied with the removal of some of her from his possession except with it, so the money is binding on her upon acceptance. And if he said 'and the named one' it would be more appropriate to include if someone other than her accepted, and the explanation of the khul' of the unauthorized person will come at the end of the chapter, God willing. And to include release (ibra'), so if she said to him 'I release you from what you owe me in exchange for my divorce,' and he did so, the release is valid and the divorce is irrevocable. Similarly, if he divorces her on condition that she release him from the thousand she guaranteed for the woman [from so-and-so], the divorce is irrevocable, as in al-Bazzaziyya. He restricted it to guard against deferment (ta'khir), for it is not property; rather, the claim is merely delayed. As if she said to him: 'Divorce me on condition that I defer what you owe me,' and he divorces her: if the deferment has a known term, the deferment is valid; if it has no known term, it is not valid, and the divorce is revocable in any case, as in al-Bazzaziyya as well.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the rules of khul' (divorce initiated by the wife with compensation). The passage begins with examples of multiple talaq pronouncements in khul'. If a husband says 'You are divorced once and you are divorced another for a thousand' and she accepts, both divorces occur and the full thousand is due. The key principle is that when multiple talaqs are mentioned with a single sum of compensation, the sum is allocated to all the talaqs unless one of them is described in a way that contradicts it being compensation. For instance, if he says 'You are divorced now one, I have the right to take back, and tomorrow another, I have the right to take back, for a thousand,' the compensation is allocated to both, and both become irrevocable (ba'in). If the first is described as revocable (with the right to take back) and the second as irrevocable, the compensation is allocated equally. The commentary then explains that the compensation must be mal (property) in the legal sense. Deferment (ta'khir) of a debt is not considered mal, so if the wife offers to defer a debt as compensation, it is not valid as compensation; the divorce remains revocable (raj'iy). However, if the deferment has a known term, it is valid as a separate agreement, but the divorce is still revocable. The author cites al-Bazzaziyya for these rulings.

Key Terms
مال (mal): Property that can be owned and traded; tangible assets or debts; not mere deferment.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
تأخير (ta'khir): Deferment of an existing debt; postponing the time of payment.
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce; husband cannot take wife back without a new marriage.
رجعة (raj'a): The right to take back the wife during the 'idda after a revocable divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife says to her husband 'Divorce me on condition that I defer the debt I owe you for one year' and he divorces her, what is the status of the divorce according to the Hanafi school?
A) The divorce is ba'in because deferment is valid compensation.
B) The divorce is raj'iy because deferment is not mal.
C) The divorce is invalid because deferment is not allowed.
D) The divorce is ba'in only if the deferment has a known term.

Key Takeaway
Khul' compensation must be mal; deferment of a debt is not mal, so the divorce remains revocable regardless of a valid deferment agreement.

Repeated Offers of Khul' and Effect of Acceptance
Ruling on repeated khul' offers and the effect of a single acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of divorces and compensation when a husband repeats the khul' offer multiple times and the wife accepts once, and explain the reasoning.

Core Idea
Each repeated khul' offer is independent; a single acceptance activates all, yielding multiple divorces and cumulative compensation.

Understanding how repeated khul' offers interact with a single acceptance is crucial for accurate divorce calculations. The Hanafi school holds that each offer is a separate proposal, and the wife's acceptance after all offers binds all. The passage also contrasts a sale metaphor scenario to illustrate how explicit divorce wording affects compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) husband says 'I divorced you by khul' for a thousand' three times, then wife accepts; (2) husband uses a sale metaphor 'I sold you one divorce for a thousand' three times, wife accepts after each, and he claims repetition.
Both involve three utterances before full acceptance.
2
Analyze the first scenario
Since no divorce occurs before acceptance, each offer remains pending. A single acceptance after all three offers activates all three, resulting in three divorces and three thousand owed.
The reason given: 'divorce depends on her acceptance.'
3
Analyze the second scenario
After the first acceptance, the wife becomes irrevocably divorced (ba'in). The second and third utterances are explicit (sarih) divorce pronouncements, which are effective even after the marriage ends, so three divorces occur. However, compensation is only one thousand because she already owned herself.
The explicit divorce (sarih) affects the already divorced woman.
4
Understand the husband's claim of repetition
In the second scenario, if the husband claims he intended to repeat the same offer (not a new one), he is not believed. The literal wording indicates three separate utterances.
The principle: explicit wording prevails over claimed intention in divorce matters.
5
Apply the reasoning to new cases
Use the same logic: repeated offers before acceptance are independent; acceptance after all activates all. In sale metaphor, the first acceptance ends the marriage, so subsequent explicit divorces add no compensation.
This distinction is key for fatwa in modern contexts like text divorces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال قد خلعتك على ألف قال ثلاث مرات فقبلت طلقت ثلاثاً بثلاثة آلاف لأنه لم يقع شيء إلا بقبولها لأن الطلاق يتعلق بقبولها ولو قال بعت منك تطليقة بألف فقالت اشتريت ثم قاله ثانياً وثالثاً كذلك وقال أردت التكرار لا يصدق ويقع الثلاث ولم يلزمها إلا الألف لأنها ملكت نفسها بالأولى وقد صرح بالطلاق في اللفظ الثانية والثالثة والصريح يلحق البائن كذا في المحيط.
And if he said: 'I have divorced you by khul' for a thousand' three times, and she accepted, she is divorced three times for three thousand, because nothing occurred except by her acceptance, since divorce depends on her acceptance. And if he said: 'I sold you one divorce for a thousand,' and she said 'I bought,' then he said it a second and third time similarly, and he said 'I intended repetition,' he is not believed, and three divorces occur, and only one thousand is binding on her, because she owned herself by the first, and he explicitly pronounced divorce in the second and third utterances, and the explicit (divorce) affects the irrevocable (divorce). Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage discusses two scenarios. First, if a husband says 'I have divorced you by khul' for a thousand' three times, and the wife accepts after all three, she becomes divorced three times and owes three thousand. The reason: the divorce is contingent on her acceptance; until she accepts, no divorce falls. Since the statement was repeated three times before acceptance, the three offers are valid and, upon a single acceptance of the proposal (if she accepts all three as one acceptance? The text says she accepted, and three Talaqs fall). Alternatively, if the husband says 'I sold you one divorce for a thousand' (using a sale metaphor) and she says 'I bought,' then he repeats it and says 'I intended only to repeat my statement,' his claim is not accepted; three divorces occur, but only one thousand is owed because the first acceptance made her own herself (i.e., the marriage ended), so the subsequent pronouncements are effective but no additional compensation is due because she is already divorced irrevocably. The author cites al-Muhit for this ruling.

Key Terms
صريح (sarih): Explicit divorce wording that does not require intention.
خلع (khul'): Divorce for compensation; here used as a proposal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says 'I have divorced you for a thousand' three times in succession, and then the wife says 'I accept.' How many divorces occur and how much does she owe?
A) One divorce and one thousand.
B) Three divorces and three thousand.
C) Three divorces and one thousand.
D) One divorce and three thousand.

Key Takeaway
When a husband repeats the khul' offer multiple times before acceptance, each offer is effective upon acceptance, resulting in multiple divorces and cumulative compensation.

Conflicting Witness Testimony in Khul' Disputes
Rulings on disputes and evidence in khul'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on conflicting witness testimony in khul' cases and determine which party's word is accepted in disputes over compensation.

Core Idea
In khul', the compensation condition is integral; conflicting witnesses invalidate the claim unless the husband admits the divorce.

Khul' is a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation. When disputes arise about whether compensation was agreed, or about the amount, the court must determine which party's evidence prevails. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi approach to such evidentiary conflicts, including the role of witness testimony and the effect of a prior irrevocable divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
The passage covers four scenarios: (1) Both agree on khul' but wife denies compensation; (2) Wife claims khul' but husband denies, and witnesses give conflicting amounts; (3) Husband claims a specific compensation, witnesses agree on less; (4) Husband claims but witnesses conflict; (5) Witnesses testify to a prior triple divorce before khul'.
Each scenario has a distinct ruling based on who is the claimant and the consistency of evidence.
2
Apply the rule for denial of compensation
If both agree khul' occurred but wife says no compensation, her word is taken because she is denying the obligation. The default is no compensation until proven.
The wife's denial is a negation (nafy) which is easier to accept.
3
Analyze conflicting witness testimony when wife claims khul'
If wife claims khul' and husband denies, and two witnesses give different amounts, the testimony is rejected entirely because each witnesses to a different condition (shart). The khul' is not proven.
The divorce is conditional on accepting the money; different amounts are different conditions.
4
Analyze conflicting testimony when husband is claimant
If husband claims a specific amount (e.g., 1500) and witnesses agree on a lesser amount (e.g., 1000), the lesser amount is accepted because the divorce is admitted by the husband, so the remaining dispute is only about the debt. If husband claims 1000 and witnesses conflict, his claim fails and he is considered to have accused a witness of lying.
The husband's admission of divorce shifts the burden; the witnesses' agreement on a part is binding.
5
Evaluate evidence of prior triple divorce
If two witnesses testify that the husband divorced the wife thrice before the khul', the wife takes back the compensation. The khul' was invalid because she was already irrevocably divorced. Her apparent affirmation of khul' does not prevent her from claiming the money back once the prior divorce is proven.
Evidence of divorce is accepted even without a formal claim from the wife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اتفقا على الخلع وقالت بغير جعل فالقول لها لأن صحة الخلع تستدعي البدل فتكون منكرة فيكون القول لها، ولو ادعت الخلع والزوج ينكره فشهد أحدهما بألف والآخر بألف وخمسمائة لا يقبل ولا يثبت الخلع لأنها تحتاج إلى إثبات أن الزوج علق الطلاق بقبول المال والطلاق المعلق بقبول الألف غير الطلاق غير الطلاق المعلق بقبول الألفين إذ هما شرطان مختلفان فكان كل واحد يشهد بغير ما يشهد به الآخر فلا يقبل، ولو كان الزوج هو المدعي وقد ادعى ألفاً وخمسمائة والمسألة بحالها تقبل على الألف لأن الطلاق وقع بإقرار الزوج فبقي دعوى الزوج ديناً مجرداً واتفق الشاهدان على الألف وانفرد أحدهما بزيادة خمسمائة فيقضي بما اتفقا عليه وإن كان يدعي ألفاً لا يقبل وقد كذب أحد شاهديه لما عرف ويقع الطلاق بإقراره وإذا شهد شاهدان أنه طلقها قبل الخلع ثلاثاً تسترد المال لأنها بمباشرة الخلع وإن كانت مقرة بصحة الخلع ظاهراً فإذا ادعت الفساد بعد ذلك صارت متناقضة في الدعوى إلا أن البينة على الطلاق تقبل من غير دعوى فيثبت أنه أخذ المال بعد البينونة فلزمه الرد؛ كذا في المحيط.
And if they both agree on the khul' and she says it was without consideration, the word is hers because the validity of khul' requires compensation, so she is denying, thus her word is accepted. And if she claims khul' and the husband denies it, and one witness testifies to a thousand and another to a thousand and five hundred, it is not accepted and khul' is not proven, because she needs to prove that the husband suspended divorce on acceptance of the money, and the divorce suspended on acceptance of a thousand is different from the divorce suspended on acceptance of two thousand, as they are two different conditions, so each witnesses to something different from the other, so it is not accepted. And if the husband is the claimant and he claims a thousand and five hundred, and the case is the same, it is accepted for a thousand because the divorce occurred by the husband's acknowledgment, so his claim remains a mere debt, and the two witnesses agreed on a thousand, and one of them alone added five hundred, so judgment is given for what they agreed upon. And if he claims a thousand, it is not accepted, and he has accused one of his witnesses of lying, as is known, and the divorce occurs by his acknowledgment. And if two witnesses testify that he divorced her thrice before the khul', she takes back the compensation, because she engaged in khul' and although she was apparently affirming the validity of the khul', if she claims invalidity thereafter, she becomes contradictory in her claim, except that evidence for divorce is accepted without a claim, so it is established that he took the money after irrevocability, so he must return it. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage addresses disputes and evidence in khul'. First, if the spouses agree that khul' occurred but differ on whether compensation was agreed, the wife's word is taken (she denies any compensation) because khul' normally requires compensation, so she is denying the extra claim; the default is no compensation. Second, if the wife claims khul' and the husband denies it, and witnesses give conflicting amounts, their testimony is not accepted because they testify to different conditions; khul' is a conditional divorce and the condition differs based on the amount. If the husband is the claimant, and he claims a specific amount, and witnesses agree on a lower amount, the lower amount is accepted because the divorce is already established by his admission; the conflict is only over the debt. If the witnesses agree on a thousand but one adds five hundred, the court rules for a thousand. If the husband claims a thousand but the witnesses conflict, his claim is rejected and he is considered to have falsely accused a witness. Finally, if two witnesses testify that the husband divorced her three times before the khul', the wife can recover the compensation because the khul' was invalid (she was already divorced). Her engagement in khul' does not prevent her from claiming the money back if proven. The evidence of the prior divorce is accepted even without her claiming it.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, usually two male witnesses or one male and two females.
جعل (ju'l): Consideration or compensation in khul'.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation.
شرط (shart): Condition upon which the divorce is suspended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a khul' dispute, the husband claims 2000 dirhams compensation, and two witnesses testify: one says 2000, the other says 2500. The wife denies khul' entirely. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The khul' is proven with 2000 because the husband's claim is supported by one witness.
B) The khul' is not proven because the witnesses give conflicting amounts.
C) The khul' is proven with 2500 because the majority of witnesses support that amount.
D) The wife's denial is accepted, so no khul' occurred.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the compensation amount in khul' is an essential condition; inconsistent witness testimony on the amount fails to prove the conditional divorce.

Khul' with a Makataba, Amah, or Umm Walad
Rulings on khul' with slave women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid khul' when the wife is a makataba, amah, or umm walad, and apply the Hanafi rule that her capacity is restricted by hajr.

Core Idea
A slave woman's khul' requires her master's permission; without it, the compensation is not binding.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines khul' when the wife is a slave or similar status. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a makataba (who owes installments for freedom) and a full slave (amah) or umm walad, treating her capacity to be bound by compensation differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wife's status
Determine if she is a makataba, amah, or umm walad. Each has different rules regarding compensation liability.
A makataba has a contract for freedom; an amah is fully owned; an umm walad has a child from her master.
2
Check the master's permission
For amah and umm walad, khul' is only valid with the master's permission. For makataba, the compensation is not binding until she becomes free unless the master permits.
The permission removes the hajr (legal incapacity).
3
Determine when compensation is binding
With master's permission, it is binding immediately. Without permission for makataba, it is deferred until she becomes free.
The hajr prevents immediate liability.
4
Analyze special cases regarding the husband's status
If the husband is a slave or mudabbar, the compensation goes to his master. If he is a makatab, his ownership right does not invalidate the marriage.
If the husband is free, later acquiring her ownership would invalidate the marriage and the khul'.
5
Apply the rules to a compensation scenario
When compensation is a slave that is later claimed, the amah is sold to cover the value. Prior debts take precedence.
The master is not liable if he did not guarantee the item.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He made absolute in making the money binding on her, so it includes the makataba, but the money is not binding on her except after emancipation, even if with the master's permission, due to her disability to give charity, and if with permission it is like her gift. And it includes the amah and umm walad, but with the condition of the master's permission, so it is binding immediately because the disability is removed by the master's permission, so it appears against her like other debts. And in al-Jami': If the master of an amah gives her in khul' on her own neck (i.e., making her personally liable) and her husband is free, the khul' occurs with nothing (i.e., no compensation from the husband). And if the husband is a makatab, or a slave, or a mudabbar, the khul' is valid and she becomes [in the case of slave or mudabbar] the property of the master of the slave and mudabbar, because she does not become the property of the husband but of the master, so the marriage does not become invalid. While for a free man, if he owns her neck after marriage, the marriage would become invalid, and if it became invalid, the khul' would become invalid, so validating it would be invalidating it. As for the makatab, a right of ownership is established for him over her, and the right of ownership does not prevent the continuation of marriage, so the marriage does not become invalid, like if he bought his wife who is an amah under a slave. If her master gives her in khul' for a slave in his possession, and then the slave given in khul' is claimed and proven to be someone else's, nothing is due from the master because he did not attribute the slave to himself nor guarantee him; thus the contract is attributed to the amah, and the amah is sold for the value of the claimed slave because the master has the power to impose the compensation for khul' on her, so it appears against her and attaches to her neck. If she has another debt before it, it is given precedence because it became obligatory by the master's choice, so it does not appear in the right of the other creditor, as in sulh. If something remains of the amah's value, it is taken after emancipation. If the master guaranteed the compensation for khul', it is taken from him. Thus in al-Muhit. And in al-Zahiriyya: A woman said to her husband, 'I have divorced myself from you for such-and-such' while he was weaving karpas, so he continued weaving, and his statement: 'She is divorced immediately even if she does not give a thousand' i.e., the thousand is binding on her, as will come at his saying 'You are divorced for a thousand.'

Commentary
This passage covers khul' when the wife is a slave or similar status. The general rule: if the wife is a makataba (slave who has a contract of manumission), khul' is valid but the compensation is not binding until she becomes free, because she is under restriction (hajr) for financial transactions. If her master permits, it is binding immediately because the disability is removed. For an ordinary slave (amah) or umm walad (slave who bore a child to her master), the master's permission is required; if given, the compensation is binding immediately. The author then cites al-Jami' for special cases: If a master gives his slave woman in khul' making her personally liable for compensation (on her neck) and her husband is free, the khul' is valid but the compensation is nothing (the master does not collect anything from the husband, but the wife becomes free? Actually the text says 'الخلع واقع بغير شيء' meaning the divorces occur without compensation to the master? Likely the master forfeits the compensation because he imposed it on her, but she is a slave who cannot own property). If the husband is a slave or mudabbar, the khul' is valid and she becomes the property of the husband's master (since a slave cannot own property, the compensation goes to his master). If the husband is free and later acquires her as property, the marriage would be invalidated, and if the marriage is invalid, the khul' is invalid. For a makatab husband, khul' is valid because he has a right of ownership but it does not invalidate marriage. The passage also discusses a case where the compensation is a slave that is later claimed by another; the sale of the wife's person to cover the loss is not allowed in Hanafi? Actually the text says the amah is sold for the value of the claimed slave. Also, priorities of debts: if she has a prior debt, that is paid first. Finally, a ruling from al-Zahiriyya: if a woman offers khul' while her husband is busy weaving, his silent act of continuing to weave is not acceptance; the divorce is immediate but the compensation is due. The phrase 'تطلق للحال وإن لم تعط ألفاً' means she is divorced immediately even if she does not give the thousand, but the thousand is due on her.

Key Terms
مكاتبة (makataba): A slave woman who has made a contract to earn her freedom by paying installments.
أمة (amah): A female slave fully owned by a master.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bore a child to her master, becomes free upon his death.
حجر (hajr): Legal incapacity to enter financial transactions without permission.

Triple Divorce in Khul' with Repeated Offers
Ruling on a specific khul' scenario with repeated divorce offers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that explicit talaq utterances are counted individually even after a ba'in separation, and explain why the husband's claim of intended repetition is not accepted.

Core Idea
Explicit divorce utterances are counted individually; a claim of intended repetition is disregarded.

This lesson examines a specific khul' scenario where a husband repeatedly offers a divorce in exchange for a payment and later claims he meant to repeat the same offer. We will explore why the Hanafi school rejects this claim, how the divorces are counted, and the resulting financial obligation. The key principle is that explicit wording (sarih) of divorce is effective regardless of the woman's marital status, and each distinct utterance is a separate divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The husband says 'I sold you a divorce for a thousand' three times, and the wife accepts each time. He later claims he intended to repeat the same offer (ta'kid).
The case is from al-Muhit, a later Hanafi work.
2
Apply the Principle of Explicit Talaq
The Hanafi principle states: 'Explicit divorce (sarih) is effective even after a ba'in separation' (والصريح يلحق البائن). This means once a woman becomes irrevocably separated, a subsequent explicit talaq still takes effect and is counted.
This principle is based on the literal meaning of the utterance, not the speaker's hidden intention.
3
Evaluate the Claim of Repetition
The husband's claim that he intended repetition is not accepted because the literal wording of the second and third utterances constitutes separate offers. In Hanafi law, a person's statement is taken at face value unless a valid reason (such as a clear contextual indicator) exists.
The husband is not believed because he explicitly uttered the divorce each time.
4
Determine the Number of Divorces
Since each utterance is a separate offer, three divorces occur. The first divorce makes the wife ba'in (irrevocably separated). The second and third divorces are still valid and counted, but they do not change the status (she is already ba'in).
The total becomes three, making the wife permanently prohibited (unless she marries another and is divorced, etc.).
5
Calculate the Financial Obligation
Only one thousand is owed because with the first divorce, the wife 'owned herself' (i.e., she became ba'in and the khul' consideration is due for that divorce). The subsequent divorces occur without additional financial obligation since she is already separated.
The payment is for the first divorce only.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الخلع فوقع الثلاث عند قبولها جملة بثلاثة آلاف ولو قال بعت منك تطليقة بألف فقالت اشتريت ثم قاله ثانياً وثالثاً كذلك وقال أردت التكرار لا يصدق ويقع الثلاث ولم يلزمها إلا الألف لأنها ملكت نفسها بالأولى وقد صرح بالطلاق في اللفظ الثانية والثالثة والصريح يلحق البائن؛ كذا في المحيط.
In khul': Triple divorce occurs when she accepts all together for three thousand. And if he said, 'I sold you a divorce for a thousand,' and she said 'I bought,' then he said it a second and third time likewise, and he said 'I intended repetition,' he is not believed, and triple divorce occurs, and only one thousand is incumbent upon her because she owned herself with the first [divorce], and he explicitly uttered divorce in the second and third utterances, and the explicit [divorce] is effective after the irrevocable [divorce]; thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Muhit about a specific khul' scenario. The husband says 'I sold you a divorce for a thousand' three times, and the wife accepts each time. If he later claims he intended mere repetition (ta'kid) of the same offer, his claim is rejected because the literal meaning is a separate offer each time. Therefore, three divorces occur, making the wife irrevocably separate (ba'in). However, she only owes one thousand because with the first divorce, she owned herself (i.e., she became ba'in) and the subsequent divorces are redundant but still count. The reasoning is that the explicit wording of divorce in the second and third utterances takes effect on an already separated woman (ba'in), so the divorce is valid but the financial obligation does not repeat.

Key Terms
تطليقة (tatliqa): A single count of divorce (one talaq).
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce; marriage cannot be renewed without new contract.
صريح (sarih): Explicit wording of divorce that does not require intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One divorce, one thousand
B) Three divorces, three thousand
C) Three divorces, one thousand
D) One divorce, three thousand

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, explicit (sarih) divorce utterances are counted individually; a claim of intended repetition is disregarded, leading to the full number of divorces but only the first payment in khul'.

Evidence in Khul' Compensation Disputes
Rulings on who is believed when there is disagreement over khul' and compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi evidentiary rules to determine who is believed when there is disagreement over khul' and its compensation (ja'l).

Core Idea
The denier’s word is taken; conflicting testimony invalidates the claim unless talaq is already admitted.

This passage presents three scenarios where the husband and wife disagree about the compensation in khul'. The Hanafi school applies consistent principles: the denier is believed, and testimony must agree on the essential condition. We will walk through each scenario to see how these rules operate in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scenario
Both agree khul' occurred, but the wife denies any compensation (ja'l) was agreed. Identify who is the claimant and who is the denier.
2
Apply the denier principle
The wife is the denier of the substitute, which is essential for khul' validity. The husband must prove the substitute. Since he cannot, the wife's word is taken.
3
Analyze conflicting testimony when wife is claimant
Wife claims khul', husband denies. Two witnesses give different amounts. Each amount is a different condition for the suspended talaq, so testimony conflicts and khul' is not established.
4
Analyze conflicting testimony when husband is claimant
Husband claims khul' with compensation, admits talaq. The talaq is established by his admission. The dispute is now only about the debt amount. Witnesses agree on 1000, one adds 500; judgment on the agreed amount.
If husband claims 1000 and witness says 1500, he contradicts his own witness, so testimony rejected.
5
Synthesize the underlying principle
The key distinction: whether talaq is already established (by admission) or depends entirely on proof of the condition. In the latter, conflicting conditions invalidate the whole claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اتفقا على الخلع وقالت بغير جعل فالقول لها لأن صحة الخلع تستدعي البدل فتكون منكرة فيكون القول لها، ولو ادعت الخلع والزوج ينكره فشهد أحدهما بألف والآخر بألف وخمسمائة لا يقبل ولا يثبت الخلع لأنها تحتاج إلى إثبات أن الزوج علق الطلاق بقبول المال والطلاق المعلق بقبول الألف غير الطلاق غير الطلاق المعلق بقبول الألفين إذ هما شرطان مختلفان فكان كل واحد يشهد بغير ما يشهد به الآخر فلا يقبل، ولو كان الزوج هو المدعي وقد ادعى ألفاً وخمسمائة والمسألة بحالها تقبل على الألف لأن الطلاق وقع بإقرار الزوج فبقي دعوى الزوج ديناً مجرداً واتفق الشاهدان على الألف وانفرد أحدهما بزيادة خمسمائة فيقضي بما اتفقا عليه وإن كان يدعي ألفاً لا يقبل وقد كذب أحد شاهديه لما عرف ويقع الطلاق بإقراره
And if they both agreed on khul' and she said 'without compensation,' then the word is hers because the validity of khul' requires a substitute, so she is a denier, thus the word is hers. And if she claimed khul' and the husband denied it, and one witness [testified] to a thousand and another to a thousand and five hundred, it is not accepted and khul' is not established because she needs to prove that the husband suspended talaq upon acceptance of money; and the talaq suspended upon acceptance of a thousand is not the talaq suspended upon acceptance of two thousand, as they are two different conditions; so each witness testifies to something other than what the other testifies, so it is not accepted. And if the husband is the claimant and he claimed a thousand and five hundred, and the case is the same, it is accepted on [the basis of] a thousand because the talaq occurred by the husband's admission, so the husband's claim remains a pure debt; and the two witnesses agreed on a thousand and one of them added five hundred, so judgment is given on what they agreed upon; and if he claims a thousand, it is not accepted and he has belied one of his witnesses for what is known, and the talaq occurs by his admission.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage covers three scenarios. First, if both agree khul' occurred but wife denies any compensation was agreed, her word is taken because she is denying the existence of the substitute (badal) which is essential for the validity of khul'. Second, if wife claims khul' and husband denies, and two witnesses give different amounts (one says 1000, other 1500), their testimony is not accepted because each testifies to a different condition for the talaq; thus khul' is not proven. Third, if husband is the claimant (i.e., he asserts khul' and claims wife owes 1500), the testimony is accepted regarding the 1000 that both witnesses agree on, because the talaq itself is already established by the husband's admission (he admitted to talaq within the khul' claim), so the remaining dispute is only about the debt amount. If husband claims only 1000 and witnesses differ, his own claim contradicts one witness, so testimony is rejected.

Key Terms
جعل (ja'l): The compensation (substitute) given by the wife in khul'.
منكرة (munkira): Denier of the claim; she denies the existence of compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife claims khul' occurred with compensation of 1000, and two witnesses testify: one for 1000 and one for 1500, what is the outcome?
A) Khul' is established and wife owes 1000
B) Khul' is established and wife owes 1500
C) Khul' is established but wife owes nothing
D) Khul' is not established

Key Takeaway
In khul' compensation disputes, the denier's word prevails, and testimony must agree on the exact condition to establish the claim.

6 min
Recovery of Money When Pre-Khul' Triple Divorce is Witnessed
Ruling on testimony that husband divorced wife thrice before khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recovery of property when witnesses testify that a triple talaq occurred before the khul', and explain the reasoning (talil) behind the rule.

Core Idea
Witness testimony to pre-khul' triple talaq invalidates khul' and forces the husband to return the property.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq where the interplay of testimony and divorce timing leads to a surprising result: even though the wife initially appeared to affirm the khul', if witnesses prove an earlier triple talaq, she recovers what she paid. The reasoning hinges on the acceptance of testimony about talaq without a formal claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the end result: the wife recovers the property she gave in khul'. This is the mufta bihi position.
The operative ruling is that return of property is mandatory.
2
Understand the evidentiary trigger
Identify the condition: two witnesses testify that the husband divorced his wife three times before the khul' agreement. Note that this testimony is accepted even without the wife's explicit claim.
Testimony about talaq is an exception to the usual rule requiring a claim.
3
Analyse the contradicting claims
The wife initially participated in the khul', indicating she accepted its validity. If she later claims the khul' was invalid due to prior talaq, she appears contradictory. But the testimony overrides this contradiction.
The wife's inconsistency does not prevent her from benefiting from the testimony.
4
Trace the reasoning (talil)
The testimony establishes that the husband took the property after the talaq had already made the wife irrevocably separated (ba'in). Therefore, he took it without a valid marital consideration, so he must return it.
The key is the temporal priority: talaq → khul' → property transfer invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا شهد شاهدان أنه طلقها قبل الخلع ثلاثاً تسترد المال لأنها بمباشرة الخلع وإن كانت مقرة بصحة الخلع ظاهراً فإذا ادعت الفساد بعد ذلك صارت متناقضة في الدعوى إلا أن البينة على الطلاق تقبل من غير دعوى فيثبت أنه أخذ المال بعد البينونة فلزمه الرد؛ كذا في المحيط.
And if two witnesses testify that he divorced her three times before the khul', she recovers the property because although she performed the khul' and apparently affirmed its validity, if she later claims its invalidity she becomes contradictory in her claim; however, testimony concerning talaq is accepted without a claim, so it is established that he took the property after irrevocable separation, so he must return it; thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This ruling addresses a scenario where witnesses testify that the husband had already divorced the wife three times prior to the khul' transaction. Even though the wife initially participated in the khul' and seemed to acknowledge its validity, if she later claims the khul' was invalid (because she was already divorced), her claim would be contradictory. However, the rule is that testimony about the timing of talaq is accepted even without an explicit claim from the wife. Therefore, if the witnesses prove that the talaq occurred before the khul', the husband took the property after the marriage was already irrevocably ended (ba'in), so he must return it.

Key Terms
بينونة (baynuna): Irrevocable separation; after triple talaq.
خلع (khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in return for compensation (usually financial) paid to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) She recovers it because the khul' was invalid
C) She recovers only half
D) The husband keeps it because the khul' was valid

Key Takeaway
Testimony of two witnesses to a pre-khul' triple talaq overrides the wife's apparent affirmation of the khul', forcing the husband to return the property.

Khul' with Women of Special Status: Liability and Scenarios
Rulings on khul' involving women with special status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the liability of a mukataba, umm walad, and slave woman in khul', distinguish when compensation is immediate versus deferred, and apply the rulings to scenarios of different husband statuses.

Core Idea
A mukataba's khul' compensation is deferred until freedom; a slave wife's is immediate with master's permission.

The Hanafi school provides detailed rulings on khul' when the wife has a special legal status—mukataba, umm walad, or ordinary slave. These rulings hinge on the concept of legal impediment (hajr) affecting financial capacity. The passage also discusses how the husband's status (free, slave, mukatab, mudabbar) impacts the validity of khul' and ownership of the wife. Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly applying khul' rulings in complex family situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the women covered
The ruling explicitly includes mukataba, ordinary female slave (ama), and umm walad. Note the general phrase 'the property is incumbent upon her' encompasses these categories.
These are women with partial or full financial constraints.
2
Distinguish the timing of liability
For a mukataba, compensation is not due until after emancipation, even if the master permits. For an ama or umm walad, if the master grants permission, the liability is immediate because the impediment is removed.
The key difference is the nature of the impediment: mukataba is under hajr until fully free; others have hajr but can be lifted by permission.
3
Analyze the effect of husband's status
If the husband is free, and the master initiates khul' on the wife's person (herself as compensation), the khul' is valid without any compensation. If the husband is a slave, mukatab, or mudabbar, khul' is valid and the wife becomes owned by the husband's master, but the marriage continues. However, if a free husband later owned her, the marriage would be invalid, so khul' would be invalid.
Ownership of a spouse invalidates marriage, but a right of ownership (as in mukatab) does not.
4
Evaluate compensation issues
If the compensation (e.g., a slave) is later reclaimed, the master is not liable; the wife is sold to pay the value. Prior debts take precedence over the khul' debt because the khul' debt was created by the master's choice. If the master guaranteed, he is liable.
This shows priority rules and liability when the compensation is not delivered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أطلق في لزومها المال فشمل المكاتبة ولكن لا يلزمها المال إلا بعد العتق ولو بإذن المولى لحجرها عن التبرع ولو بالإذن كهبتها، وشمل الأمة وأم الولد ولكن بشرط إذن المولى فيلزمها للحال لانفكاك الحجر بإذن المولى فظهر في حقه كسائر الديون. وفي الجامع : لو خلع الأمة مولاها على رقبتها وزوجها حر فالخلع واقع بغير شيء، ولو كان الزوج مكاتباً أو عبداً أو مدبراً جاز الخلع وصارت لسيد العبد والمدبر لأنها لا تصير مملوكة للزوج بل للمولى فلا يبطل النكاح وفي الحر لو ملك رقبتها بعد النكاح لبطل ولو بطل بطل الخلع فكان في تصحيحه ابطاله وأما المكاتب فإنه يثبت له فيها حق الملك وحق الملك لا يمنع بقاء النكاح فلا يفسد النكاح كما لو اشترى زوجة أمة تحت عبد خلعها مولاها على عبد في يديه ثم استحق العبد المخلوع عليه فلا شيء على المولى لأنه لم يضف العبد المخلوع عليه إلى نفسه ولا ضمنه فكان العقد مضافاً إلى الأمة وتباع الأمة في قيمة العبد المستحق لأن المولى يملك ايجاب بدل الخلع عليها فظهر في حقه فتعلق برقبتها، فإن كان عليها دين آخر قبله بدأ به لأنه وجب باختيار المولى فلم يظهر في حق الغريم كما في الصلح، فإن بقي شيء الأمة يؤخذ من بعد العتق فإن كان المولى ضمن بدل الخلع أخذ به؛ كذا في المحيط.
He gave an absolute ruling on the liability of the property [in khul'], which includes the mukataba, but the property is not incumbent upon her except after emancipation, even if with the master's permission, because she is prevented from gratuitous dispositions, even with permission like her gift. And it includes the female slave and umm walad, but with the condition of the master's permission, so it is incumbent upon her immediately because the prevention is removed by the master's permission, so it becomes apparent in his right like other debts. And in al-Jami': If the master of a female slave releases her with khul' on her person and her husband is free, the khul' occurs without anything. And if the husband is a mukatab, a slave, or a mudabbar, the khul' is valid and she becomes [owned] by the master of the slave and mudabbar because she does not become owned by the husband but by the master, so the marriage does not become invalid; but in the case of a free man, if he owned her person after marriage, the marriage would become invalid, and if it became invalid, the khul' would be invalid, so in validating it there is its invalidation. As for the mukatab, he has the right of ownership in her, and the right of ownership does not prevent the continuation of marriage, so it does not invalidate the marriage, like if the husband of a slave woman under [the authority of] a slave bought her. [Another scenario:] If her master made khul' on a slave in his possession, then the slave given as compensation was reclaimed, there is nothing on the master because he did not attribute the slave given as compensation to himself nor did he guarantee it, so the contract was attached to the female slave, and the female slave is sold for the value of the reclaimed slave because the master has the power to impose the substitute of khul' upon her, so it becomes apparent in his right and attaches to her person. If she had another debt prior to this, it is given precedence because it was obligated by the master's choice, so it does not become apparent in the right of the creditor, as in sulh. If something remains, it is taken from the female slave after emancipation. If the master guaranteed the substitute of khul', it is taken from him; thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This lengthy passage covers several rulings about khul' involving women with special legal status. First, the statement 'the property is incumbent upon her' is general and includes a mukataba (a slave who has contracted to purchase her freedom). However, a mukataba does not owe the compensation until after she is fully freed, because she is legally prevented from gratuitous dispositions even with her master's permission. For an ordinary female slave (ama) or umm walad (slave mother of the master's child), if the master permits the khul', the compensation is due immediately because the master's permission removes the legal impediment, and the debt becomes like other debts. Then, from al-Jami', if the master of a female slave initiates khul' on her person (i.e., the wife herself as compensation) and her husband is free, the khul' is valid without any compensation because the master is effectively transferring ownership. If the husband is a slave, mukatab, or mudabbar, the khul' is valid and the wife becomes owned by the master of the slave/mudabbar, not by the husband, so the marriage does not become invalid (unlike a free husband who would become her owner, invalidating the marriage). For a mukatab husband, he has a right of ownership but it does not invalidate the marriage. Further, if the master makes khul' on a slave in his possession and that slave is later reclaimed by rightful owner, the master is not liable because he did not personally guarantee it; instead, the contract is attached to the female slave (the wife), and she is sold to cover the value of the reclaimed slave. If she has prior debts, those take precedence because the khul' debt was created by the master's choice and does not take priority over earlier debts. Any remaining amount is taken from her after emancipation. If the master personally guaranteed the khul' compensation, he is liable.

Key Terms
مكاتبة (mukataba): A female slave who has made a contract with her master for her freedom upon payment.
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A female slave who has borne her master a child.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose freedom has been promised upon the master's death.
حجر (hajr): Legal impediment preventing certain financial transactions.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) She is liable only after the master's death.
D) She is liable only if she becomes free.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school applies nuanced rules to khul' compensation when the wife has special status, balancing legal impediments, permission, and priority of debts.

Rulings on Khul' from al-Zahiriyya, Jami' al-Fusulayn, Kafi al-Hakim, and al-Bazzaziyya
Collection of brief rulings on khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid khul' in various scenarios, including the requirement of immediate acceptance and the method of dividing compensation among multiple wives.

Core Idea
Khul' requires immediate acceptance; while walking, speech continuity is key; lump sum is divided by dower.

This lesson presents four distinct rulings from later Hanafi works on the validity of khul' in specific circumstances. These cases illustrate the importance of immediate and connected acceptance, the treatment of khul' with multiple wives, and the handling of disputes about the sequence of offer and acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the al-Zahiriyya ruling
Identify the scenario: wife offers khul' while husband weaves. Determine if his continued weaving with speech constitutes acceptance. Note that the ruling deems it valid if the speech is simultaneous.
The husband's action (weaving) does not preclude acceptance if his words are immediate.
2
Analyze the Jami' al-Fusulayn ruling
Consider the case: husband says 'I make khul' for X dirhams', wife counts then accepts. Evaluate whether her acceptance is valid after counting. The ruling indicates it is valid if the offer remains standing.
Delayed acceptance (after counting) is acceptable as long as no rejection or withdrawal occurs.
3
Analyze the Kafi al-Hakim ruling
Examine the division of a lump-sum compensation when a man makes khul' with two wives. The amount is divided according to the dower each wife received at marriage.
This ensures proportionality based on the financial consideration in each marriage.
4
Analyze the al-Bazzaziyya rulings
Study two points: (1) khul' while walking requires continuous speech; if broken, both khul' and talaq are invalid. (2) In a dispute about acceptance timing, the husband's word is taken because he denies the khul'.
Continuity of speech is a condition for validity; the husband's denial shifts the burden to the wife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية : امرأة قالت لزوجها اختلعت منك بكذا وهو ينسج كرباساً فجعل ينسج وهو قوله : (تطلق للحال وإن لم تعط (ألفاً أي ويلزمها الألف كما يأتي عند قوله «أنت طالق بألف» يصح اهـ. يخاصمها ثم قال خلعت قالوا إن لم يطل ذلك فهو جواب .اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين : قال خلعتك بكذا درهماً فجعلت المرأة تعد الدراهم فلما تم العد قالت قبلت ينبغي أن وفي كافي الحاكم : وإذا خلع الرجل امرأتيه على ألف درهم فإن الألف تنقسم عليهما على قدر ما تزوجهما عليه من المهر .اهـ. وفي البزازية : اختلعا وهما يمشيان إن كان كلام كل منهما متصلاً بالآخر صح، وإن لم يكن متصلاً لا يصح ولا يقع الطلاق أيضاً، ولو اختلعا وزعمت تمام الخلع وادعى القيام ثم القبول فالقول له لأنه انكار الخلع اهـ .
And in al-Zahiriyya: A woman said to her husband, 'I have khul' from you for such-and-such,' while he was weaving a cloth, and he continued weaving while [it was] his speech: 'You are divorced immediately even if you do not give a thousand,' i.e., and the thousand is incumbent upon her as will come at his saying 'You are divorced for a thousand' it is valid. Then he quarreled with her, then he said 'I have made khul',' they said: If that is not long, then it is an answer. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: He said 'I have made khul' with you for such dirhams,' and the woman began to count the dirhams; when she finished counting, she said 'I accept'; it should be that... And in Kafi al-Hakim: If a man makes khul' with his two wives for one thousand dirhams, then the thousand is divided between them according to the dower he married each with. And in al-Bazzaziyya: If they make khul' while both are walking, if each one's speech is connected to the other's, it is valid; if not connected, it is not valid and talaq also does not occur. And if they made khul' and she claimed completion of khul' while he claimed standing then acceptance, the word is his because he is denying the khul'.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage collects four short rulings from different Hanafi works. First, from al-Zahiriyya: A wife offers khul' while the husband is weaving. If he continues weaving while saying words that indicate acceptance, it may suffice if the response is immediate. The text is a bit unclear, but the ruling is that if the husband's words are simultaneous with the wife's offer, khul' is valid. Second, from Jami' al-Fusulayn: A husband says 'I make khul' for such dirhams,' and the wife begins counting. The ruling suggests that her counting and then saying 'I accept' after completion is valid if the offer is still standing. Third, from Kafi al-Hakim: If a husband makes khul' with his two wives for one lump sum, the payment is divided according to their respective dowers. Fourth, from al-Bazzaziyya: If khul' is conducted while walking, the speech must be continuous for validity. If continuity is broken, the khul' is invalid and talaq does not occur either. If a dispute arises about whether the acceptance happened after standing or before, the husband's word is taken because he is denying the khul'.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): A form of divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
كرباس (kirbas): A type of cloth; weaving.
مهر (mahr): Dower; the mandatory gift from husband to wife at marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Khul' is valid only when the acceptance is immediate and connected to the offer, and any lump sum compensation is divided according to the dower when multiple wives are involved.

Talaq on Payment: Immediate Effect and Conditions for Liability
Ruling on talaq conditioned on payment and conditions affecting wife's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a talaq conditioned on payment is effective immediately upon acceptance, and identify the circumstances under which the wife is not liable for the property.

Core Idea
Talaq on payment occurs immediately upon acceptance, not upon actual payment.

In this passage, al-Marghinani clarifies a common misunderstanding about talaq on payment. He explains that when a husband uses the word 'ala to link the divorce to a payment, the divorce becomes effective as soon as the wife accepts, regardless of whether she later pays. This is a key distinction between a conditional talaq and a talaq on payment. He also addresses exceptions when the wife is under legal interdiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes two scenarios: (1) husband says 'you are divorced on condition you give me a thousand' and wife accepts; (2) husband says 'you are divorced on your entering the house' and wife accepts. In both, the divorce occurs immediately upon acceptance.
2
Understand the linguistic rule
The word 'ala (upon/on condition) here is used to attach the offer to the acceptance (ta'liq al-ijab bi al-qabul), not to make the divorce conditional on the future event. Therefore, the divorce is not suspended on the payment or entry.
This is based on Hanafi usul.
3
Determine the wife's liability
After the divorce, the wife owes the property (the thousand) if she accepted, unless she is terminally ill, insane, or coerced. The text suggests it is better to specify these exceptions.
4
Apply the rule to a mahjura woman
A woman under legal interdiction due to insanity (mahjura) who accepts khul' gets a valid divorce but does not owe the property. The divorce is ba'in if worded as khul', raj'i if worded as talaq.
This shows that capacity affects liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودخل تحت الطلاق على مال لو طلقها على إعطاء المال لما في الخانية : لو قال لامرأته أنت طالق على أن تعطيني ألف فقالت قبلت تطلق للحال وإن لم تعط ألفاً لامرأته أنت درهم طالق على دخولك الدار فقبلت تطلق للحال وإن لم تدخل لأن كلمة «على» لتعليق الإيجاب بالقبول لا للتعليق بوجود القبول .اهـ. ولو قال ولزمها المال إن لم تكن مريضة مرض الموت ولا سفيهة ولا مكرهة لكان أولى لأن المحجورة بالسفه لو قبلت الخلع وقع ولا يلزمها المال ويكون بائناً إن كان بلفظ الخلع رجعياً إن كان بلفظ الطلاق كما في شرح المنظومة.
And it is included under talaq on property: if he divorces her upon giving property, because in al-Khaniyya: If he said to his wife 'You are divorced on condition that you give me a thousand,' and she said 'I accept,' she is divorced immediately even if she does not give a thousand. [Similarly] if he said to his wife 'You are divorced on your entering the house,' and she accepted, she is divorced immediately even if she does not enter, because the word 'ala' is for attaching the offer to acceptance, not for conditioning upon the occurrence of acceptance. And if he said, 'And the property is incumbent upon her if she is not terminally ill, nor insane, nor coerced,' that would be better, because if a woman legally interdicted due to insanity accepted khul', it takes effect but the property is not incumbent upon her, and she becomes ba'in if it was with the word khul', and raj'i if with the word talaq, as in Sharh al-Manzuma.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage distinguishes talaq on payment from conditional talaq. In al-Khaniyya, if a husband says 'You are divorced on condition that you give me a thousand' and she accepts, the divorce occurs immediately upon her acceptance, not later when she actually gives the money. Similarly, if he conditions talaq on her entering the house, the divorce occurs upon acceptance, not upon entry. The reason is that the word 'ala' (upon/on condition) here is used to link the offer to her acceptance, not as a future condition. Thus the divorce is effective immediately, and she still owes the money if the condition is later fulfilled? Actually the text says 'even if she does not give' meaning the divorce is not conditional on actual payment. However, the liability for the property is separate. The second part clarifies that if the wife is terminally ill, insane, or coerced, the property may not be owed. For a woman under interdiction due to insanity, if she accepts khul', the divorce occurs but she does not owe the money. The divorce is ba'in if worded as khul', raj'i if worded as talaq.

Key Terms
على ('ala): In this context, it links the talaq to acceptance, not to a future event.
محجورة (mahjura): A woman under legal interdiction due to insanity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a talaq on payment is effective immediately upon the wife's acceptance, and the wife's liability for the payment is subject to exceptions like illness, insanity, or coercion.
