Sick Woman's Khul' and Death: The Least of Three
Ruling on khul' by terminally ill woman who dies during iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of 'least of three' to determine the husband's entitlement when a terminally ill woman makes khul' and dies, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A sick woman's khul' is a bequest — the husband gets only the least of his inheritance, the khul' substitute, and one-third of the estate.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific intersection of divorce and inheritance: when a terminally ill woman initiates khul' (divorce for compensation) and then dies during her 'iddah. Since khul' is a gratuitous transfer, it is treated like a bequest and limited to one-third of the estate. The key question is how much the husband can recover, given that he may also be an heir. The author presents the Hanafi rule and highlights a difference between Abu Hanifa and his two students.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the three amounts
The passage describes a sick woman who makes khul' for her mahr (dower) and then dies. The husband's entitlement depends on comparing three values: his inheritance share from her estate, the khul' substitute (the mahr), and one-third of her total wealth. The rule is to give the least of these three.
This is to protect other heirs from excessive depletion of the estate.
2
Differentiate based on consummation and 'iddah status
If the marriage was not consummated, half the mahr returns to the husband by talaq, and the other half is a bequest. If consummated, the entire mahr is a bequest. The 'iddah status matters: after 'iddah, inheritance rights are irrelevant; before, they are considered.
This affects which amounts are compared.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa applies the 'least of three' rule uniformly during 'iddah. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) argue that during 'iddah the husband is no longer an heir because he consented to separation, so only the khul' substitute and one-third are compared (inheritance ignored).
This is a legitimate difference within the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the rule to a concrete example
Suppose a woman has an estate of 120,000, makes khul' for 30,000 mahr, and dies during 'iddah. Her husband's inheritance share is 12,000. One-third of estate = 40,000. According to Abu Hanifa, the least is 12,000 (inheritance). According to Sahibayn, compare 30,000 and 40,000: least is 30,000. So the husband gets different amounts.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is clear.
5
Extend to the case of a relative husband
If the husband is a cousin (and inherits by blood), the one-third rule still applies but the bequest to an heir requires permission of other heirs for the excess over his inheritance. This prevents a husband from gaining more than his share through a deathbed khul'.
This shows the principle's consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المريضة فقال في جامع الفصولين مريضة اختلعت من زوجها بمهرها ثم ماتت ينظر إلى ثلاثة أشياء : إلى ميراثه منها وإلى بدل الخلع وإلى ثلث مالها فيجب أقلها لا الزيادة؛ كذا في «شحي» وفي (حل) في هذه الصورة لو لم يدخل بها سقط نصف المهر بطلاقه والنصف الآخر وصية وهو لغير الوارث فصح من الثلث، فلو دخل بها وماتت بعد مضي العدة فكل المهر وصية وتصح من الثلث إذا الاختلاع تبرع ولو ماتت في العدة هكذا عند أبي يوسف ومحمد إذا الزوج لم يبق وارثاً لرضاه بالفرقة. وعند أبي حنيفة يعطى الأقل من ميراثه ومن بدل الخلع ومن الثلث إذ اتهما في حق سائر الورثة ولم يتهما في الأقل وهو نظير ما قلنا جميعاً في طلاقها بسؤالها في مرض الموت. وحاصل التفاوت بين مضي العدة عدم مضيها أنه بعد مضيها لا ينظر إلى قدر حق الزوج في الميراث وإنما ينظر إلى الثلث فيسلم للزوج قدر الثلث من بدل الخلع ولو أكثر من ميراثه وقبل مضيها لا ينظر إلى الثلث وإنما ينظر إلى ميراثه فيسلم للزوج قدر إرثه من بدل الخلع دون ثلث المال لو ثلثه أكثر كذا ط. ولو كان الزوج ابن عمها فلو لم يرث منها بأن كان لها عصبات أخر أقرب منه فهو والأجنبي سواء، ولو يرثها بقرابة وماتت بعد مضيها ينظر إلى بدل الخلع وإلى إرثه بالقرابة، فلو كان البدل قدر إرثه أو أقل سلم له ذلك، ولو أكثر فالزيادة على قدر إرثه لا تسلم له إلا بإجازة الورثة. هذا لو كانت مدخولة وإلا فالنصف يعود إلى الزوج بطلاق قبل دخوله لا بحكم الوصية وفي النصف الآخر ينظر لو كان الزوج أجنبياً فهو متبرع فيصح من الثلث، ولو كان ابن عمها أو على ألف قوله : (كذا في شحي هذا رمز بالشين المعجمة والحاء المهملة إلى شرح الطحاوي وفي
As for the sick woman, he said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: A sick woman made khul' from her husband for her dower, then she died. Consideration is given to three things: to his inheritance from her, to the substitute of khul', and to one-third of her wealth. The least of them is obligatory, not the excess; thus in 'Shahi' and in 'Hal' in this scenario: If he had not consummated the marriage, half of the dower is dropped by his talaq, and the other half is a bequest and is for a non-heir, so it is valid from one-third. If he consummated and she died after the iddah, then the entire dower is a bequest and is valid from one-third, because khul' is a gratuitous transaction. If she died during the iddah, it is thus according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: the husband is no longer an heir because he consented to the separation. According to Abu Hanifa, he is given the least of his inheritance, the khul' substitute, and one-third, because they are concerned about other heirs and not concerned about the least. This is similar to what we said all together about her divorce upon her request in terminal illness. The sum of the difference between passing of iddah and not: after its passing, consideration is not given to the husband's right of inheritance but to one-third; so the husband receives up to one-third of the khul' substitute even if more than his inheritance. Before its passing, consideration is not given to one-third but to his inheritance; so the husband receives up to his inheritance from the khul' substitute, not the one-third if one-third is more. And if the husband was her cousin (ibn ammiha), if he does not inherit from her because she has other closer agnatic heirs, then he is like a stranger. If he inherits by blood relationship and she dies after the iddah, consideration is given to the khul' substitute and his inheritance by blood. If the substitute equals his inheritance or less, it is given to him; if more, the excess over his inheritance is not given to him without the heirs' permission. This if the marriage was consummated; otherwise, half returns to the husband by talaq before consummation, not by bequest, and for the other half, if the husband is a stranger, he is a donor so it is valid from one-third; if he is her cousin... [text continues with reference].
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage details the ruling for a woman who makes khul' while terminally ill (marad al-mawt) and then dies. Since khul' is a gratuitous transaction, it is subject to the one-third rule like a bequest. The rule is to compare three amounts: (1) the husband's share of inheritance from her, (2) the khul' compensation (here the dower), and (3) one-third of her total wealth. The husband takes the least of these three. This protects the other heirs from excessive diminution of the estate. The jurisprudence differs depending on whether the husband consummated the marriage and whether the wife died during the iddah or after. If consummated and she dies after iddah, the whole dower is a bequest, valid from one-third. If during iddah, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the husband is not an heir because he consented to separation, so he only gets up to the lesser of substitute and one-third (ignoring inheritance). Abu Hanifa says to always take the least of the three. The distinction between death during iddah and after is that after iddah, the husband's inheritance right is irrelevant, so only the one-third and substitute are compared. Before iddah, he may still inherit, so his inheritance is also considered. If the husband is a cousin and inherits by blood, he is not a stranger; the bequest to him would be to an heir, so it is only valid with the permission of other heirs beyond his inheritance share. If not consummated, half of the dower returns to husband by talaq before consummation, and the other half is a bequest, with the same one-third rule.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness; transactions during this period are considered bequests and are limited to one-third of the estate without heirs' consent.
وصية (wasiyya): Bequest; a gratuitous disposition valid only up to one-third of the estate; for a bequest to a non-heir, no permission needed within one-third; to an heir, permission of all heirs is required.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (usually the mahr or other payment).
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The substitute (compensation) given by the wife to the husband in khul', often the dower.
عدة (iddah): Waiting period after divorce or death; during this period, a divorced woman cannot remarry. In this passage, the status of iddah affects inheritance and bequest rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The full dower
B) His inheritance share
C) The least of his inheritance, the khul' substitute, and one-third of the estate
D) The greater of his inheritance and the khul' substitute

Key Takeaway
When a terminally ill woman makes khul' and dies during iddah, the husband is entitled to the least of his inheritance, the khul' substitute, and one-third of the estate, according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn ignore inheritance during iddah.

Procedure and Disputes in Khul' Acceptance
Rulings on the procedure of khul' and disputes about the timing of acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on the procedure of khul' acceptance, including permissible delay, division of compensation among multiple wives, and the effect of disconnected speech, and state the evidentiary rule when there is a dispute about the order of offer and acceptance.

Core Idea
Acceptance in khul' must be immediate and connected to the offer; disconnected speech invalidates, but a short customary delay is permitted.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq collects several practical rulings from different Hanafi sources regarding the procedure of khul'. It clarifies that a wife may take a reasonable time to count the compensation before accepting, that a lump sum for multiple wives is divided proportionally to their mahr, and that while walking, the speech of both parties must be connected. It also resolves a dispute about who spoke first by placing the burden on the one claiming the khul' occurred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three distinct rulings in the passage.
The passage presents three separate scenarios: (1) a wife delays acceptance while counting compensation, (2) a man divorces two wives for a lump sum, and (3) a couple performs khul' while walking. Additionally, there is a rule for when the couple disputes the order of offer and acceptance.
Each ruling comes from a different source: Jami' al-Fusulayn, Kafi al-Hakim, and al-Bazzaziyya.
2
Analyze the first ruling: permissible delay in acceptance.
If the husband says 'I khul' you for such dirhams' and the wife counts the dirhams before accepting, the acceptance is valid if the counting is not prolonged. This permits a short customary delay for practical verification.
The key condition is that the delay should not be excessive (طال).
3
Apply the second ruling: division of compensation among multiple wives.
When a man khul's his two wives for a single lump sum (e.g., 1000 dirhams), the sum is divided between them in proportion to the mahr each received. For example, if wife A had mahr 300 and wife B had mahr 700, then A gets 300 and B gets 700, or if the total is 1000, the ratio holds.
This ensures fairness based on the original dower.
4
Examine the third ruling: khul' while walking and the requirement of connected speech.
If the couple performs khul' while walking, the speech of each must be connected to the other (i.e., immediate response). If there is a break or gap, the khul' is invalid and no divorce occurs.
Connectedness (اتصال الكلام) is a general condition for contracts but is emphasized here due to the moving context.
5
Evaluate the dispute resolution rule: who speaks first?
If the wife claims the khul' is complete but the husband denies it, and there is a dispute about the order (e.g., husband claims he first offered then she accepted, or vice versa), the husband's word is taken because he denies the occurrence of khul' altogether. The burden of proof lies on the one asserting its occurrence (the wife).
This is based on the principle that the defendant's denial is accepted with an oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يخاصمها ثم قال خلعت قالوا إن لم يطل ذلك فهو جواب .اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين : قال خلعتك بكذا درهماً فجعلت المرأة تعد الدراهم فلما تم العد قالت قبلت ينبغي أن وفي كافي الحاكم : وإذا خلع الرجل امرأتيه على ألف درهم فإن الألف تنقسم عليهما على قدر ما تزوجهما عليه من المهر .اهـ. وفي البزازية : اختلعا وهما يمشيان إن كان كلام كل منهما متصلاً بالآخر صح، وإن لم يكن متصلاً لا يصح ولا يقع الطلاق أيضاً، ولو اختلعا وزعمت تمام الخلع وادعى القيام ثم القبول فالقول له لأنه انكار الخلع اهـ .
He argued with her then said 'I have khul'ed you.' They said: If that was not prolonged, it is a response. End. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: He said 'I have khul'ed you for such and such dirhams' and the woman started counting the dirhams; when she finished counting she said 'I accept.' It should be... In Kafi al-Hakim: When a man khul's his two wives for one thousand dirhams, the thousand is divided between them according to the mahr he had given each. End. In al-Bazzaziyya: They khul'ed while walking; if each one's speech is connected to the other, it is valid; if not connected, it is not valid and the divorce does not occur either. If they khul'ed and she claims the completion of the khul' and he claims that he first made the offer and then the acceptance, the word is his because he denies the occurrence of the khul'. End.

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq collects several rulings from different Hanafi sources regarding the procedure of khul'. The first ruling from Jami' al-Fusulayn deals with a case where the husband says 'I have khul'ed you for such dirhams' and the wife begins counting the dirhams before accepting. The text suggests that the acceptance should be considered valid despite the delay if the counting is not prolonged. The second ruling from Kafi al-Hakim addresses khul' of two wives simultaneously for a lump sum of one thousand dirhams: the sum is divided between them proportionally to their respective mahr amounts. The third ruling from al-Bazzaziyya states that for khul' to be valid while walking, the speech of each party must be connected; otherwise the khul' is invalid and no divorce occurs. If there is a dispute about the order—whether the husband initiated and then the wife accepted, or vice versa—the husband's word is taken because he denies the occurrence of the khul' altogether, and the burden of proof is on the one claiming its occurrence (the wife).

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
إيجاب (ijab): The offer made by one party to initiate the contract of khul'.
قبول (qabul): The acceptance by the other party that completes the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The khul' is valid but divorce does not occur.
D) The khul' is suspended until their speech becomes connected.

Key Takeaway
The validity of khul' depends on the immediacy and connectedness of acceptance; a short permissible delay does not invalidate, but disconnected speech (especially while walking) nullifies the contract.

Immediate Effect of Conditional Khul'
Ruling on immediate effect of conditional khul' using 'ala'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a khul' conditioned on payment takes effect immediately in Hanafi fiqh, and identify when the compensation is not binding.

Core Idea
In Hanafi khul', divorce is immediate upon acceptance; 'ala' links the offer to acceptance, not to the condition's fulfillment.

This lesson examines a specific ruling on conditional khul'. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a condition that suspends the divorce and a condition that simply describes the compensation. The key is the word 'ala', which attaches the talaq to the wife's acceptance, not to the actual performance of the condition. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying khul' rulings in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon: conditional khul' (talaq for compensation). The ruling is that the talaq occurs immediately upon the wife's acceptance, regardless of whether the condition is later fulfilled.
2
Understand the linguistic reasoning
Recognize that the word 'ala' in the offer ('You are divorced on condition that...') is interpreted as linking the offer to the acceptance, not to the fulfillment of the condition. Thus, the divorce is not suspended.
Hanafi usul: 'ala' here is for 'ta'liq al-ijab bi al-qabul', not for suspensory ta'liq.
3
Note the exceptions regarding compensation
The compensation is only obligatory upon the wife if she is legally capable: not terminally ill, not interdicted (foolish spendthrift), and not coerced. In such cases, the talaq still occurs but the money is not due.
The wife's incapacity bars the obligation of compensation but does not invalidate the divorce.
4
Distinguish between ba'in and raj'i divorce
The type of divorce (ba'in or raj'i) depends on the wording used. If the husband uses the word 'khul'', the divorce is ba'in; if he uses the word 'talaq', it is raj'i (revocable).
This distinction affects the possibility of reconciliation and the need for a new marriage contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودخل تحت الطلاق على مال لو طلقها على إعطاء المال لما في الخانية : لو قال لامرأته أنت طالق على أن تعطيني ألف فقالت قبلت تطلق للحال وإن لم تعط ألفاً لامرأته أنت درهم طالق على دخولك الدار فقبلت تطلق للحال وإن لم تدخل لأن كلمة «على» لتعليق الإيجاب بالقبول لا للتعليق بوجود القبول .اهـ. ولو قال ولزمها المال إن لم تكن مريضة مرض الموت ولا سفيهة ولا مكرهة لكان أولى لأن المحجورة بالسفه لو قبلت الخلع وقع ولا يلزمها المال ويكون بائناً إن كان بلفظ الخلع رجعياً إن كان بلفظ الطلاق كما في شرح المنظومة.
And included under talaq for compensation: if he divorces her in exchange for giving money, as in al-Khaniyya: if he says to his wife 'You are divorced on condition that you give me a thousand' and she says 'I accept,' she is divorced immediately even if she does not give the thousand; likewise if he says 'You are divorced on condition that you enter the house' and she accepts, she is divorced immediately even if she does not enter, because the word 'ala' is for linking the offer to acceptance, not for linking to the occurrence of the acceptance. End. And it would be better to add: 'The money is obligatory upon her, unless she is terminally ill, or an interdicted spendthrift, or coerced,' because if an interdicted spendthrift accepts khul', the divorce occurs but the money is not obligatory upon her, and it is ba'in if done with the word khul', raj'i if done with the word talaq, as in Sharh al-Manzuma.

Commentary
This passage clarifies that in conditional khul', the divorce takes effect immediately upon acceptance, regardless of whether the condition is fulfilled later. The word 'ala' is a preposition that attaches the talaq to the acceptance, not to the fulfillment of the condition. The author also notes that the wife's liability for the compensation depends on her legal capacity: if she is terminally ill, interdicted due to foolishness, or coerced, the money is not obligatory, but the divorce still occurs. The type of divorce (ba'in or raj'i) depends on the wording used.

Key Terms
على ('ala): A preposition used to link the divorce to the condition; it attaches the offer to the acceptance, not the condition's fulfillment.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when 'ala' is used in a conditional khul' offer, the divorce takes effect immediately upon the wife's acceptance, regardless of her subsequent fulfillment of the condition, but the compensation is only binding if she has full legal capacity.

Sick Wife's Khul' and Death: Compensation Limits and the Hanafi Dispute
Rulings on khul' by a terminally ill wife who dies, with intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on khul' compensation when a terminally ill wife dies, and distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from that of the Sahibayn regarding the impact of the 'idda on inheritance rights.

Core Idea
When a terminally ill wife seeks khul' and dies, the husband receives the least of his inheritance, the compensation, and one-third of her estate.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with a nuanced scenario: a wife who is terminally ill (marida) initiates khul' and then dies. The khul' is valid, but the compensation is subject to limitations to protect the other heirs. There is a well-known disagreement within the Hanafi school between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn regarding whether the husband's inheritance right is forfeited when he consents to the divorce during the 'idda.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The case is a terminally ill wife who seeks khul' in exchange for her mahr and then dies from that illness. The khul' is valid but the compensation is subject to limits.
The wife's illness is 'marad al-mawt' (terminal illness).
2
State the general rule
Three amounts are considered: the husband's inheritance share from the wife, the agreed khul' compensation (badal), and one-third of the wife's total estate. The husband receives the least of these three.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) differ when the wife dies during the 'idda. They argue that by consenting to khul', the husband forfeits his inheritance right, so only the compensation and one-third are considered. Abu Hanifa maintains that the inheritance right is not lost until the 'idda is completed.
The dispute hinges on whether the husband is still an heir during the 'idda.
4
Apply to sub-scenarios
The passage covers cases: after 'idda vs. during 'idda; consummated vs. non-consummated; husband as heir by kinship vs. stranger. Each affects the calculation.
For non-consummated marriage, half the mahr returns to the husband due to divorce, not as a bequest.
5
Note the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the husband always gets the minimum of the three, protecting other heirs. Under Sahibayn during 'idda, he could receive more if the compensation exceeds his inheritance but is within one-third.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المريضة فقال في جامع الفصولين مريضة اختلعت من زوجها بمهرها ثم ماتت ينظر إلى ثلاثة أشياء : إلى میر راثه منها وإلى بدل الخلع وإلى ثلث مالها فيجب أقلها لا الزيادة؛ كذا في «شحي» وفي (حل) في هذه الصورة لو لم يدخل بها سقط نصف المهر بطلاقه والنصف الآخر وصية وهو لغير الوارث فصح من الثلث، فلو دخل بها وماتت بعد مضي العدة فكل المهر وصية وتصح من الثلث إذا الاختلاع تبرع ولو ماتت في العدة هكذا عند أبي يوسف ومحمد إذا الزوج لم يبق وارثاً لرضاه بالفرقة. وعند أبي حنيفة يعطى الأقل من ميراثه ومن بدل الخلع ومن الثلث إذ اتهما في حق سائر الورثة ولم يتهما في الأقل وهو نظير ما قلنا جميعاً في طلاقها بسؤالها في مرض الموت. وحاصل التفاوت بين مضي العدة عدم مضيها أنه بعد مضيها لا ينظر إلى قدر حق الزوج في الميراث وإنما ينظر إلى الثلث فيسلم للزوج قدر الثلث من بدل الخلع ولو أكثر من ميراثه وقبل مضيها لا ينظر إلى الثلث وإنما ينظر إلى ميراثه فيسلم للزوج قدر إرثه من بدل الخلع دون ثلث المال لو ثلثه أكثر كذا ط. ولو كان الزوج ابن عمها فلو لم يرث منها بأن كان لها عصبات أخر أقرب منه فهو والأجنبي سواء، ولو يرثها بقرابة وماتت بعد مضيها ينظر إلى بدل الخلع وإلى إرثه بالقرابة، فلو كان البدل قدر إرثه أو أقل سلم له ذلك، ولو أكثر فالزيادة على قدر إرثه لا تسلم له إلا بإجازة الورثة. هذا لو كانت مدخولة وإلا فالنصف يعود إلى الزوج بطلاق قبل دخوله لا بحكم الوصية وفي النصف الآخر ينظر لو كان الزوج أجنبياً فهو متبرع فيصح من الثلث، ولو كان ابن عمها له ويرثها فله الأقل من إرثه ومن نصف المهر. هذا لو ماتت في ذلك المرض، ولو برئت منه سلم للزوج كل البدل كهبتها منه ثم يرثها ولا إرث بينهما بالزوجية ماتت في العدة أو بعدها لتراضيهما ببطلان حقه. هذا لو كانت مريضة فلو اختلعت صحيحة والزوج مريض فالخلع جائز بالمسمى قل أو كثر ولا إرث بينهما مات في العدة أو بعدها، ولو خلها أجنبي من الزوج بمال ضمنه للزوج وكان ذلك في مرض موت الأجنبي جاز ويعتبر البدل من ثلث مال الأجنبي، فلو كان الزوج مريضاً حين تبرع الأجنبي بخلعها فلها الإرث لو مات الزوج من مرضه ذلك وهي في العدة لأنها لم ترض بهذا الطلاق فيعتبر الزوج فاراً اهـ.
As for the sick woman, it says in Jami' al-Fusulayn: A sick woman sought khul' from her husband in exchange for her mahr and then died. Three things are considered: her husband's inheritance from her, the khul' compensation, and one-third of her wealth. The least of these is taken, not the greater. Thus in 'Shahi' (Sharh al-Tahawi) and in 'Hul' (al-Hul?): In this situation, if he had not consummated the marriage, half the mahr falls due due to the divorce and the other half is a bequest, and it is for a non-heir so it is valid from the third. If he consummated and she died after the 'idda, the entire mahr is a bequest and is valid from the third because khul' is a voluntary gift. If she died during the 'idda, it is like this according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad because the husband no longer remains an heir since he consented to the separation. According to Abu Hanifa, he is given the least of his inheritance, the khul' compensation, and the third, because they (the Sahibayn) considered the rights of the other heirs, but they did not consider the least. And this is analogous to what we all say regarding her divorce at her request in terminal illness. The summary of the difference between the 'idda having passed and not having passed is that after it passes, the husband's share of inheritance is not considered, only the third, so the husband receives up to one-third of the khul' compensation even if it is more than his inheritance. Before the 'idda passes, the third is not considered, only his inheritance, so the husband receives up to the amount of his inheritance from the khul' compensation, not the third if the third is greater. If the husband is her paternal cousin and does not inherit from her because she has other closer agnates, he is like a stranger. If he inherits from her by kinship and she dies after the 'idda passes, the khul' compensation and his inheritance by kinship are considered; if the compensation is equal to or less than his inheritance, it goes to him; if more, the excess does not go to him without the consent of the heirs. This is if she was consummated; otherwise, half returns to the husband due to the divorce before consummation, not as a bequest. As for the other half, if the husband is a stranger, he is a donor, so it is valid from the third; if he is her paternal cousin and inherits from her, he receives the lesser of his inheritance and half the mahr. This is if she died in that illness. If she recovered from it, the entire compensation goes to the husband as if she had gifted it to him, then he inherits from her, and there is no inheritance between them due to marriage if she dies during the 'idda or after, because they both agreed to the annulment of his right. This is if she was sick. If she sought khul' while healthy and the husband is sick, the khul' is valid for the specified amount whether little or much, and they do not inherit from each other if he dies during the 'idda or after. If a third party ransomed her from the husband with wealth that he guarantees to the husband, and this was during the third party's terminal illness, it is valid, and the compensation is considered from one-third of the third party's wealth. If the husband was sick when the third party donated to khul' her, she inherits if the husband dies from that illness while she is in the 'idda because she did not consent to this divorce, so the husband is considered a fugitive (farr). End.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This lengthy passage addresses the complex rulings when a terminally ill wife seeks khul' and then dies. The core principle is that the husband's claim to the compensation is limited to the least of three amounts: his share of her inheritance, the agreed compensation, and one-third of her estate. This protects the rights of other heirs. There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider the compensation fully if she dies during the 'idda (since the husband loses his right of inheritance by consenting to the divorce), while Abu Hanifa always applies the minimal amount rule. The passage also distinguishes between cases where the marriage was consummated or not, and where the husband inherits by kinship or not. Additional scenarios include: the wife recovering (then the compensation is fully due), the husband being sick (no inheritance), and a third party paying the compensation (treated as a gift from the third party's third).

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest; in this context, the khul' compensation is treated as a bequest from the sick wife's estate.
مهر (mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife at marriage; in this khul', the wife gives up her mahr as compensation.
عدة ('idda): The waiting period after divorce or death; here it determines whether the husband still has inheritance rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when a terminally ill wife seeks khul' and then dies, how is the compensation determined?
A) The full agreed compensation is given to the husband.
B) The husband receives the least of three amounts: his inheritance, the compensation, and one-third of the estate.
C) The husband receives the compensation only if it does not exceed one-third of the estate.
D) The compensation is invalid altogether.

Key Takeaway
When a terminally ill wife seeks khul' and dies, the compensation is limited to the least of three amounts to protect other heirs, with a dispute on the husband's inheritance rights during the 'idda.

Coercion and Multiple Offers in Khul'
Rulings on coerced khul' and multiple offers by the wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on coerced khul' and multiple offers, and apply them to disputes about compensation.

Core Idea
Coercion nullifies the compensation in khul'; multiple offers bind by the last one unless the husband initiated.

Khul' is a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation. But what happens if she is forced to accept? Or if she makes several offers for different amounts? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies these scenarios, showing how the school balances consent with contractual clarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct rulings
The passage presents two separate issues: coercion in khul' and multiple offers by the wife. Recognize that each has its own legal effect.
2
Analyze the coercion ruling
If the wife is coerced into accepting khul', the compensation is not binding on her. In a dispute about coercion, her word with an oath is accepted.
Coercion affects only the financial aspect, not the divorce itself.
3
Analyze the multiple offers ruling
When the wife makes multiple offers (e.g., different amounts), the last offer is binding. If the husband makes the offers, both amounts are binding on her.
The default assumption is that the wife's latest offer reflects her final intent.
4
Reason from the underlying principle
In the wife's multiple offers, the later offer replaces the earlier. In the husband's offers, the wife's acceptance is deemed to cover both because the husband's proposal is a single package.
This distinction hinges on who is the proposer and the nature of the offer.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Consider: Wife says 'Divorce me for 500 dirhams' then 'for 300 dirhams'. Husband divorces. The last offer of 300 binds. Now if husband says 'I divorce you for 500 or 300', and wife accepts, both are binding.
Practice using the rules from the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كانت مكرهة على القبول لم يلزمها البدل. وفي القنية : ولو اختلفا في الكره بالخلع والطوع فالقول مع اليمين .اهـ. وفي الظهيرية لو قالت طلقني ثلاثاً بألف درهم طلقني ثلاثاً بمائة دينار فطلقها ثلاثاً طلقت بمائة دينار ولو كان الإيجاب من الزوج بالمالين لزمها المالان اهـ.
If she was coerced into acceptance, the compensation is not binding upon her. In al-Qunyah: If they differ regarding whether the khul' was done under coercion or willingly, the word is supported by oath. End. In al-Zahiriyya: If she said 'Divorce me three times for one thousand dirhams; divorce me three times for one hundred dinars,' and he divorced her three times, she is divorced for one hundred dinars. If the offer was from the husband for both amounts, both amounts are binding upon her. End.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents two separate rulings. First, if the wife is coerced into accepting khul', the compensation is not obligatory on her, although the divorce may still occur (depending on the effect of coercion on the talaq itself). In a dispute about whether there was coercion, the wife's word with an oath is accepted. Second, when the wife makes multiple offers for different amounts (e.g., 'divorce me for 1000 dirhams' and 'divorce me for 100 dinars'), and the husband divorces her, she is bound by the last offer (100 dinars). However, if the husband makes the offers, both amounts are binding on her because the acceptance is deemed to be for the greater obligation.

Key Terms
مكرهة (mukrahah): A woman coerced into accepting khul'.
يمين (yamin): Oath; the wife's claim of coercion is accepted with her oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wife says 'Divorce me three times for 500 dirhams' and then 'Divorce me three times for 300 dirhams.' The husband divorces her three times. How much must she pay?
A) 500 dirhams.
B) 300 dirhams.
C) 800 dirhams.
D) Nothing; the offers are invalid.

Key Takeaway
In khul', coercion invalidates the compensation; multiple offers bind by the last one, unless the husband initiated, then both amounts are binding.

The Principle of Compensation in Khul'
Clarifying husband's non-liability in khul' with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the wife gives compensation in khul' and apply it to scenarios where the husband is mistakenly considered to pay.

Core Idea
In khul', compensation always flows from wife to husband; the husband never pays.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a critical point in Hanafi fiqh regarding khul': the husband is never required to pay any compensation. Many people mistakenly think the husband gives something, but the text corrects this using practical examples. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly applying khul' in contemporary situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Khul' is a divorce initiated by the wife (or with her consent) in exchange for compensation. The passage establishes that the compensation is always binding on the wife, never on the husband.
The key phrase is 'ولزمها المال' (the money is binding upon her).
2
Analyze the first example: 'I khul' you for my slave'
If the husband says this, the divorce occurs upon her acceptance, but no money or property is due from him. The slave is not given by the husband; rather, the wife forfeits her rights (like mahr).
This shows the husband does not pay; the wife's claim is released.
3
Analyze the second example: 'I khul' you for the debt you owe me'
If the wife owes a debt and the husband says this, the debt is forgiven and the divorce occurs. Nothing is due from the husband.
The debt itself becomes the compensation, so no payment is made.
4
Analyze the third example: compensation turns out to be husband's property
If the wife khul' for a slave that later turns out to be the husband's, she owes nothing because the intended compensation never left his possession.
This reinforces that the husband neither gives nor receives in these cases.
5
Understand the practical implication
Many people mistakenly attribute khul' to the husband paying, but the text emphasizes that this is incorrect. The ruling protects the husband from financial obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار بقوله «ولزمها «المال» إلى أنه لا يتصور أن يلزمه مال في الخلع ولذا قال في المجتبى : خلعتك على عبدي وقف على قبولها ولم يجب شيء قلنا : الظاهر أنه عنى بقوله «وقف» على قبولها أي وقوع الطلاق ومعرفة هذه المسألة من أهم المهمات في هذا الزمان لأن الناس يعتادون إضافة الخلع إلى مال الزوج يعد إبرائها إياه من المهر ، فبهذا علم أنها إذا قبلت وقع الطلاق ولم يجب على الزوج شيء. وفي منية الفقهاء : خلعتك بمالي عليك من الدين فقبلت ينبغي أن يقع الطلاق ولا يجب شيء ويبطل الدين، ولو كانت اختلعت على عبد ثم تبين أنه عبد الزوج بتصادقهما ينبغي أن لا يلزمها شيء لسلامة البدل له .اهـ
And he indicated by his statement 'the money is binding upon her' that it is not conceivable that money should be binding upon him in khul'. For this reason, it is said in al-Mujtaba: 'I have khul'ed you for my slave' stops on her acceptance, and nothing is due from him. We say: Apparently he meant by 'stops' that the occurrence of the divorce stops on her acceptance. Knowing this issue is of the utmost importance in this time because people habitually attribute khul' to the husband's wealth after her release from the mahr. Thus it is understood that when she accepts, the divorce occurs and no money is due from the husband. In Munyat al-Fuqaha': 'I have khul'ed you for the debt you owe me' and she accepts, it should be that the divorce occurs, nothing is due from him, and the debt is invalidated. If she sought khul' for a slave and then it becomes clear by their agreement that it was the husband's slave, nothing is binding upon her because the compensation did not leave the husband. End.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage emphasizes a crucial point: in khul', the compensation is always from the wife to the husband, never the reverse. The author notes a common contemporary misunderstanding where people think the husband gives something. The examples clarify: if the husband says 'I khul' you for my slave,' the offer is conditional on her acceptance; if she accepts, the slave is not given by the husband, but rather the wife's claim to mahr or other rights are given up. Similarly, if the wife says 'I khul' you for the debt I owe you,' the debt is forgiven, but the husband does not pay anything. Even if the compensation is later found to be the husband's property, the wife owes nothing because the intended compensation (the slave) never actually left the husband's possession.

Key Terms
مال (mal): Wealth or compensation; in this context, it refers to the consideration given by the wife in khul'.
خلع (khul'): Divorce at the wife's initiative (or with her consent) in exchange for compensation paid by the wife.
عوض ('iwad): Consideration or compensation; in khul', it is the mal given by the wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says to his wife: 'I khul' you for the 1000 dirhams you owe me.' She accepts. What is the consequence?
A) The husband pays 1000 dirhams to the wife.
B) The divorce occurs and the debt is forgiven; the husband pays nothing.
C) The divorce does not occur because the husband must pay.
D) The wife must pay 1000 dirhams to the husband.

Key Takeaway
In khul', the compensation is always from the wife to the husband; the husband never pays.

Khul' Without Compensation and Post-Khul' Increase
Ruling on khul' without specifying compensation and on increasing compensation after khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi ruling on the validity of khul' without mentioning compensation and explain why an increase in compensation after khul' is not valid.

Core Idea
Khul' without specified compensation is valid; increasing compensation after khul' is void.

Two key questions arise in khul' practice: what happens if the spouses agree to khul' but do not mention any compensation? And after the khul' is finalized, can they agree to increase the compensation? This passage from al-Bahr al-Rai'iq clarifies the Hanafi position on both, highlighting an intra-madhhab difference on the first issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first issue: khul' without compensation
Note that the passage discusses whether khul' can be valid without specifying any compensation. There is a narration from Imam Muhammad requiring compensation, but the correct view (asahh) deems it valid.
2
Understand the consequence of the asahh view
When khul' is valid without compensation, the divorce takes effect. The compensation is not fixed, so the wife owes nothing; the khul' is treated as a regular divorce (talaq).
3
Identify the second issue: increase after khul'
The passage then states that any increase in the compensation after the khul' contract is concluded is invalid, because the contract is complete and cannot be altered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظاهر اقتصاره على لزومها المال أنه لو تخالعا ولم يذكرا من المال شيئاً أن لا يصح الخلع وهو رواية عن محمد لأنه لا يكون إلا بالمال ولكن الأصح أنه يصح؛ كذا في المجتبى. وفي الخانية : الزيادة في البدل بعد الخلع غير صحيحة.
And the apparent restriction to the binding of the money upon her implies that if they khul' without mentioning any money, the khul' is not valid. This is a narration from Muhammad because khul' can only be with compensation. But the correct view is that it is valid. Thus in al-Mujtaba. In al-Khaniyya: The increase in the compensation after khul' is not valid.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues. First, can khul' occur without specifying any compensation? There is a narration from Imam Muhammad that it is invalid because khul' requires compensation. However, the correct (asahh) view is that it is valid; the khul' will be considered as a regular divorce (talaq) without compensation, or the compensation will be determined by custom. Second, once the khul' is concluded and the compensation is agreed, any later increase in the compensation is not valid, as the contract is complete.

Key Terms
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The compensation given by the wife to the husband in khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) The khul' is valid only if compensation is assumed.

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi view permits khul' even without specifying compensation, and any post-khul' increase in compensation is not valid.

Resolving Contradictions on Husband's Liability in Khul'
Hashiya reconciling contradictions on husband's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school reconciles the apparent contradiction regarding the husband's liability in khul' and identify the key condition (istithna) that allows it.

Core Idea
The husband can be liable in khul' if his payment is framed as an exception from the mahr (istithna), not as an independent obligation.

In khul', the wife typically gives compensation to secure her release. An earlier statement in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq suggests the husband can never be liable. However, a case from al-Qunyah appears to contradict this. This marginal note (hashiya) resolves the tension by distinguishing scenarios and introducing a legal device: istithna (exception).

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
State the two conflicting rulings: (1) husband cannot be liable in khul', (2) husband can be liable (as in al-Qunyah's case).
2
Apply the reconciliation principle
Note that the first ruling applies when the wife gives no wealth; the Qunyah case involves wealth from both sides (the wife gives up her mahr).
Thus no contradiction when context is considered.
3
Recognize the legal device of istithna
The husband's liability can be structured as an exception from the mahr—as if he keeps part of the mahr and pays it back. This makes it permissible.
Istithna is a valid device in Hanafi law to modify obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خل بالخاء المعجمة رمز إلى الخصائل قوله : (كذا ط) هو بالطاء المهملة رمز للمحيط قوله : (ثم يرثها) أي بالقرابة قوله : (وأشار بقوله ولزمها المال إلى أنه لا يتصور أن يلزمه مال الخ) ينافيه ما يأتي بعد نحو ورقة عن القنية : اختلعت نفسها بالمهر بشرط أن يعطيها كذا مناً من الأرز الأبيض وخالعها به ينبغي أن يصح، ولا يشترط بيان مكان الايفاء عنده إلا أن يقال المراد بعدم تصور ذلك حيث لم يكن من جهتها مال بخلاف مسألة القنية فإن المال من الطرفين وكأنها بذلت المهر في مقابلة الطلاق والأرز. ويوضحه ما يأتي قبيل تلك المسألة : لو خالعها على عبد ومهرها ألف ثم زادها ألفاً فتأمله . وانظر ما يأتي في شرح قوله ويسقط الخلع والمباراة كل حق عند قول المؤلف الثالث أن يقع ببدل على الزوج وقوله بعده ثم اعلم أنه بقي هنا صورة». وحاصله أن المختار جواز كون البدل عليه بأن يحمل على الاستثناء من المهر كأنه قال إلا قدراً من المهر فإنه لا يسقط عني فيجوز إيجاب البدل عليه إذا اختلعت على عوض ويكون مقابلاً ببدل الخلع قوله : ولكن الأصح أنه يصح) قال في النهر :
Khal with kha' and lam is a symbol for al-Khasa'il. His statement: (Kadha Ta) is with the plain Ta, a symbol for al-Muhit. His statement: (then he inherits her) meaning by kinship. His statement: (And he indicated by his statement 'the money is binding upon her' that it is not conceivable that money should be binding upon him, etc.) is contradicted by what comes after about a folio from al-Qunyah: She sought khul' in exchange for her mahr on condition that he give her such and such a quantity of white rice, and he khul'ed her with it. It should be valid. And specification of the place of delivery is not required according to him, unless it is said that the intent by 'not conceivable' is where there is no wealth from her side, unlike the case in al-Qunyah where the wealth is from both sides, as if she gave up the mahr in exchange for the divorce and the rice. And this is clarified by what comes before that issue: If he khul'ed her for a slave and her mahr was one thousand, then he added a thousand to her, consider. And look at what comes in the commentary on his statement: 'Khul' and mubara'ah cancel every right' at the author's third condition that it occurs with compensation from the husband, and his statement after: 'Then know that there remains here a form.' The summary is that the chosen view is that the compensation can be upon the husband by interpreting it as an exception from the mahr, as if he said 'except an amount of the mahr that does not drop from me.' Thus it is permissible for the compensation to be upon the husband when she seeks khul' with a consideration, and it is exchanged for the khul' compensation. His statement: (but the correct view is that it is valid) said in al-Nahr.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This marginal note (hashiya) resolves an apparent contradiction in the text. Earlier, it was stated that the husband cannot be required to pay anything in khul'. However, a case from al-Qunyah suggests the husband does pay (e.g., providing rice in addition to the wife giving up her mahr). The commentator explains that the earlier statement applies only when the wife gives no wealth from her side. In the Qunyah case, the wife gives up her mahr, and the husband provides rice; effectively, both parties give something. The chosen view is that the compensation can be upon the husband if it is structured as an exception from the mahr (i.e., part of the mahr does not drop and the husband pays that part). This does not contradict the principle that the wife is the primary giver, but allows mutual exchange.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
استثناء (istithna): Exception; here, the husband's payment is framed as an exception from the wife's mahr that he keeps.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The husband can be liable if the compensation is framed as an exception from the mahr.
C) The husband can never be liable.
D) The husband is liable if the wife refuses to pay.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows the husband to be liable in khul' when his payment is treated as an exception from the mahr (istithna).

Khul' During Illness and Its Effect on Inheritance
Ruling on khul' during illness and its effect on inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inheritance following khul' during illness in all five scenarios presented.

Core Idea
Khul' during illness is valid, but inheritance is adjusted to prevent abuse.

This lesson examines the rulings related to khul' when one or both parties are ill at the time of divorce. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies how inheritance rights are affected in such situations, balancing the validity of khul' with the need to prevent circumvention of inheritance laws. We will explore five distinct scenarios and their outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the health status of the wife and husband at the time of khul'.
The ruling changes depending on who is ill. Note whether the wife, husband, or a third party (who pays compensation) is ill.
2
Determine the outcome of the illness (death or recovery).
If the ill party dies during that illness, inheritance may be affected. If they recover, normal rules apply.
3
Apply the rule for wife ill: husband receives the lesser of his normal inheritance or half the mahr.
This prevents the husband from gaining by divorcing an ill wife. If she recovers, he gets full compensation and inherits normally.
4
Apply the rule for husband ill: khul' is valid and no inheritance passes between them.
Because the wife initiated divorce, she loses inheritance rights regardless of whether the husband dies in that illness.
5
Consider third-party khul' scenarios.
If a third party pays on the wife's behalf, the ruling depends on the health of the third party and the husband. The compensation is limited to one-third of the third party's wealth if he is terminally ill.
If the husband was ill when the third party paid, the wife inherits if the husband dies because she did not consent to the divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
له ويرثها فله الأقل من إرثه ومن نصف المهر. هذا لو ماتت في ذلك المرض، ولو برئت منه سلم للزوج كل البدل كهبتها منه ثم يرثها ولا إرث بينهما بالزوجية ماتت في العدة أو بعدها لتراضيهما ببطلان حقه. هذا لو كانت مريضة فلو اختلعت صحيحة والزوج مريض فالخلع جائز بالمسمى قل أو كثر ولا إرث بينهما مات في العدة أو بعدها، ولو خلها أجنبي من الزوج بمال ضمنه للزوج وكان ذلك في مرض موت الأجنبي جاز ويعتبر البدل من ثلث مال الأجنبي، فلو كان الزوج مريضاً حين تبرع الأجنبي بخلعها فلها الإرث لو مات الزوج من مرضه ذلك وهي في العدة لأنها لم ترض بهذا الطلاق فيعتبر الزوج فاراً اهـ.
He inherits from her, so he gets the lesser of his inheritance and half the dower. This is if she dies in that illness. And if she recovers from it, the husband gets the entire compensation as if she had gifted it to him, then he inherits from her, and there is no inheritance between them due to marital bond, whether she dies during the iddah or after, because of their mutual consent to the annulment of his right. This is if she was ill. But if she initiated khul' while healthy and the husband was ill, the khul' is valid with the specified (consideration) whether little or much, and there is no inheritance between them whether he dies during the iddah or after. And if a third party ransoms her from the husband with wealth, he guarantees it to the husband, and if that is during the terminal illness of the third party, it is valid, and the consideration is considered from one-third of the third party's wealth. But if the husband was ill when the third party donated the khul' for her, then she inherits if the husband dies from that illness while she is in the iddah, because she did not consent to this divorce, so the husband is considered a fugitive (from inheritance rules). End.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the commentary on khul' concerning illness and its effect on inheritance. The text covers several scenarios: (1) When the wife is ill and initiates khul', then dies in that illness, the husband inherits from her but only the lesser of his normal inheritance or half the dower. (2) If she recovers, the husband gets the full compensation and then inherits as normal. (3) If the wife is healthy but the husband is ill, the khul' is valid and neither inherits from the other. (4) If a third party pays on the wife's behalf during his own terminal illness, the payment is valid but limited to one-third of his wealth. (5) If the husband is ill at the time the third party pays, the wife inherits from him if he dies because she did not consent to the divorce; the husband is deemed to have circumvented inheritance. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that khul' is valid even when illness is present, but inheritance rights may be affected to prevent abuse.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce by redemption from the wife's side
بدل (badal): The consideration paid by the wife in khul'
عدة (iddah): The waiting period after divorce

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a terminally ill wife initiates khul' and then dies in that illness, the husband's inheritance is:
A) His full normal share
B) Half the mahr only
C) The lesser of his normal share or half the mahr
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, khul' during illness is valid but inheritance is adjusted to prevent the healthier party from exploiting the illness to alter inheritance rights.

Consideration in Khul': Validity Without Mentioning Wealth
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of khul' without specifying consideration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khul' without specifying consideration and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the majority.

Core Idea
Khul' is valid even without mentioning any wealth—the separation is the primary objective, not the exchange.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a critical nuance in khul' (divorce initiated by the wife). The matn states that wealth is binding on her, raising the question: what if no wealth is mentioned? The commentator navigates an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, clarifying that the relied-upon position is that khul' remains valid even without specifying a consideration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine the exact question being disputed: Is khul' valid if no compensation (wealth) is mentioned?
2
State the conflicting positions
Imam Muhammad (in one narration) holds it invalid because khul' is analogous to a sale requiring known consideration. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it valid.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the majority view is that khul' does not require explicit consideration.
3
Analyze the proof for invalidity
Imam Muhammad's proof: Khul' is an exchange, and an exchange with unknown consideration is invalid like a sale with unknown price.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The majority argue that the primary objective of khul' is separation, not financial exchange. The Quranic verse 'wa la yahillu lakum…' is general and permits khul' with mutual consent even without mentioning wealth.
Also, the matn's phrase 'and the wealth is binding on her' restricts obligation to the wife, but does not require its mention.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that khul' is valid (sahih) without specifying consideration. The thamarah al-khilaf: if no wealth is mentioned, divorce occurs and no payment is due; if invalidated, no divorce occurs.
This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار بقوله «ولزمها «المال» إلى أنه لا يتصور أن يلزمه مال في الخلع ولذا قال في المجتبى : خلعتك على عبدي وقف على قبولها ولم يجب شيء قلنا : الظاهر أنه عنى بقوله «وقف» على قبولها أي وقوع الطلاق ومعرفة هذه المسألة من أهم المهمات في هذا الزمان لأن الناس يعتادون إضافة الخلع إلى مال الزوج يعد إبرائها إياه من المهر ، فبهذا علم أنها إذا قبلت وقع الطلاق ولم يجب على الزوج شيء. وفي منية الفقهاء : خلعتك بمالي عليك من الدين فقبلت ينبغي أن يقع الطلاق ولا يجب شيء ويبطل الدين، ولو كانت اختلعت على عبد ثم تبين أنه عبد الزوج بتصادقهما ينبغي أن لا يلزمها شيء لسلامة البدل له .اهـ وظاهر اقتصاره على لزومها المال أنه لو تخالعا ولم يذكرا من المال شيئاً أن لا يصح الخلع وهو رواية عن محمد لأنه لا يكون إلا بالمال ولكن الأصح أنه يصح؛ كذا في المجتبى. وفي الخانية : الزيادة في البدل بعد الخلع غير صحيحة . خل بالخاء المعجمة رمز إلى الخصائل قوله : (كذا ط) هو بالطاء المهملة رمز للمحيط قوله : (ثم يرثها) أي بالقرابة قوله : (وأشار بقوله ولزمها المال إلى أنه لا يتصور أن يلزمه مال الخ) ينافيه ما يأتي بعد نحو ورقة عن القنية : اختلعت نفسها بالمهر بشرط أن يعطيها كذا مناً من الأرز الأبيض وخالعها به ينبغي أن يصح، ولا يشترط بيان مكان الايفاء عنده إلا أن يقال المراد بعدم تصور ذلك حيث لم يكن من جهتها مال بخلاف مسألة القنية فإن المال من الطرفين وكأنها بذلت المهر في مقابلة الطلاق والأرز. ويوضحه ما يأتي قبيل تلك المسألة : لو خالعها على عبد ومهرها ألف ثم زادها ألفاً فتأمله . وانظر ما يأتي في شرح قوله ويسقط الخلع والمباراة كل حق عند قول المؤلف الثالث أن يقع ببدل على الزوج وقوله بعده ثم اعلم أنه بقي هنا صورة». وحاصله أن المختار جواز كون البدل عليه بأن يحمل على الاستثناء من المهر كأنه قال إلا قدراً من المهر فإنه لا يسقط عني فيجوز إيجاب البدل عليه إذا اختلعت على عوض ويكون مقابلاً ببدل الخلع قوله : (ولكن الأصح أنه يصح) قال في النهر :
And He indicated by His saying 'and the wealth is binding on her' that it is inconceivable that wealth be binding on him in khul'. Hence, in al-Mujtaba: 'I have made khul' with you for my slave' is suspended on her acceptance, and nothing becomes obligatory. We say: The apparent meaning is that by 'suspended' he means the occurrence of divorce. Understanding this issue is among the most important matters in this time because people are accustomed to adding khul' to the husband's wealth after her release from the dower. Thus, it is known that if she accepts, divorce occurs and nothing is obligatory on the husband. In Munyat al-Fuqaha': 'I have made khul' with you for the debt that you owe me,' and she accepted, it is expected that divorce occurs, nothing is obligatory, and the debt is extinguished. And if she made khul' for a slave, then it becomes clear that it is the husband's slave by their mutual admission, it is expected that nothing is binding on her because the consideration is intact for him. End. The apparent restriction to her being bound by the wealth is that if they make khul' without mentioning any wealth, the khul' is not valid. This is a narration from Muhammad because khul' is only with wealth. But the correct view is that it is valid. Thus in al-Mujtaba. In al-Khaniyyah: An increase in the consideration after khul' is not valid. ...
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The text centers on the phrase 'ولزمها المال' (and the wealth is binding on her) from the matn. The commentator explains that only the wife can be required to pay in khul'; the husband cannot be required to pay. He then discusses various scenarios: if the husband says 'I made khul' for my slave,' it is suspended on her acceptance; if she accepts, divorce occurs without any payment from the husband. Similarly, if the khul' is for a debt the wife owes, the divorce occurs and the debt is extinguished. If the subject of khul' turns out to be the husband's property, nothing is due on her. Then the commentator addresses the issue of khul' without specifying any wealth: there is a narration from Imam Muhammad that it is invalid because khul' requires consideration, but the correct (al-sahh) position is that it is valid. This shows the Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether khul' requires an explicit mention of consideration. The relied-upon position is that it is valid. Also, any increase in the consideration after the khul' is invalid. The text also discusses a potential contradiction where the husband may be required to pay if he makes a condition, but the commentator resolves it by considering it as an exception from the dower. Overall, this passage clarifies the nature of compensation in khul' and emphasizes that it is always from the wife, not the husband.

Key Terms
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The consideration required in khul'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position, what happens if a couple performs khul' without mentioning any compensation?
A) Divorce occurs and no payment is due
B) Divorce does not occur
C) Divorce occurs only if wife pays something
D) It is invalid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, khul' is valid even without specifying consideration; the wife owes nothing unless agreed.

The Prohibition of Husband Taking Compensation in Khul' When He is Nushuz
Ruling with proof on prohibition of husband taking compensation when he is nushuz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the husband taking compensation in khul' when he is nushuz, and explain the Hanafi resolution of the apparent conflict between Quran 4:20 and 2:229.

Core Idea
A husband may not take compensation in khul' when he is at fault (nushuz); to do so is haram.

This lesson tackles a critically important distinction in khul' (divorce by redemption). Many assume compensation is always permissible for the husband. However, the Hanafi school rules that if the husband is the one averse (nushuz), taking any compensation is haram. This ruling is derived from Quran 4:20, and the apparent conflict with 2:229 is resolved by applying each verse to a different scenario. The commentator also refutes a claim of abrogation, affirming the harmony of the Quranic text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruled Act and Its Hukm
The act in question is the husband taking compensation from his wife in exchange for khul' when he is the one with nushuz (aversion). The matn says 'kariha' (it is disliked), but the commentator clarifies that this dislike is tahrimi (prohibitory), meaning it is haram.
The matn uses 'kariha' in a technical sense; the commentator explains the true ruling.
2
Locate the Primary Proof
The primary dalil is Quran 4:20: 'And if you want to replace one wife with another and you have given one of them a great amount [in gifts], do not take from it anything.' The imperative prohibition 'do not take' indicates haram in Hanafi usul.
The verse is general but applies specifically when the husband is at fault.
3
Address the Apparent Conflict
Quran 2:229 says: 'There is no blame upon them for what she ransoms herself with' — permitting khul'. This seems to contradict 4:20. The conflict is resolved by identifying the scenario for each verse.
The conflict is only apparent; both verses are sahih and must be reconciled.
4
Apply the Hanafi Resolution
The Hanafi resolution: 4:20 applies when the husband is nushuz (aversion from him), while 2:229 applies when the wife is nushuz or both are averse. Thus, each verse governs a different situation, so no contradiction exists.
This is a tafsir of the Quran by specifying the context, not an abrogation.
5
Evaluate the Claim of Abrogation
Some scholars (like Ibn Zayd) claimed that 4:20 is abrogated by 2:229. The commentator refutes this, showing that the verses are consistent and not contradictory, so no naskh is needed. The ruling of prohibition stands.
The commentator uses the principle that a general text can be specified without abrogation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكره له أخذ شيء إن نشز) أي كرهها والنشوز يكون من الزوجين وهو كراهة كل واحد منهما صاحبه كما في المغرب. وفي المصباح : نشزت المرأة من زوجها نشوزاً من بابي قعد وضرب عصت زوجها وامتنعت عليه ونشز الرجل من امرأته نشوزاً بالوجهين تركها وجفاها. وفي التنزيل وإن امرأة خافت من بعلها نشوزاً أو اعراضاً [النساء : ١٢٨] وأصله الارتفاع يقال نشز من مكانه نشوزاً بالوجهين إذا ارتفع عنه. . وفي السبعة «وإذا قيل انشروا فانشزوا بالضم والكسر والنشز بفتحتين المكان المرتفع من الأرض والسكون لغة فيه اهـ. وأراد بالكراهة كراهة التحريم المنتهضة سبباً للعقاب والحق أن الأخذ في هذه الحالة حرام قطعاً لقوله تعالى فلا تأخذوا منه شيئاً ﴾ [النساء : ۲۰] ولا يعارضه الآية الأخرى فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۲۹] لأن تلك فيما إذا كان النشوز من قبله فقط والأخرى فيما إذا خافا أن لا يقيما حدود الله فليس من قبله فقط نشوز على أنهما لو تعارضا كانت حرمت الأخذ ثابتة بالعمومات القطعية فإن الإجماع على حرمة أخذ مال المسلم بغير حق وفي إمساكها لا لرغبة بل إضراراً وتضييقاً ليقتطع ما لها في مقابلة خلاصها من الشدة التي هي معه فيها ذلك وقال تعالى ولا تمسكوهن ضراراً لتعتدوا ومن يفعل ذلك فقد ظلم نفسه [البقرة : ۲۳۱] فهذا دليل قطعي على حرمة أخذ مالها كذلك فيكون حراماً إلا أنه لو أخذ جاز في الحكم أي يحكم بصحة التمليك وإن كان بسبب خبيث وتمامه في فتح القدير. وفي الدر المنثور أخرج ابن أبي جرير عن ابن زيد في الآية قال : ثم رخص بعد فقال فإن خفتم أن لا يقيما حدود الله فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به قال فنسخت هذه تلك اه والحاصل أن ما في النساء منسوخ بآية البقرة وهو يقتضي حل الأخذ مطلقاً إذا رضيت . أطلقه فشمل القليل والكثير ويلحق به الإيراء عما لها عليه فإنه لا يجوز أيضاً إذا كان النشوز منه لأنه اعتداء وإضرار قوله : وإن نشزت (لا أي لا يكره له الأخذ إذا كانت هي الكارهة. أطلقه فشمل القليل والكثير وإن كان أكثر مما أعطاها وهو المذكور في الجامع الصغير، وسواء كان منه نشوز لها أيضاً أو لا، فإن كانت الكراهة من الجانبين فالإباحة ثابتة بعبارة قوله تعالى فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۲۹] وإن كانت من جانبها فقط فبدلالتها يعني ويسقط المهر على ما مر . :قلت وسيأتي في كلام المؤلف عند قوله ويسقط الخلع والمباراة كل حق الخ عن الخلاصة وغيرها وسنذكر تحقيق المقام . هناك قوله : (وفي امساكها لا لرغبة الجار والمجرور خبر مقدم وقوله «ذلك» مبتدأ مؤخر والإشارة إلى قوله أخذ مال المسلم بغير حق قوله : (وهو يقتضي حل الأخذ مطلقاً) أي سواء كان النشوز منه أو منها . قلت لكن قد علمت مما قدمه أن آية فلا تأخذوا منه شيئاً [النساء : ٢٠] فيما إذا كان النشوز منه وآية فلا جناح عليهما ) [البقرة : ۲۲۹] فيما إذا كان منها فلا تعارض
His saying: 'And it is disliked for him to take anything if he (the husband) is nushuz' means its dislike is extreme. Nushuz occurs from both spouses; it is each one's aversion to the other, as in al-Mughrib. In al-Misbah: 'Nashazat al-mar'ah min zawjiha nushuzan' – she disobeyed and refused him. 'Nashaza al-rajul min imra'atihi' – he left and avoided her. In the Quran: 'And if a woman fears from her husband nushuz or aversion' [4:128]. Its origin is elevation. In al-Sab'ah: 'And when it is said, "Spread out," then spread out' with damm and kasr; nashaz is the high ground. He meant by dislike a prohibition that necessitates punishment. The truth is that taking in this situation is absolutely forbidden due to His saying 'So do not take anything from it' [4:20]. And the other verse 'There is no blame upon them for what she ransoms herself with' [2:229] does not contradict it, because that is when nushuz is solely from him, and the other when they fear they cannot maintain the limits of Allah. So it is not solely from him. Even if they were contradictory, the prohibition of taking is established by absolute general proofs, for there is consensus on the prohibition of taking a Muslim's wealth without right. And in detaining her not out of desire but to harm and restrict so that she will give her wealth in exchange for release from the hardship she is with him in, Allah says: 'And do not detain them to harm them to transgress; and whoever does that has wronged himself' [2:231]. This is a decisive proof for the prohibition of taking her wealth in such a manner. However, if he does take it, it is effective in terms of legal judgment, i.e., the ownership is valid even if due to a corrupt cause. The full discussion is in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Durr al-Manthur: Ibn Jarir reported from Ibn Zayd regarding the verse: 'Then He granted a concession afterwards and said: If you fear that you cannot maintain the limits of Allah, then there is no blame upon them for what she ransoms herself with' [2:229]. He said: This abrogated that [4:20]. So the conclusion is that the verse in al-Nisa' is abrogated by the verse in al-Baqarah, which permits taking absolutely if she is willing. It is general and includes little and much. By analogy, if he makes her swear an oath regarding what she owes him, it is also not permissible if nushuz is from him because it is transgression and harm. His saying: 'And if she (the wife) is nushuz, no, i.e., it is not disliked for him to take if she is the one who dislikes him.' It is general and includes little and much, even if it is more than what she gave him, as mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Whether or not there is also nushuz from him, if the aversion is from both sides, permissibility is established by the text of His saying 'there is no blame upon them for what she ransoms herself with' [2:229]. And if it is only from her side, then by its indication, i.e., the dower falls, as before. I say: It will come in the author's words at his saying 'and khul' and mubara'ah cancel every right' from al-Khulasa and others, and we will mention the verification of the matter there. There is his saying: 'And in detaining her not out of desire' – the preposition and its object are an advanced predicate, and 'that' is a delayed subject, and the reference is to his saying 'taking a Muslim's wealth without right.' His saying: 'And it necessitates the permissibility of taking absolutely' means whether nushuz is from him or from her. I say: But you have known from what was presented that the verse 'do not take anything' [4:20] applies when nushuz is from him, and the verse 'no blame' [2:229] applies when it is from her, so there is no contradiction.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. It explains the matn statement 'وكره له أخذ شيء إن نشز' (it is disliked for him to take anything if he is nushuz). The commentator defines nushuz as aversion from either spouse. He then establishes that if the husband is the one averse and wants to take compensation, it is haram, citing Quran 4:20 which forbids taking back anything given. The verse 2:229 which permits khul' is not in contradiction because it applies when the aversion is mutual or from the wife. If there is contradiction, the prohibition is supported by consensus and general proofs about not taking Muslim wealth unjustly. However, if the husband does take it, the ownership is valid legally. The commentator then mentions a view that 4:20 is abrogated by 2:229, so taking is permissible absolutely if the wife agrees. But the commentator's own view is that there is no abrogation; each verse applies to a different scenario, so no contradiction. Thus, the ruling is: it is forbidden for the husband to take compensation if he is nushuz; permissible if the wife is nushuz.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushuz): Aversion or disobedience by either spouse; the legal cause for different rulings in khul'.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Disliked (makruh tanzih)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
The husband's taking compensation in khul' when he is nushuz is haram; the Quranic verses are not contradictory but apply to different scenarios.
