The Ruling on a Nashiz Husband Taking from His Wife
Commentary proving the prohibition when husband is nashiz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband is nashiz and evaluate the claim of abrogation between Quran 4:20 and 2:229.

Core Idea
Taking from the wife when the husband is nashiz is haram by Quran, consensus, and reason.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies an important marital fiqh issue: what happens when the husband is the one at fault? While the matn says 'disliked', the commentator upgrades it to haram and engages with a potential abrogation dispute. Let us trace the proof and understand why the husband cannot take any money in khul' when he is nashiz.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of nushuz
Nushuz is defined as dislike and aversion between spouses; it can come from either side. The commentator cites lexicons to establish the linguistic meaning and its Qur'anic usage.
Note that nushuz from the husband includes leaving and harsh treatment.
2
Identify the ruling: karahah tahrimiyyah = haram
The matn says 'disliked', but the commentator clarifies that this is a prohibitive dislike (karahah tahrimiyyah), meaning it is haram to take anything from the wife when the husband is nashiz.
In Hanafi usul, karahah tahrimiyyah is close to haram and entails sin.
3
Examine the primary dalil: Quran 4:20
The verse 'Do not take anything from it' is a direct prohibition. According to Hanafi usul, a prohibition (nahy) indicates that the act is haram.
The verse is in the context of divorce and taking back dower.
4
Address the potential contradiction with Quran 2:229 (khul')
Some claim that 2:229 (no sin if she ransoms herself) abrogates 4:20, making khul' payment always permissible. The commentator rejects this by specifying the different situations: 4:20 applies when the husband is nashiz, 2:229 applies when both fear they cannot uphold Allah's limits.
Alternatively, even if abrogated, the prohibition is supported by other categorical proofs.
5
Resolve the contradiction and conclude the Hanafi position
The commentator favors specification (takhsis) over abrogation, and also adduces consensus on the prohibition of taking a Muslim's property without right, and the verse against oppressive detention (2:231). Thus, when the husband is nashiz, taking from the wife is absolutely haram.
The mufta bihi is that it is haram; if taken, ownership is valid in judicial terms but the act is sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكره له أخذ شيء إن نشز) أي كرهها والنشوز يكون من الزوجين وهو كراهة كل واحد منهما صاحبه كما في المغرب. وفي المصباح : نشزت المرأة من زوجها نشوزاً من بابي قعد وضرب عصت زوجها وامتنعت عليه ونشز الرجل من امرأته نشوزاً بالوجهين تركها وجفاها. وفي التنزيل وإن امرأة خافت من بعلها نشوزاً أو اعراضاً [النساء : ١٢٨] وأصله الارتفاع يقال نشز من مكانه نشوزاً بالوجهين إذا ارتفع عنه. . وفي السبعة «وإذا قيل انشروا فانشزوا بالضم والكسر والنشز بفتحتين المكان المرتفع من الأرض والسكون لغة فيه اهـ. وأراد بالكراهة كراهة التحريم المنتهضة سبباً للعقاب والحق أن الأخذ في هذه الحالة حرام قطعاً لقوله تعالى فلا تأخذوا منه شيئاً ﴾ [النساء : ۲۰] ولا يعارضه الآية الأخرى فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۲۹] لأن تلك فيما إذا كان النشوز من قبله فقط والأخرى فيما إذا خافا أن لا يقيما حدود الله فليس من قبله فقط نشوز على أنهما لو تعارضا كانت حرمت الأخذ ثابتة بالعمومات القطعية فإن الإجماع على حرمة أخذ مال المسلم بغير حق وفي إمساكها لا لرغبة بل إضراراً وتضييقاً ليقتطع ما لها في مقابلة خلاصها من الشدة التي هي معه فيها ذلك وقال تعالى ولا تمسكوهن ضراراً لتعتدوا ومن يفعل ذلك فقد ظلم نفسه [البقرة : ۲۳۱] فهذا دليل قطعي على حرمة أخذ مالها كذلك فيكون حراماً إلا أنه لو أخذ جاز في الحكم أي يحكم بصحة التمليك وإن كان بسبب خبيث وتمامه في فتح القدير. وفي الدر المنثور أخرج ابن أبي جرير عن ابن زيد في الآية قال : ثم رخص بعد فقال فإن خفتم أن لا يقيما حدود الله فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به قال فنسخت هذه تلك اه والحاصل أن ما في النساء منسوخ بآية البقرة وهو يقتضي حل الأخذ مطلقاً إذا رضيت . أطلقه فشمل القليل والكثير ويلحق به الإيراء عما لها عليه فإنه لا يجوز أيضاً إذا كان النشوز منه لأنه اعتداء وإضرار
His saying: (And it is disliked for him to take anything if he is nashiz) meaning it is disliked for him. And nushuz can be from both spouses: it is the dislike of each one for the other, as in al-Mughrib. In al-Misbah: A woman is nashiz from her husband by the two measures of qa'ada and daraba: she disobeys her husband and refuses him. And a man is nashiz from his wife by both measures: he leaves her and treats her harshly. And in the Revelation: 'And if a woman fears from her husband nushuz or aversion' [4:128]. Its origin is elevation; it is said: he rose from his place with both measures if he rises from it. And in al-Sab'ah: 'And when it is said: arise, then arise' with damm and kasr. And al-nashz with two fathas is the raised place of the earth, and sukun is a language therein. He intended by karahah the karahah of tahrim that is a cause for punishment, and the truth is that taking in this situation is absolutely haram by His statement: 'Do not take anything from it' [4:20]. And the other verse 'There is no sin upon them in what she ransoms herself with' [2:229] does not contradict it, because that [first] is when nushuz is only from him, and the other is when they fear that they cannot uphold the limits of Allah. So it is not nushuz only from him. Even if they contradicted, the prohibition of taking is established by categorical general proofs, for there is consensus on the prohibition of taking a Muslim's property without right. And detaining her not out of desire but harming and oppressing to take her property in exchange for her deliverance from the hardship she is in with him, He said: 'Do not detain them harmfully to transgress; and whoever does that has wronged himself' [2:231]. So this is a categorical proof of the prohibition of taking her property likewise, so it is haram. However, if he took it, it is valid in judgment, i.e., the ownership is judged valid even though it was due to a corrupt cause. Its completion is in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Durr al-Manthur: Ibn Abi Jarir narrated from Ibn Zayd regarding the verse: He said: then He granted concession afterwards and said: 'If you fear that you cannot uphold the limits of Allah, then there is no sin upon them in what she ransoms herself with.' He said: this abrogated that. The result: what is in al-Nisa' is abrogated by the verse of al-Baqarah, and it implies permissibility of taking absolutely if she consents. He made it absolute, so it includes little and much. And annexed to it is the reduction of what she owes him, for that is also not permissible if the nushuz is from him, because it is transgression and harm.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling from the matn regarding the husband who is nashiz (disobedient, averse). The commentator first defines nushuz, citing lexicons: it is dislike and aversion between spouses, and the verb can apply to both. Then he clarifies that the 'karahah' (dislike) mentioned in the matn is actually karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitive dislike), meaning it is haram to take anything from the wife in this situation. He proves this from the Qur'anic verse 'Do not take anything from it [what you gave]' (4:20), which addresses husbands who want to take back the dower when they intend to divorce their wives and have given them a great amount. He addresses the potential contradiction with the verse 'There is no sin upon them in what she ransoms herself with' (2:229), which allows khul'. The commentator resolves this by specifying that each verse applies to a different situation: the prohibition applies when the nushuz is from the husband, while the permission applies when both fear they cannot uphold Allah's limits (i.e., the wife initiates khul' due to her own aversion). He further supports the prohibition with the principle of consensus that taking a Muslim's property without right is haram, and that detaining the wife harmfully to extract her property is also haram by another verse (2:231). He then mentions that according to some, the verse in al-Nisa' is abrogated by al-Baqarah, but the commentator does not fully endorse this, as the latter verse is not absolute. He concludes that if the nushuz is from the husband, it is not permissible to take anything, even if she consents, because it is a form of oppression.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushūz): Dislike and aversion between spouses; disobedience or harsh treatment by either party.
كراهة التحريم (karāhat al-taḥrīm): A level of prohibition that is established by speculative evidence, but here the commentator asserts it is haram (tahrim).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, which of the following is the correct ruling when a husband is nashiz and his wife wants khul'?
A) It is permissible for him to take part of the dower because she initiated divorce.
B) It is haram for him to take anything because he is the nashiz.
C) It is makruh (disliked) but valid.
D) It is permissible only if the amount is small.

Key Takeaway
When the husband is at fault (nashiz), he cannot take any of the dower in khul'; the prohibition is absolute and supported by multiple proofs.

The Ruling When Wife Is Nashizah: Taking More Than the Dower
Commentary on permissibility of taking more than dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking more than the dower in khul' when the wife is nashizah and explain the proof from the Quran.

Core Idea
When the wife is the averse party, the husband may take any amount, even exceeding the dower, due to the absolute permission of the Quranic text.

In this lesson, we continue the discussion of khul' by examining a key scenario: when the wife initiates the separation because she is averse (nashizah). The classical Hanafi texts raise the question of whether the husband may take more than the dower he gave. The commentator resolves a seeming tension between different narrations and proofs, ultimately affirming the broad permission from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage addresses the case where the wife is the nashizah (averse). The matn states it is not disliked (la yukrah) for the husband to take something from her in khul'.
This is the starting point: the husband's taking is not automatically prohibited or disliked.
2
Determine the scope of the ruling
The commentator explains that the ruling is absolute ('atlaqahu) – it includes little and much, even if the amount exceeds the dower he originally gave. This is the position of al-Jami' al-Saghir.
The absolute wording of the verse 'fala junah' supports this.
3
Distinguish sub-cases based on fault
If both parties are averse, permissibility is from the explicit Quranic text (Surah al-Baqarah 2:229). If only the wife is averse, permissibility is by its implication (since she is ransoming herself).
This distinction justifies the application in both scenarios.
4
Resolve apparent contradiction with other evidence
The verse 'Do not take anything' (Surah al-Nisa 4:20) applies when the husband is the averse party. The verse of permission (2:229) applies when the wife is averse. No contradiction exists.
The verses address different situations.
5
Evaluate the hadith evidence and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
A hadith says 'as for the increase, no.' The commentator argues this solitary hadith cannot restrict the absolute text of the Quran because it is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah. He sides with the absolute permission over the matn's karahah.
This reflects the usul principle that a khabar wahid cannot restrict a qat'i text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وإن نشزت (لا أي لا يكره له الأخذ إذا كانت هي الكارهة. أطلقه فشمل القليل والكثير وإن كان أكثر مما أعطاها وهو المذكور في الجامع الصغير، وسواء كان منه نشوز لها أيضاً أو لا، فإن كانت الكراهة من الجانبين فالإباحة ثابتة بعبارة قوله تعالى فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۲۹] وإن كانت من جانبها فقط فبدلالتها يعني ويسقط المهر على ما مر . :قلت وسيأتي في كلام المؤلف عند قوله ويسقط الخلع والمباراة كل حق الخ عن الخلاصة وغيرها وسنذكر تحقيق المقام . هناك قوله : (وفي امساكها لا لرغبة الجار والمجرور خبر مقدم وقوله «ذلك» مبتدأ مؤخر والإشارة إلى قوله أخذ مال المسلم بغير حق قوله : (وهو يقتضي حل الأخذ مطلقاً) أي سواء كان النشوز منه أو منها . قلت لكن قد علمت مما قدمه أن آية فلا تأخذوا منه شيئاً [النساء : ٢٠] فيما إذا كان النشوز منه وآية فلا جناح عليهما ) [البقرة : ۲۲۹] فيما إذا كان منها فلا تعارض بالاولى والمذكور في الأصل كراهة الزيادة على ما أعطاها وينبغي حمله على خلاف الأول كما ينبغي حمل الحديث عليه أيضاً وهو قوله أما الزيادة فلا لأن النص نفي الجناح مطلقاً فتقييده بخبر الواحد لا يجوز لما عرف في الأصول ولذا قال في فتح القدير: إن رواية الجامع أوجه وصحح الشمني رواية الأصل لأحاديث ذكرها .
His saying: 'And if she is nashizah (no)' meaning no, it is not disliked for him to take if she is the averse one. He made it absolute, so it includes little and much, even if it is more than what he gave her, and that is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir. And it is the same whether there is nushuz from him towards her or not. If the aversion is from both sides, permissibility is established by the literal wording of His statement: 'There is no sin upon them in what she ransoms herself with' [2:229]. And if it is only from her side, then by its implication, meaning the dower is dropped as previously mentioned. I say: There will come in the author's statement at his saying 'and the khul' and mubara'ah drop every right' from al-Khulasah and others, and we will mention the investigation of the matter there. His saying: 'And in detaining her not out of desire' [the prepositional phrase is a delayed predicate, and 'that' is a delayed subject, and the reference is to his saying 'taking a Muslim's property without right']. His saying: 'And it implies the permissibility of taking absolutely' i.e., whether the nushuz is from him or from her. I say: But you have learned from what I presented that the verse 'Do not take anything from it' [4:20] is when the nushuz is from him, and the verse 'There is no sin upon them' [2:229] is when it is from her, so there is no contradiction. Rather, the mention in the matn of karahah for taking more than what he gave should be understood as contrary to this first case, and likewise the hadith should be taken accordingly: his saying 'As for the increase, no', because the text negated sin absolutely, so restricting it by a solitary hadith is not permissible as known in usul. Hence he said in Fath al-Qadir that the narration of al-Jami' is more appropriate, and al-Shumnni authenticated the narration of the matn due to hadith he mentioned.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the khul' chapter, now addressing the case where the wife is the nashizah (averse). The commentator explains that if she is the one who dislikes him, it is not disliked for the husband to take something from her in khul', and this is absolute, including even an amount exceeding the dower he gave. He distinguishes three scenarios: if both are at fault, permissibility is from the explicit text of Quran 2:229; if only she is at fault, permissibility is by its implication (since she is ransoming herself). He then addresses a potential contradiction between the verses of prohibition (4:20) and permission (2:229), asserting they apply to different situations. He also discusses the matn's statement about karahah of taking more than the dower, stating this should be understood as against the first (husband at fault) case, and a hadith saying 'as for the increase, no' is not sufficient to restrict the absolute permission of the Quran. He mentions that the narration in al-Jami' al-Saghir is more appropriate, but al-Shumnni validated the matn's narration based on other hadith.

Key Terms
بضاعة (buḍā‘ah): Not present in this passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only up to the amount of the dower
B) Any amount, including more than the dower
C) Nothing at all, because khul' is invalid
D) Only a nominal amount

Key Takeaway
The husband may take any amount, even more than the dower, from a nashizah wife, because the Quranic text is absolute and unconstrained.

The Principle: What Is Valid as Mahr Is Valid as Khul' Consideration
Principle that what is valid as mahr is valid as khul' consideration, with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that valid mahr items are valid khul' consideration and apply it to examples.

Core Idea
What suffices as mahr suffices as khul' consideration because the vulva is less valuable at dissolution.

In this lesson, we explore the foundational rule that any item valid as dower (mahr) can serve as the wife's payment in khul'. The reasoning is analogical: if an item is good enough to compensate the vulva when it is at its highest value (marriage), it is certainly good enough when it is released at a lower value (khul'). We will look at the proof, the conditions, and several concrete examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
The rule is: 'What is valid as mahr is valid as khul' consideration.' The proof is a qiyas: the vulva is mutaqawwim at marriage (entry) and non-mutaqawwim at khul' (exit), so any compensation valid for the higher value is valid for the lower.
This is a clear talil (justification) based on the relative value of the vulva.
2
Examine the examples of valid considerations
Valid examples include: a described garment, a measured or weighed item, cultivation of her land, riding her animal, and her personal service (without seclusion). These are all valid as mahr, so they are valid in khul'.
The key condition is that the item must be specified and free from gharar.
3
Understand when the consideration is invalid
If the khul' is for a garment or house without proper description, the consideration is invalid. In that case, the wife must return the original mahr (the mahr she received at marriage).
This shows that the principle requires specification; ambiguity invalidates the consideration.
4
Recognize the authority and mufta bihi
This principle is from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and is part of Zahir al-Riwayah. The mufta bihi is that whatever is valid as mahr is valid as khul' consideration, but not vice versa.
The following lesson addresses exceptions to the reverse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وما صلح مهر اصلح بدل الخلع لأن ما صلح عوضاً للمتقوم أولى أن يصلح عوضاً لغير المتقوم فإن البضع غير متقوم حالة الخروج ومتقوم حالة الدخول فمنع الأب خلع صغيرته على مالها وجاز له تزوج ولده بماله ونفذ خلع المريضة من الثلث، وجاز تزويج المريض بمهر المثل من جميع ماله فصح الخلع على ثوب موصوف أو مكيل أو موزون كالمهر، وكذا على زراعة أرضها أو ركوب دابتها وخدمتها على وجه لا يلزم خلوة بها أو خدمة أجنبي لأن هذه تجوز مهراً وبطل البدل فيه لو كان ثوباً أو داراً كالمهر ووجب عليها رد المهر. وأشار إلى أن هذا الأصل لا ينعكس كلياً فلا يصبح أن يقال ما لا يصلح مهراً لا يصلح بدلاً في الخلع لأنه لو خالعها على ما في بطن جاريتها أو غنمها صح وله ما في بطونها ولا يجوز مهراً بل يجب مهر المثل، وكذا على أقل من عشرة، وكذا على ما في يدها؛ كذا في التبيين وفتح القدير. وذكر في غاية البيان أنه مطرد منعكس كلياً لأن الغرض من طرد الكلي أن يكون مالاً متقوماً ليس فيه جهالة مستتمة وما دون العشرة بهذه المثابة، ومن عكس الكلي أن لا يكون مالاً متقوماً أو أن يكون فيه جهالة مستتمة وما دون العشرة مال متقوم ليس فيه جهالة فلا يرد السؤال لا على الطرد الكلي ولا على عكسه .اهـ. وفي المحيط : لو اختلعت على ثوب لم يتبين جنسه أو على دار فله المهر وفي العبد يلزمها الوسط، ولو اختلعت على ما تكتسبه العام أو على ما ترثه من المال أو على أن تزوجه امرأة وتمهرها عنه فالشرط باطل وترد المهر، ولو اختلعت بحكمه أو بحكمها صح فإن حكمت ولم يرض الزوج رجع بالمهر، ولو خلعها على ألف إلى الحصاد ثبت الأجل، ولو قالت إلى قدوم فلان أو موته وجب المال حالاً، ولو خالعها على دراهم معينة فوجدها ستوقة يرجع بالجياد، وكذلك الثوب على أنه هروي فإذا هو مروي يرجع بهروي وسط ولا يرد بدل الخلع إلا بعيب فاحش فإن كان حلال عدم بین بينهما حتى تنسخ إحداهما بالأخرى قوله : وصحح الشمني رواية الأصل) قد علمت المنافاة الروايتين بما ذكره من التوفيق وهو مصرح به في الفتح فإنه ذكر أولاً أن المسألة مختلفة بين الصحابة ثم ساق النصوص من الطرفين ثم حقق ثم قال : وعلى هذا يظهر كون رواية الجامع أوجه. نعم يكون أخذ الزيادة خلاف الأولى والمنع محمول عل ما هو الأولى وطريق القرب إلى الله سبحانه قوله : (وذكر في غاية البيان أنه مطرد منعكس الخ) قال في النهر : لا يخفى أن الصلاحية المطلقة وكون مطلق المال المتقوم خالياً عن الكمية يصلح مهراً ممنوع فلذا منع المحققون انعكاسها كلية
His saying: (And what is valid as a mahr is valid as a consideration for khul') because what is valid as compensation for something of value is more worthy to be valid as compensation for something not of value. For the vulva is not of value at the time of exit (khul') but is of value at the time of entry (marriage). Thus the father is prevented from doing khul' of his minor daughter for her property, but he is allowed to marry his son for his property. And the khul' of a sick woman is executed from one-third. And it is permissible for a sick man to marry for mahr al-mithl from all his property. So khul' is valid for a described garment, or a measured or weighed item, like the mahr. Likewise for cultivation of her land, or riding her animal, or her service in a way that does not require seclusion with her or service of a foreigner, because these are valid as mahr. And the consideration is invalid if it were a garment or house like the mahr, and she must return the mahr. He indicated that this principle is not universally reversible, so one cannot say: what is not valid as mahr is not valid as a consideration in khul'. Because if he does khul' with her for what is in the belly of his slave-girl or his sheep, it is valid and he gets what is in their bellies, but it is not valid as mahr; rather mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Likewise for less than ten [dirhams]. Likewise for what is in her hand. Thus in al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir. And it is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that it [the principle] is regular and universally reversible, because the purpose of the regularity of the universal is that it be valuable property without complete ignorance, and less than ten is of this nature. And of the reversal of the universal is that it not be valuable property or that it have complete ignorance. And less than ten is valuable property without ignorance, so the objection does not arise against the regularity or its reversal. End. In al-Muhit: If she did khul' for a garment whose type was not specified, or for a house, then he gets the mahr, and for a slave she must pay the middle value. And if she did khul' for what she will earn in the year, or for what she will inherit of wealth, or that she marry him a woman and pay the mahr for him, the condition is invalid and she returns the mahr. And if she did khul' by his judgment or her judgment, it is valid; if she judged and the husband did not consent, he reverts to the mahr. And if he did khul' with her for one thousand until harvest, the term is confirmed. And if she said 'until the arrival of so-and-so' or 'his death', the wealth is due immediately. And if he did khul' with her for specified dirhams and found them bad, he returns to good dirhams. Likewise a garment as Herawi and it turned out to be Marwi, he returns to a medium Herawi. And the consideration in khul' is not returned except for a grave defect. If it was lawful... [text unclear] ...between them until one abrogates the other. His saying: 'And al-Shumnni authenticated the narration of the matn' you have known the conflict between the two narrations by what he mentioned of reconciliation, which is explicit in al-Fath, for he stated first that the issue is disputed among the Companions, then he presented the texts from both sides, then he investigated, then he said: Upon this, the narration of al-Jami' is more appropriate. Indeed, taking the increase is against the best, and prohibition is carried on what is best and the way of closeness to Allah. His saying: 'And it is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that it is regular and reversible...' He said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that absolute validity and that absolute valuable property devoid of quantity is valid as mahr is prevented, so the verifiers prevented its universality of reversal.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage discusses the general principle that anything which can serve as a valid dower (mahr) can also serve as the consideration (badal) in a khul'. The reasoning is that the vulva (buda') is more valuable at the time of marriage (when it is compensated) than at the time of khul' (when it is being released). Therefore, if something is good enough to be the price of the vulva at its highest value, it is certainly suitable for its lower value. The text then gives examples: khul' is valid for a described garment, a measured or weighed item, for cultivation of her land, riding her animal, or her personal service (without seclusion). However, the principle is not fully reversible: there are things that are valid as khul' consideration but not as dower, such as something in the belly of a slave girl or sheep (unborn young), or an amount less than ten dirhams. These are valid in khul' but require mahr al-mithl in marriage. The passage then lists various rulings from al-Muhit about specific conditions in khul', such as unspecified terms, future earnings, or defective items. The commentator also discusses the reliability of narrations regarding taking more than the dower, favoring the narration that permits it absolutely.

Key Terms
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul‘): The consideration given by the wife to the husband in exchange for divorce.
مهر (mahr): Dower given by husband to wife at marriage, which is a model for valid consideration in khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid consideration in khul' according to the principle taught in this lesson?
A) An unspecified garment
B) Cultivation of her land for one year
C) A house without description
D) Service that involves seclusion with an ajnabi

Key Takeaway
Anything valid as mahr (specified, valuable, deliverable) is valid as khul' consideration, but the reverse has exceptions.

Exceptions: When the Khul' Consideration Differs from Mahr
Exceptions to the general rule and intra-Hanafi debate on reversibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list examples of items valid as khul' consideration but not as mahr, and explain the intra-Hanafi debate on the reversibility of the principle.

Core Idea
The khul' consideration can include items like unborn livestock or less than ten dirhams, which are invalid as mahr.

While the general rule is that what is valid as mahr is valid as khul' consideration, the reverse is not always true. Hanafi scholars discuss several items that can serve as badal al-khul' but would not be acceptable as dower. This lesson examines those exceptions, the rationale behind them, and the differing views within the school on whether the principle is fully reversible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed exception
The passage states that the principle is not universally reversible: 'you cannot say what is not valid as mahr is not valid as khul' consideration.' Examples are given.
This contradicts a strict reading of the rule.
2
List the specific exceptions from the text
Items valid in khul' but not mahr: (1) what is in the belly of a slave-girl or sheep (unborn), (2) less than ten dirhams, (3) unspecified wealth 'what is in her hand'.
In mahr, these are invalid due to gharar or insufficient value; in khul', they are acceptable.
3
Understand the conflicting opinion
Ghayat al-Bayan argues that the principle IS regular and universally reversible, claiming that items like less than ten dirhams are valuable and known, so they should be valid in both. The objection is about absolute validity.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Examine additional rulings from al-Muhit
Al-Muhit provides further cases: unspecified garment/house, future earnings, inheritance, marriage as consideration – all invalid. Also rules on defective items and terms.
These illustrate the boundary conditions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator sides with non-reversibility, as indicated by the statement 'the principle is not universally reversible' and the examples. This is the relied-upon position.
The debate shows the importance of analyzing the intended meaning of the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تزوجه امرأة وتمهرها عنه فالشرط باطل وترد المهر، ولو اختلعت بحكمه أو بحكمها صح فإن حكمت ولم يرض الزوج رجع بالمهر، ولو خلعها على ألف إلى الحصاد ثبت الأجل، ولو قالت إلى قدوم فلان أو موته وجب المال حالاً، ولو خالعها على دراهم معينة فوجدها ستوقة يرجع بالجياد، وكذلك الثوب على أنه هروي فإذا هو مروي يرجع بهروي وسط ولا يرد بدل الخلع إلا بعيب فاحش فإن كان حلال عدم بین بينهما حتى تنسخ إحداهما بالأخرى قوله : وصحح الشمني رواية الأصل) قد علمت المنافاة الروايتين بما ذكره من التوفيق وهو مصرح به في الفتح فإنه ذكر أولاً أن المسألة مختلفة بين الصحابة ثم ساق النصوص من الطرفين ثم حقق ثم قال : وعلى هذا يظهر كون رواية الجامع أوجه. نعم يكون أخذ الزيادة خلاف الأولى والمنع محمول عل ما هو الأولى وطريق القرب إلى الله سبحانه قوله : (وذكر في غاية البيان أنه مطرد منعكس الخ) قال في النهر : لا يخفى أن الصلاحية المطلقة وكون مطلق المال المتقوم خالياً عن الكمية يصلح مهراً ممنوع فلذا منع المحققون انعكاسها كلية
His saying: (And what is valid as a mahr is valid as a consideration for khul') because what is valid as compensation for something of value is more worthy to be valid as compensation for something not of value. For the vulva is not of value at the time of exit (khul') but is of value at the time of entry (marriage). Thus the father is prevented from doing khul' of his minor daughter for her property, but he is allowed to marry his son for his property. And the khul' of a sick woman is executed from one-third. And it is permissible for a sick man to marry for mahr al-mithl from all his property. So khul' is valid for a described garment, or a measured or weighed item, like the mahr. Likewise for cultivation of her land, or riding her animal, or her service in a way that does not require seclusion with her or service of a foreigner, because these are valid as mahr. And the consideration is invalid if it were a garment or house like the mahr, and she must return the mahr. He indicated that this principle is not universally reversible, so one cannot say: what is not valid as mahr is not valid as a consideration in khul'. Because if he does khul' with her for what is in the belly of his slave-girl or his sheep, it is valid and he gets what is in their bellies, but it is not valid as mahr; rather mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Likewise for less than ten [dirhams]. Likewise for what is in her hand. Thus in al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir. And it is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that it [the principle] is regular and universally reversible, because the purpose of the regularity of the universal is that it be valuable property without complete ignorance, and less than ten is of this nature. And of the reversal of the universal is that it not be valuable property or that it have complete ignorance. And less than ten is valuable property without ignorance, so the objection does not arise against the regularity or its reversal. End. In al-Muhit: If she did khul' for a garment whose type was not specified, or for a house, then he gets the mahr, and for a slave she must pay the middle value. And if she did khul' for what she will earn in the year, or for what she will inherit of wealth, or that she marry him a woman and pay the mahr for him, the condition is invalid and she returns the mahr. And if she did khul' by his judgment or her judgment, it is valid; if she judged and the husband did not consent, he reverts to the mahr. And if he did khul' with her for one thousand until harvest, the term is confirmed. And if she said 'until the arrival of so-and-so' or 'his death', the wealth is due immediately. And if he did khul' with her for specified dirhams and found them bad, he returns to good dirhams. Likewise a garment as Herawi and it turned out to be Marwi, he returns to a medium Herawi. And the consideration in khul' is not returned except for a grave defect. If it was lawful... [text unclear] ...between them until one abrogates the other. His saying: 'And al-Shumnni authenticated the narration of the matn' you have known the conflict between the two narrations by what he mentioned of reconciliation, which is explicit in al-Fath, for he stated first that the issue is disputed among the Companions, then he presented the texts from both sides, then he investigated, then he said: Upon this, the narration of al-Jami' is more appropriate. Indeed, taking the increase is against the best, and prohibition is carried on what is best and the way of closeness to Allah. His saying: 'And it is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that it is regular and reversible...' He said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that absolute validity and that absolute valuable property devoid of quantity is valid as mahr is prevented, so the verifiers prevented its universality of reversal.

Commentary
This passage discusses the general principle that anything which can serve as a valid dower (mahr) can also serve as the consideration (badal) in a khul'. The reasoning is that the vulva (buda') is more valuable at the time of marriage (when it is compensated) than at the time of khul' (when it is being released). Therefore, if something is good enough to be the price of the vulva at its highest value, it is certainly suitable for its lower value. The text then gives examples: khul' is valid for a described garment, a measured or weighed item, for cultivation of her land, riding her animal, or her personal service (without seclusion). However, the principle is not fully reversible: there are things that are valid as khul' consideration but not as dower, such as something in the belly of a slave girl or sheep (unborn young), or an amount less than ten dirhams. These are valid in khul' but require mahr al-mithl in marriage. The passage then lists various rulings from al-Muhit about specific conditions in khul', such as unspecified terms, future earnings, or defective items. The commentator also discusses the reliability of narrations regarding taking more than the dower, favoring the narration that permits it absolutely.

Key Terms
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul‘): The consideration given by the wife to the husband in exchange for divorce.
مهر (mahr): Dower given by husband to wife at marriage, which is a model for valid consideration in khul'.

Ruling on Taking Extra in Khul' and Preferred Narration
Discusses the ruling on the wife giving extra in khul' and the strength of narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking extra in khul' and explain why it is makruh tanzihi rather than haram.

Core Idea
Taking extra in khul' is disliked, not forbidden, because the Quranic permission is absolute.

This lesson explores a nuanced ruling in khul' (divorce by redemption). The key question is whether a husband may take more than the mahr he gave. The Hanafi school, based on usul principles, distinguishes between impermissible and disliked. We will examine the conflicting narrations and the reasoning behind the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon (the husband taking extra in khul') and the initial ruling stated in the original text (makruh).
The act is the husband accepting more than the mahr from the wife in exchange for khul'.
2
Locate the conflicting narrations
Identify the two narrations within the Hanafi school: one in al-Asl (makruh) and one in al-Jami' al-Saghir (permissible). Understand that the difference is over the legal classification, not the validity of the khul'.
Both narrations agree that the khul' itself is valid; the dispute is only about the moral ruling on the extra amount.
3
Apply the usul principle
Analyze the Quranic text (2:229) which is absolute (mutlaq) in permitting khul' for any amount. According to Hanafi usul, a solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid) cannot restrict or specify a qat'i text. Therefore, the hadith prohibiting extra cannot make it haram.
The hadith 'As for the increase, no' is zanni in transmission and cannot override the qat'i Quranic text.
4
Note the tarjih (preference)
Review the tarjih: al-Shamni authenticated the original narration (makruh) based on other hadiths, while Fath al-Qadir found the permissive narration more appropriate. The mufta bihi is the original narration (makruh tanzihi).
The final fatwa relies on al-Shamni's authentication, making the ruling makruh tanzihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالأولى والمذكور في الأصل كراهة الزيادة على ما أعطاها وينبغي حمله على خلاف الأول كما ينبغي حمل الحديث عليه أيضاً وهو قوله أما الزيادة فلا لأن النص نفي الجناح مطلقاً فتقييده بخبر الواحد لا يجوز لما عرف في الأصول ولذا قال في فتح القدير: إن رواية الجامع أوجه وصحح الشمني رواية الأصل لأحاديث ذكرها.
Preferably, what is mentioned in the original is the dislike of the increase over what he gave her, and it should be interpreted contrary to the first, just as the hadith should also be interpreted accordingly, which is his saying: 'As for the increase, no' because the text negates sin absolutely, so restricting it with a solitary report is not permissible due to what is known in usul. That is why it is said in Fath al-Qadir: 'Indeed, the narration of al-Jami' is more appropriate, and al-Shamni authenticated the original narration due to hadiths he mentioned.'
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the ruling on the wife giving extra in khul' (divorce by redemption). The original text (al-asl) states that it is disliked (makruh) for the husband to take more than what he gave her (as mahr). This should be understood as being against the preferred (khilaf al-awla), not as prohibited. The hadith cited says 'As for the increase, no'—but since the Quranic text (2:229) permits khul' absolutely without restriction, limiting it with a solitary hadith is not valid according to Hanafi usul. Therefore, the stronger view is that taking extra is not haram but merely against the better. Al-Shamni authenticated the original narration (that it is makruh) based on other hadiths. The passage also notes that Fath al-Qadir prefers the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir (which allows extra), but the relied-upon position is the dislike.

Key Terms
الزيادة (al-ziyada): The excess amount the wife gives above what she received as mahr in khul'
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary hadith that is not mutawatir; cannot restrict a qat'i text

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is haram and the khul' is invalid
B) It is makruh tanzihi but the khul' is valid
C) It is permissible and recommended
D) It is fard to take exactly the mahr

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that taking extra in khul' is makruh tanzihi (disliked but valid) because the Quranic permission is absolute and cannot be restricted by solitary hadith.

The Principle of Mahr-Khul' Symmetry and Its Exceptions
Fiqh principle with proof (qiyas) and discussion of reversal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that anything valid as mahr is valid as badal khul', and identify the exceptions where the rule is not reversible.

Core Idea
What is valid as mahr is valid for khul', but the reverse is not absolute.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi rule in khul' (divorce by redemption): whatever is suitable as mahr (dower) is also suitable as the substitute (badal) paid by the wife. The reasoning is based on qiyas aulawi (a fortiori): if an item is acceptable compensation for a valuable right (the vulva at entry), it is even more suitable for a non-valuable right (exit). However, the rule is not fully reversible; some items invalid as mahr are valid as badal. We will explore the proof, examples, and the intra-madhab debate on reversibility.

Guided Path
1
State the rule and its reasoning
Identify the core principle: mahr-valid items are badal-valid. Understand the talil (legal reasoning) using qiyas aulawi: compensation for a valuable item (mahr) is a higher standard, so it automatically qualifies for a lower standard (badal).
The vulva is valuable at entry (marriage) but non-valuable at exit (khul').
2
List examples of valid badal from the text
Extract the examples given: a described garment, measured or weighed items, farming the wife's land, riding her animal, or her service (without seclusion). All are valid because they are valid as mahr.
Service by a stranger is also valid as badal, but not as mahr – an exception?
3
Identify the exceptions (non-reversibility)
Note that some items invalid as mahr are valid as badal: khul' for what is in the womb of a slave-girl, for less than ten dirhams, or for what is in her hand. These are valid badal but not valid mahr.
The rule 'what is invalid as mahr is invalid as badal' does not hold.
4
Analyse the Ghayat al-Bayan counterargument
Ghayat al-Bayan argues the rule is fully reversible, claiming that items like less than ten dirhams are actually valid as mahr (since they are valuable property without uncertainty). Then the rule would hold. Understand the disagreement.
The author dismisses this, showing that less than ten is not valid mahr in the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The operative ruling is that the principle is accepted but not fully reversible. The authentic view follows the exceptions, not the claim of full reversibility. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The excerpt from Ghayat al-Bayan is cited but not adopted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وما صلح مهر اصلح بدل الخلع لأن ما صلح عوضاً للمتقوم أولى أن يصلح عوضاً لغير المتقوم فإن البضع غير متقوم حالة الخروج ومتقوم حالة الدخول فمنع الأب خلع صغيرته على مالها وجاز له تزوج ولده بماله ونفذ خلع المريضة من الثلث، وجاز تزويج المريض بمهر المثل من جميع ماله فصح الخلع على ثوب موصوف أو مكيل أو موزون كالمهر، وكذا على زراعة أرضها أو ركوب دابتها وخدمتها على وجه لا يلزم خلوة بها أو خدمة أجنبي لأن هذه تجوز مهراً وبطل البدل فيه لو كان ثوباً أو داراً كالمهر ووجب عليها رد المهر. وأشار إلى أن هذا الأصل لا ينعكس كلياً فلا يصبح أن يقال ما لا يصلح مهراً لا يصلح بدلاً في الخلع لأنه لو خالعها على ما في بطن جاريتها أو غنمها صح وله ما في بطونها ولا يجوز مهراً بل يجب مهر المثل، وكذا على أقل من عشرة، وكذا على ما في يدها؛ كذا في التبيين وفتح القدير. وذكر في غاية البيان أنه مطرد منعكس كلياً لأن الغرض من طرد الكلي أن يكون مالاً متقوماً ليس فيه جهالة مستتمة وما دون العشرة بهذه المثابة، ومن عكس الكلي أن لا يكون مالاً متقوماً أو أن يكون فيه جهالة مستتمة وما دون العشرة مال متقوم ليس فيه جهالة فلا يرد السؤال لا على الطرد الكلي ولا على عكسه .اهـ.
He said: 'And whatever is suitable as mahr is suitable as the substitute for khul', because what is suitable as compensation for a valuable item is more suitable to be compensation for a non-valuable item. For the vulva is non-valuable at the time of exit and valuable at the time of entry. So the father is prevented from having his minor daughter do khul' with her property, but he is permitted to marry his son with his property. And the khul' of a sick woman is executed from one-third. And a sick man's marriage for mahr al-mithl from all his property is permitted. So khul' is valid for a described garment, or measured, or weighed, like mahr. Similarly, for farming her land, riding her animal, or her service in a way that does not require seclusion with her or the service of a stranger, because these are permissible as mahr. But the substitute is invalid if it is a garment or house, like mahr, and she must return the mahr. And he indicated that this principle is not reversible entirely, so it cannot be said whatever is not suitable as mahr is not suitable as substitute in khul', because if he made khul' with her on what is in the womb of his slave-girl or his sheep, it is valid and he gets what is in their wombs, and that is not valid as mahr; rather, mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Likewise, on less than ten [dirhams], and likewise on what is in her hand. Thus in al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir. And it is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that it is universal and reversible entirely, because the purpose of the positive universality is that it be valuable property without complete uncertainty, and less than ten is of this nature. And the purpose of the converse is that it be not valuable property or that it have complete uncertainty, and less than ten is valuable property without uncertainty, so the objection does not apply to either the positive universality or its converse. End.'
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and a discussion of a legal principle. It establishes that anything valid as mahr (dower) is valid as the substitute (badal) in khul'. The reasoning (talil) is that mahr is compensation for the vulva (buda') which becomes valuable through marriage, whereas in khul', the vulba is being exited and is non-valuable; so if something is suitable as compensation for a valuable item, it is more suitable for a non-valuable one (qiyas aulawi). Examples: khul' for a described garment, measured or weighed items, farming usufruct, or service are valid because they are valid as mahr. However, the rule is not fully reversible: some things invalid as mahr are valid as badal, e.g., khul' for what is in the womb of a slave-girl or for less than ten dirhams. Ghayat al-Bayan argues for complete reversibility, but the author notes that the correct view is that the rule is not reversible in every case. The passage also includes an intra-madhab point: the father cannot give his minor daughter in khul' on her property (because she owns it, but he has no authority over her vaguba? Actually, the text says 'mana' al-abu khula saghiratihi 'ala maliha' meaning the father is prohibited from making khul' for his minor daughter with her property, but he can marry her son to her? The translation needs care. This passage is dense with furoo' (branches).

Key Terms
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The consideration paid by the wife (or a third party) to exit the marriage in khul' divorce
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): Mahr equivalent to that of women of similar status; used when no mahr is specified or invalid

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A described garment
B) Farming the wife's land
C) What is in the womb of a slave-girl
D) A specific house

Key Takeaway
The rule that mahr-valid items are khul'-valid is a guiding principle, but it is not absolute; exceptions exist where non-mahr items are permissible as badal.

Khul' with Unspecified or Future Substitutes
Legal rulings on validity of khul' substitute based on specification and ownership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which substitutes in khul' are valid or invalid based on certainty and ownership, and state the resulting ruling for each case.

Core Idea
A khul' substitute must be known and owned at the time; otherwise the khul' is invalid and the husband gets the mahr.

In this lesson, we examine several cases from al-Muhit that test the boundaries of a valid substitute in khul'. The rulings illustrate the Hanafi requirement that the badal be specified and currently owned. When the substitute is uncertain, future, or conditional, the khul' fails and the original mahr is owed. Understanding these boundaries helps avoid common errors in drafting khul' agreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of substitute
Read the case and determine what the wife offers as the substitute (e.g., unspecified garment, future earnings, judgment, deferred payment).
2
Check for certainty and ownership
Is the substitute known and currently owned by the wife? If it is uncertain or future, it is invalid.
Future earnings and inheritance are not owned yet.
3
Apply the ruling
If valid, the substitute is owed; if invalid, the khul' is void and the husband gets the mahr.
4
Distinguish deferred payment
For deferred payment, if the time is known (e.g., harvest), it is valid; if the time is unknown (e.g., arrival of someone), it is immediate.
Unknown time causes gharar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : لو اختلعت على ثوب لم يتبين جنسه أو على دار فله المهر وفي العبد يلزمها الوسط، ولو اختلعت على ما تكتسبه العام أو على ما ترثه من المال أو على أن تزوجه امرأة وتمهرها عنه فالشرط باطل وترد المهر، ولو اختلعت بحكمه أو بحكمها صح فإن حكمت ولم يرض الزوج رجع بالمهر، ولو خلعها على ألف إلى الحصاد ثبت الأجل، ولو قالت إلى قدوم فلان أو موته وجب المال حالاً، ولو خالعها على دراهم معينة فوجدها ستوقة يرجع بالجياد، وكذلك الثوب على أنه هروي فإذا هو مروي يرجع بهروي وسط ولا يرد بدل الخلع إلا بعيب فاحش فإن كان حلال الدم أو اليد فأمضى عنده رجع عليها بقيمته عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما بنقصان قيمته لأن كونه حلال الدم بمنزلة الاستحقاق عنده وعندهما بمنزلة النقصان ولو اختلعت على عبد بعينه فمات في يدها أو استحق فعليها قيمته ، فإن ظهر أنه كان ميتاً وقت الانخلاع فله مهرها . ولو خلعها على حيوان ثم صالحته على دراهم أو مكيل أو موزون جاز يداً بيد. ولو خالعها على عبد ومهرها ألفا ثم زادها ألفاً ثم استحق العبد رجع عليها بألف وبنصف قيمة العبد لأن المرأة بذلت العبد بإزاء البضع وألف درهم فانقسم العبد عليهما نصفين: نصفه بدل الخلع ونصفه بيعاً بالألف، والمبيع متى استحق ثمنه رجع بثمنه وبدل الخلع متى استحق تجب قيمته فيرجع بنصف قيمة العبد ولو خلع امرأتيه على عبد قسمت قيمته على مسميهما في العقد لأنه قيمة بضعيهما لا على مهر مثليهما لأن الزيادة على المسمى مكروهة في الخلع والزيادة في بدل الخلع باطلة لأنها زادت بعد هلاك المعقود عليه فصار كما لو زاد في بدل الصلح عن دم العمد فإنها لا تصح .اهـ.
And in al-Muhit: If she made khul' on a garment whose type was not specified, or on a house, then he gets the mahr. And regarding the slave, she must pay the average. If she made khul' on what she will earn this year, or on what she will inherit from the money, or on that she marries a woman to him and gives her mahr on his behalf, the condition is void and she returns the mahr. If she made khul' on his judgment or her judgment, it is valid. If she judged and the husband did not consent, he gets the mahr. If he divorced her by khul' for a thousand until the harvest, the term is valid. If she said 'until the arrival of so-and-so' or 'his death', the money is due immediately. If she made khul' on specific dirhams and found them to be debased, he gets good ones. Similarly, a garment on condition it is Harawi and it turned out to be Marwi, he gets a medium Harawi. And the substitute for khul' is not returned except for a serious defect. If it had permissible blood or a hand, and he approved, then according to Abu Hanifa she must pay its value; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) she pays the reduction in value. Because its being permissible blood is like entitlement according to him, and according to them like a reduction. If she made khul' on a specific slave and he died in her hand or is claimed, she must pay his value. If it appears he was dead at the time of khul', he gets her mahr. If he made khul' on an animal, then later settled with dirhams or measured or weighed items, it is valid hand-to-hand. If he made khul' on a slave and her mahr is a thousand, then he increased her a thousand, then the slave is claimed, he gets from her a thousand and half the value of the slave. Because the woman gave the slave in exchange for the vulva and a thousand dirhams, so the slave is divided between them into two halves: half is badal khul' and half is a sale for the thousand. When a sold item is claimed, its price is returned; when badal khul' is claimed, its value is due. So he gets half the value of the slave. If he made khul' with his two wives on one slave, its value is divided according to what they named in the contract, because it is the value of their vulvae, not according to the mithl of their mahr, because increase over the named amount is disliked in khul', and increase in badal khul' is void because she increased after the destruction of the subject matter, so it becomes like if one increased in the blood-money settlement for intentional killing, it is not valid. End.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a collection of ruling statements from al-Muhit, providing numerous specific cases regarding the validity and consequences of badal khul'. The rulings cover: (1) If the substitute is unspecified in type or is a house, the husband gets the mahr (the khul' is invalid). (2) Khul' on future earnings or inheritance is invalid, condition void, she returns mahr. (3) Khul' on her own or his judgment is valid; if she judges and he doesn't accept, he gets mahr. (4) Deferred payment to a known time is valid; to an unknown event is immediate. (5) Defective substitute: if the defect is serious, it is returned; if the defect is temporary (e.g., halal blood or severed hand), the husband can choose to accept and get compensation according to the three imams. (6) If the slave was dead at contract, khul' invalid, she returns mahr. (7) Settlement after khul' (e.g., from animal to cash) is valid spot. (8) Complex case: khul' on a slave while mahr was also involved; if the slave is claimed, the husband recovers half its value and the additional thousand. (9) Khul' with two wives on a single slave: the value is split by the named amounts, not by their mahr values. These are all practical branches (furu') that illustrate the rules of khul' substitute.

Key Terms
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The substitute given by the wife in return for divorce
غرر (gharar): Uncertainty that invalidates a contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a wife makes khul' on her judgment (bi hukmiha) and she judges that she pays 500 dirhams, but the husband does not consent, what is the ruling?
A) The khul' is void and she pays nothing
B) The khul' is valid and she pays 500 dirhams
C) The husband gets the mahr
D) The husband must consent or the khul' is invalid

Key Takeaway
The substitute in khul' must be known and possessed at the time; otherwise, the khul' is invalid and the husband receives the mahr.

Defects in Khul' Substitute and Compensation
Rulings on defective khul' substitutes and intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between defects that allow return of the substitute and defects that only require compensation, and state the Hanafi positions on compensation for remissible defects.

Core Idea
Only a serious defect allows returning the khul' substitute; for temporary defects, compensation is the remedy, with a dispute on the amount.

When the substitute in khul' is defective, the husband has options. This lesson clarifies the types of defects and the remedies. A key distinction is between a serious defect (ayb fahish) that warrants returning the item, and a remissible defect (like halal blood) where the husband can keep it and claim compensation. The Hanafi masters differ on how to calculate that compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of defect
Is it a quality defect (e.g., wrong type of garment) or a physical defect?
2
Apply rule for quality defects
If the substitute is of lower quality than specified, the husband gets the specified quality or its equivalent value.
E.g., debased coins -> good coins; wrong type garment -> medium of specified type.
3
Distinguish physical defects
If the defect is serious (fahish), the husband may return the substitute. If it is not serious, he may accept and claim compensation.
Examples of fahish: missing limb, permanent defect. Examples of non-fahish: temporary stain, halal blood.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf on remissible defects
For defects like halal blood, Abu Hanifa holds she pays full value; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say she pays the reduction in value.
The fatwa is on the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Source Text

Destruction, Claims, and Multiple Wives in Khul'
Rulings on substitute perishing, being claimed, and apportionment among multiple wives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the liability when the substitute perishes or is claimed, and calculate the distribution when a single substitute covers multiple obligations.

Core Idea
If the substitute is destroyed or claimed, the wife is liable for its value; when a substitute serves multiple purposes, it is divided proportionally.

This lesson tackles scenarios where the khul' substitute is no longer available—either because it perished, was claimed by a third party, or was already dead. It also addresses the unique situation where a single slave is used as substitute for two wives. The rulings demonstrate how Hanafi fiqh handles liability and apportionment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the status of the substitute
Is the substitute still in existence? Was it destroyed, claimed, or dead at contract?
2
Apply liability rules
If it perishes or is claimed after contract, she pays its value. If it was dead at contract, the khul' is void and he gets mahr.
She is liable for the substitute once contracted.
3
Analyze combined transactions
If the substitute is combined with a separate transaction (e.g., mahr increase), apportion the value proportionally.
The slave is divided half for khul', half for sale.
4
Handle multiple wives
If one substitute is given for two wives, split its value according to the amounts named in each contract, not by mahr values.
Reason: increase over named amount is disliked and void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

According to the passage, if a wife makes khul' on a specific slave and it is later discovered that the slave was dead at the time of the contract, what is the ruling?
A) She must pay the value of the slave
B) The khul' is valid and she owes the value
C) The husband gets the mahr
D) The khul' is void and no money changes hands

Key Takeaway
The wife is liable for the value if the specific substitute is destroyed or claimed; multiple obligations are apportioned according to the agreed amounts.

intermediate
6 min
Khul' with Ambiguous Substitute for Two Wives
Provides rulings on khul' with ambiguous substitute from al-Tatarkhaniyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a husband addresses ambiguous khul' to his two wives with different substitutes and explain why the divorce takes effect without payment.

Core Idea
Ambiguous allocation of khul' substitute between two wives makes the substitute void; divorce occurs without payment.

In al-Tatarkhaniyya, a specific scenario is addressed: a husband says to his two wives, 'One of you is divorced by a thousand dirhams, and the other by a hundred dinars,' and both accept. The ruling clarifies that the divorce takes effect without any substitute being paid. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that khul' is broader than sale, especially when the substitute is not properly allocated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The husband addresses both wives simultaneously with different substitutes but does not specify which wife receives which substitute.
This is a case of ambiguous designation.
2
Determine the ruling
Both wives are divorced, and no substitute is due because the allocation is ambiguous.
The divorce is valid despite the ambiguity.
3
Understand the reason
Because the substitute is not specifically allocated to each wife, it becomes void; the divorce still takes effect.
4
Note the exception on death
If the husband dies after acceptance, each wife pays half of the amount and no inheritance passes between them.
This is from the narration of Ibn Sama'a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التتارخانية : إذا قال لامرأتيه إحداكما طالق بألف درهم والأخرى بمائة دينار فقبلتا طلقتا بغير شيء. وروى ابن سماعة عن محمد : إذا قال لامرأتيه إحداكما طالق بألف فقبلتا ومات فعلى كل واحدة منهما خمسمائة ولا ميراث اهـ. وفي القنية : اختلعت نفسها بالمهر بشرط أن الزوج يعطيها كذا مناً من الأرز الأبيض وخالعها به ينبغي أي يصح ولا يشترط بيان مكان الإيفاء عند أبي حنيفة لأن الخلع أوسع من البيع ففي بت : خالعها على ثوب بشرط أن تسلم إليه الثوب فقبلت فهلك الثوب قبل التسليم لم تبن لأنه يجعل نفس التسليم شرطاً . مخ: وهبت مهرها لأخيها فأخذ أخوها منه المهر قبالة ثم اختلعت نفسها منه بشرط أن تسلم له القبالة غداً فقبل ولم تسلم إليه القبالة غداً لا تحرم. ولو اختلعت بشرط الصك أو قالت بشرط أن يرد عليها أقمشتها فقيل لا تحرم ويشترط كتابة الصك ورد الأقمشة في المجلس خلعتك على عبدي وقف على قبولها ولم يجب شيء. خلعتك بمالي عليك من الدين وقبلت ينبغي أن يقع الطلاق ولا يجب شيء ويبطل الدين. ادعت مهرها على زوجها فأنكره ثم اختلعت نفسها بمهرها وقبل ثم تبين بالشهود أنها كان امرأته قبل الخلع فليس له شيء ولو اختلعت على عبد ثم تبين أنه عبد الزوج ولا ذلك إلا بالتصادق فينبغي أن لا يلزمها شيء لأن ما هو بدل الخلع يسلم له كما لو علم أنه عبده. وسئل لو كان الخلع على دراهم أو دنانير ثم تبين أنها للزوج لم يجب شيء .اهـ.
And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: If a man says to his two wives: 'One of you is divorced by a thousand dirhams, and the other by a hundred dinars,' and they both accept, they are divorced without anything. And Ibn Sama'a narrated from Muhammad: If he said to his two wives: 'One of you is divorced by a thousand,' and they both accept and he dies, then each one is liable for five hundred, and no inheritance. End. And in al-Qunyah: She made khul' of herself for the mahr on condition that the husband give her so many manns of white rice, and he made khul' with that – it should be considered valid, and it is not required to specify the place of fulfillment according to Abu Hanifa because khul' is wider than sale. So in the text: He made khul' with her on a garment on condition that she hand over the garment to him, she accepted, then the garment perished before delivery – she does not become unlawful (i.e., the divorce does not take effect). Because he made the delivery itself a condition. Contrast: She gifted her mahr to her brother, then her brother took a receipt from him for the mahr, then she made khul' of herself from him on condition that she hand over the receipt to him tomorrow, he accepted, and she did not hand over the receipt tomorrow – she does not become forbidden. If she made khul' on condition of a document, or said on condition that he return her clothes, it is said she does not become forbidden, and it is required that the document be written and the clothes be returned in the sitting. 'I made khul' with you on my slave' – pending her acceptance – nothing is due. 'I made khul' with you for the debt you owe me,' and she accepted – it is appropriate that the divorce occurs and nothing is due, and the debt is void. She claimed her mahr from her husband, he denied it, then she made khul' of herself with her mahr and he accepted, then it was proven by witnesses that she was his wife before the khul' – he gets nothing. If she made khul' on a slave and then it appeared that the slave was the husband's – and that is only known through mutual confirmation – it is appropriate that nothing be required of her, because what is the substitute for khul' is given to her just as if he knew it was his slave. He was asked: If the khul' is on dirhams or dinars, and then it appears that they belong to the husband, nothing is due. End.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage presents specific rulings from al-Tatarkhaniyya and al-Qunyah. The first part from Tatarkhaniyya addresses khul' for two wives with an ambiguous designation: if the husband says 'one of you is divorced for a thousand, the other for a hundred', and both accept, they are divorced without paying anything because the substitute is not properly allocated. A narration from Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad states that if both accept a single amount and the husband dies, each pays half and no inheritance (i.e., the divorce is effective but they do not inherit from each other). The second part from al-Qunyah deals with conditional khul': (1) If she makes khul' on condition that the husband give her rice, without specifying the place of delivery, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa because khul' is broader than sale (which would require specification). (2) If she makes khul' on a garment conditional on her handing it over, and it perishes before delivery, the divorce does not occur. (3) If she makes khul' conditional on handing over a receipt (from her brother's transaction), and she fails, the divorce does not occur. (4) If she makes khul' conditional on writing a document or returning clothes, it is said the divorce does not occur unless the condition is fulfilled in the sitting. (5) If she says 'I made khul' on my slave' pending acceptance, no obligation. (6) If she makes khul' for a debt she owes, divorce occurs and the debt is voided. (7) If she claims mahr, husband denies, then she makes khul' for that mahr, and later witnesses prove she was his wife before, the husband gets nothing. (8) If she makes khul' on a slave that turns out to be the husband's, nothing is due if they both confirm it. (9) If the substitute is dirhams that belong to the husband, nothing is due. These rulings illustrate the importance of certainty and delivery of the substitute in khul'.

Key Terms
الخُلع أوسع من البيع (al-khulu' awsa' min al-bay'): Khul' is more flexible than sale; therefore, its conditions regarding unknown elements are more lenient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from Tatarkhaniyya, if a husband says to his two wives, 'One of you is divorced by a thousand dirhams and the other by a hundred dinars,' and they both accept, what is the ruling?
A) Both are divorced and each owes the specified amount
B) The divorce does not take place due to ambiguity
C) Both are divorced without owing anything
D) The wife who is designated later must pay

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, ambiguous designation of substitute in khul' does not prevent divorce; the substitute becomes void.

Conditional Khul': Validity and Effects of Conditions
Provides detailed scenarios on conditional khul' from al-Qunyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditions that affect the validity of khul' and those that do not, and apply the principle that khul' is wider than sale.

Core Idea
Conditions in khul' are treated leniently; some conditions do not invalidate the divorce but may affect the substitute.

Al-Qunyah presents numerous scenarios of conditional khul'. This lesson explores how conditions like delivery of goods, timing, or document writing affect the validity of the divorce. The key principle is that khul' is broader than sale, so unspecified place of delivery is acceptable, but conditions that are integral to the transaction must be fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition in each scenario
For each case in al-Qunyah, determine what condition is placed on the khul' (e.g., delivery of rice, handing over a receipt, writing a document).
2
Determine if the condition is integral or ancillary
Integral conditions directly affect the substitute or its delivery; ancillary conditions are separate promises.
The text distinguishes based on the nature of the condition.
3
Apply the rule for integral conditions
If the condition is integral and not fulfilled, the divorce does not take effect.
Example: the garment perishes before delivery.
4
Apply the rule for ancillary conditions
If the condition is not integral, failure does not prevent divorce (e.g., khul' for a debt).

Rulings on Pledge, Delegation, and Agency in Khul'
Ruling statements from al-Khaniyya and al-Mujtaba on khul'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings from al-Khaniyya and al-Mujtaba regarding pledge, delegation, and agency in khul'.

Core Idea
Khul' substitute may be secured by pledge; delegation to husband is valid without his presence; one person may act for both parties.

This lesson presents three distinct rulings from later Hanafi compilations (al-Khaniyya and al-Mujtaba) that clarify the flexibility of the khul' contract. These rulings affirm that the khul' transaction can be secured through pledge or guarantee, can be delegated by the wife to her husband or a slave to his master, and can involve a single agent representing both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on securing the khul' substitute
The passage states that giving a pledge (rahn) or guarantee (kafala) for the substitute is valid. This treats the substitute as a debt that can be collateralized.
2
Identify the ruling on delegation of khul'
The passage states that if a woman delegates khul' to her husband, or a slave to his master, and the husband/master performs the khul' without the delegator's presence, it is valid. Delegation does not require the delegator's presence at execution.
3
Identify the ruling on agency from both sides
The passage states that one person can act as agent for both the husband and wife in the khul' contract. This is permissible because khul' is akin to a sale where agency for both is allowed.
The passage also mentions a clarification about mutual confirmation for ownership of the substitute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية : ويجوز الرهن والكفالة ببدل الخلع. وفي المجتبى : فوضت الخلع إلى زوجها أو العبد إلى المولى ففعل بغير حضرتهما جاز والواحد يتولى الخلع من الجانبين. وفي عتاق الأصل الواحد يكون وكيلاً من الجانبين في (ولا ذلك إلا بالتصادق كذا في النسخ ولكن سيعيد العبارة قريباً بلفظ «ولا يعلم ذلك إلا بالتصادق وتقدم قبل ورقة ونصف بلفظ ثم تبين أنه عبد الزوج بتصادقهما» قوله : (والواحد يتولى
And in al-Khaniyya: Pledge and guarantee are valid for the substitute of khul'. And in al-Mujtaba: She delegated the khul' to her husband, or the slave to the master, and he did it without their presence – it is valid. One person can handle khul' from both sides. And in 'Itaq al-Asl: One person can be agent from both sides... 'And that is only through mutual confirmation' – so in the copies, but he will soon repeat the phrase as 'and it is not known except through mutual confirmation', and earlier half a leaf ago he said 'then it appears it is the husband's slave through their mutual confirmation.' He said: 'One person handles'...
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage provides additional rulings from al-Khaniyya and al-Mujtaba (later Hanafi collections). It states that it is valid to give a pledge (rahn) or guarantee (kafala) for the substitute due in khul'. This means the debt from khul' can be secured. From al-Mujtaba: if a woman delegates the khul' to her husband (i.e., authorizes him to pronounce it), or if a slave delegates to his master, and the husband/master performs the khul' without the delegator's presence, it is valid. Also, one person can act as agent for both the husband and wife in a khul' transaction. The last part from 'Itaq al-Asl mentions that one person can act as agent from both sides, and clarifies a phrase about the substitute being the husband's slave only being known through mutual confirmation. This is a reference to an earlier ruling about the substitute turning out to belong to the husband.

Key Terms
الرهن والكفالة ببدل الخلع (al-rahn wa al-kafala bi-badal al-khul'): The wife may offer a pledge or a guarantor for the payment of the substitute in khul'
تولى الخلع من الجانبين (tawalla al-khul' min al-janibayn): One person acts as agent for both the husband and wife in the khul' contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows securing the khul' substitute via pledge, delegation of khul' to the husband/master even in absentia, and a single agent representing both parties.

Khul' with a Specific Slave: Liability for Loss or Defect
Rulings on khul' with a specific slave when it dies, is taken, or is found dead.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on khul' with a specific slave and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on liability when the slave perishes or is taken.

Core Idea
In khul' with a specific slave, if it perishes, the wife pays full value (Abu Hanifa) or decrease (Sahibayn); the ruling depends on analogy to entitlement vs. defect.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the nuances of khul' when the consideration is a specified slave. It addresses what happens if the slave dies, is claimed by another, or is found dead at the time of contract. These rulings hinge on the valuation of the slave and the distinction between full liability and decrease in value, revealing a key intra-Hanafi methodological difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The passage discusses khul' with a specific slave as consideration. Identify the different outcomes: slave dies in wife's hand, slave is taken by a third party (istihqaq), slave found dead at contract time, and a scenario with additional payment.
Focus on the first two as they involve ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that if the slave dies or is taken, the wife must pay its full value. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that she pays only the decrease in value. Determine the basis for each view.
The key phrase: 'because its being permissible of blood is like entitlement (istihqaq) according to him, and according to them like decrease (nuqsan).'
3
Trace the analogical reasoning
Abu Hanifa analogizes the death/taking to istihqaq (complete loss of title), requiring full value. The Sahibayn analogize it to a defect (partial loss), requiring only the decrease. Understand how each treats the same event differently.
This is a talil (reasoning) passage.
4
Examine the 'found dead' scenario
If the slave was dead at the time of khul', the husband does not take the slave's value; instead, he gets the wife's mahr (dower). This is because the consideration was void from the start.
Contrast with the previous scenario where the slave was alive at contract and died later.
5
Apply the mixed payment scenario
When the husband increases the wife's mahr and the slave is later taken, the slave is split: half for khul' and half as sale. The husband returns the increase and half the slave's value.
This shows the combined nature of the transaction: part divorce compensation, part sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدم أو اليد فأمضى عنده رجع عليها بقيمته عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما بنقصان قيمته لأن كونه حلال الدم بمنزلة الاستحقاق عنده وعندهما بمنزلة النقصان ولو اختلعت على عبد بعينه فمات في يدها أو استحق فعليها قيمته ، فإن ظهر أنه كان ميتاً وقت الانخلاع فله مهرها . ولو خلعها على حيوان ثم صالحته على دراهم أو مكيل أو موزون جاز يداً بيد. ولو خالعها على عبد ومهرها ألفا ثم زادها ألفاً ثم استحق العبد رجع عليها بألف وبنصف قيمة العبد لأن المرأة بذلت العبد بإزاء البضع وألف درهم فانقسم العبد عليهما نصفين: نصفه بدل الخلع ونصفه بيعاً بالألف، والمبيع متى استحق ثمنه رجع بثمنه وبدل الخلع متى استحق تجب قيمته فيرجع بنصف قيمة العبد
...blood or hand, he ruled accordingly, she returns to him its value according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the decrease in its value because its being permissible of blood is like entitlement according to him, and according to them like decrease. And if she khala' with a specific slave, and it died in her hand or was taken by another, upon her is its value. Then if it appeared that it was dead at the time of khul', then he gets her mahr. And if he khala' her with an animal, then she reconciled with him for dirhams or measurable or weighable, it is permissible hand-to-hand. And if he khala' her with a slave, and her mahr was one thousand, then he increased her by one thousand, then the slave was taken, he returns to her one thousand and half the value of the slave, because the woman gave the slave in exchange for the sexual act and one thousand dirhams, so the slave is divided between the two halves: half is the consideration for khul' and half is a sale for one thousand, and when the sold item is taken, he returns its price, and when the consideration for khul' is taken, its value is due, so he returns half the value of the slave.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage addresses multiple scenarios in khul' involving a specified slave. The first part mentions a ruling regarding blood money or limb, where if the husband rules in a certain way, she must pay the value according to Abu Hanifa, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say she pays the decrease in value because they treat the permissibility of blood as equivalent to entitlement (istihaqq) in decreasing value. Then it rules that if a woman performs khul' with a specific slave and the slave dies in her possession or is taken by someone else (e.g., it was claimed by another), she must pay its value to the husband. If it is discovered that the slave was already dead at the time of khul', then the husband gets her mahr (dower) instead. Next, if the khul' was made with an animal and then she agrees to pay dirhams or other fungible items, it is valid as a hand-to-hand transaction. Finally, if khul' is made with a slave and the wife's mahr was 1000, and the husband increases her mahr by another 1000, then the slave is later taken back (e.g., found to belong to someone else), the husband returns the 1000 increase and half the value of the slave. The reasoning: the woman gave the slave in exchange for the marital right and 1000 dirhams, so the slave is split into two halves: half is the khul' consideration, half is a sale for the 1000. If the sold part is taken, he returns its price; if the khul' consideration is taken, its value is due. So he returns half the slave's value.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce at the wife's request with compensation paid to the husband.
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The consideration or compensation given by the wife in exchange for her release from marriage.
الاستحقاق (al-istihqaq): The taking of property by a rightful claimant (e.g., the slave is claimed by another).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman performs khul' with a specific slave, and the slave dies in her hand before delivery, what is she liable for according to Abu Hanifa?
A) She pays nothing because the slave was not delivered.
B) She pays the full value of the slave.
C) She pays the decrease in the slave's value from the time of contract to death.
D) She pays half the value of the slave.

Key Takeaway
In khul' with a specified slave, the wife's liability for loss or taking depends on an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: full value (Abu Hanifa) vs. decrease (Sahibayn), based on whether the event is analogized to complete loss or partial defect.
