Khul' with Two Wives: Division of Consideration and Invalid Allocation
Rulings on khul' with two wives and division of consideration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing the consideration when a man divorces both wives with a single object, and explain why an invalid allocation of amounts results in no payment.

Core Idea
In khul', the consideration is divided according to what is named; invalid allocation yields no payment.

This lesson examines two key rulings from the Hanafi school regarding khul' when two wives are involved. The first deals with a khul' in exchange for a single slave, where the value is divided according to the amounts specified in the contract. The second considers a scenario where a husband says to his two wives 'one of you is divorced for a specific amount' and both accept, leading to a situation where the allocation is invalid and the wives are divorced without payment. These rulings illustrate the importance of clear consideration in khul' and the consequences of ambiguity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case of khul' with two wives using a single slave.
The husband divorces both wives in exchange for one slave. The value of the slave must be divided between the two wives.
2
Analyze the division of the value.
The value is divided according to the amounts named in the contract, not according to the typical mahr of the wives. Because the value represents the price of their sexual rights (bada').
Increase over the named amount is disliked and void if done after the contract.
3
Understand the principle behind the division.
Any increase over the named consideration after the contract is void, analogous to increasing blood money after settlement.
4
Examine the TatarKhaniyya narration.
If the husband says 'One of you is divorced for 1000 dirhams and the other for 100 dinars' and both accept, the allocation is ambiguous, so the divorce takes effect but no consideration is due.
5
Examine the Ibn Sama'a narration.
If the husband says 'One of you is divorced for 1000' (unspecified currency) and both accept, then upon his death, each wife pays 500 and there is no inheritance between them.
The amount is divided equally due to lack of allocation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو خلع امرأتيه على عبد قسمت قيمته على مسميهما في العقد لأنه قيمة بضعيهما لا على مهر مثليهما لأن الزيادة على المسمى مكروهة في الخلع والزيادة في بدل الخلع باطلة لأنها زادت بعد هلاك المعقود عليه فصار كما لو زاد في بدل الصلح عن دم العمد فإنها لا تصح .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : إذا قال لامرأتيه إحداكما طالق بألف درهم والأخرى بمائة دينار فقبلتا طلقتا بغير شيء. وروى ابن سماعة عن محمد : إذا قال لامرأتيه إحداكما طالق بألف فقبلتا ومات فعلى كل واحدة منهما خمسمائة ولا ميراث اهـ. وفي القنية : اختلعت نفسها بالمهر بشرط أن الزوج يعطيها كذا مناً من الأرز الأبيض وخالعها به ينبغي أي يصح ولا يشترط بيان مكان الإيفاء عند أبي حنيفة لأن الخلع أوسع من البيع ففي بت : خالعها على ثوب بشرط أن تسلم إليه الثوب فقبلت فهلك الثوب قبل التسليم لم تبن لأنه يجعل نفس التسليم شرطاً . مخ: وهبت مهرها لأخيها فأخذ أخوها منه المهر قبالة ثم اختلعت نفسها منه بشرط أن تسلم له القبالة غداً فقبل ولم تسلم إليه القبالة غداً لا تحرم. ولو اختلعت بشرط الصك أو قالت بشرط أن يرد عليها أقمشتها فقيل لا تحرم ويشترط كتابة الصك ورد الأقمشة في المجلس خلعتك على عبدي وقف على قبولها ولم يجب شيء. خلعتك بمالي عليك من الدين وقبلت ينبغي أن يقع الطلاق ولا يجب شيء ويبطل الدين. ادعت مهرها على زوجها فأنكره ثم اختلعت نفسها بمهرها وقبل ثم تبين بالشهود أنها كان امرأته قبل الخلع فليس له شيء ولو اختلعت على عبد ثم تبين أنه عبد الزوج ولا ذلك إلا بالتصادق فينبغي أن لا يلزمها شيء لأن ما هو بدل الخلع يسلم له كما لو علم أنه عبده. وسئل لو كان الخلع على دراهم أو دنانير ثم تبين أنها للزوج لم يجب شيء .اهـ. وفي الخانية : ويجوز الرهن والكفالة ببدل الخلع. وفي المجتبى : فوضت الخلع إلى زوجها أو العبد إلى المولى ففعل بغير حضرتهما جاز والواحد يتولى الخلع من الجانبين.
And if he khala' his two wives with a slave, its value is divided according to the names given in the contract because it is the value of their sexual rights, not according to their dowers of the like, because increase over what is named is disliked in khul', and increase in the consideration for khul' is void because it increased after destruction of the object of contract, so it is like if one increased in the consideration for blood money of intentional killing, it is not valid. End quote. In al-TatarKhaniyya: If he said to his two wives, 'One of you is divorced for one thousand dirhams and the other for one hundred dinars,' and they accepted, they are divorced for nothing. And Ibn Sama'a narrated from Muhammad: If he said to his two wives, 'One of you is divorced for one thousand,' and they accepted and he dies, upon each is five hundred, and no inheritance. End quote. In al-Quniya: She khala' herself for the mahr on condition that the husband gives her so many mans of white rice, and he khala' her with it, it is proper, i.e., valid, and specification of place of delivery is not required according to Abu Hanifa because khul' is broader than sale. In al-Bazz: He khala' her for a garment on condition that she deliver the garment to him, she accepted, then the garment perished before delivery, she does not become separate because he made the delivery itself a condition. Different: She gifted her mahr to her brother, then her brother took from him the mahr as a loan or bond, then she khala' herself from him on condition that she deliver the bond to him tomorrow, he accepted, and she did not deliver the bond tomorrow, she does not become unlawful. And if she khala' with a condition of a document or she said with condition that he return her cloths, it is said she does not become unlawful, and writing the document and returning the cloths in the session is required. 'I khala' you for my slave that is a waqf on her acceptance, and nothing is due.' 'I khala' you for what is due to me from you of debt, and she accepted, it is proper that divorce occurs and nothing is due, and the debt is void. She claimed her mahr from her husband, he denied it, then she khala' herself for her mahr and he accepted, then it became clear by witnesses that she was his wife before the khul', so he has nothing. And if she khala' for a slave, then it became clear that it was the husband's slave, and that is only known by mutual confession, then it is proper that nothing is due from her because what is the consideration for khul' yields to him as if he knew it was his slave. And he was asked: If the khul' was for dirhams or dinars, then it became clear that they were the husband's, nothing is due. End quote. In al-Khaniyya: Pledge and guarantee for the consideration of khul' are valid. In al-Mujtaba: She delegated the khul' to her husband or the slave to the master, and he did it without their presence, it is valid, and one person can conduct the khul' on both sides.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage consolidates multiple rulings from various Hanafi texts on khul'. First, if a man divorces both his wives in return for a single slave, the value of the slave is divided according to the amounts specified in the contract for each wife, not according to their typical mahr, because any increase over what is named is disliked in khul' and an increase after the destruction of the subject matter is void. Then, from al-TatarKhaniyya: if a man says to his two wives 'one of you is divorced for 1000 dirhams and the other for 100 dinars' and they both accept, they are both divorced without any payment because the allocation is invalid. In another narration from Muhammad, if he says 'one of you is divorced for 1000' and both accept, then the husband dies, each owes 500 and there is no inheritance between them. From al-Quniya: if a woman khala' herself for her mahr on condition that the husband gives her a certain amount of rice, it is valid and the place of delivery need not be specified according to Abu Hanifa because khul' is more flexible than sale. However, if the khul' is conditioned on the husband doing something (like delivering a garment), and the condition is not fulfilled, the divorce does not take effect. Other rulings include khul' with a condition of a written document or return of cloths, khul' against a debt, and cases where the object of khul' turns out to belong to the husband. In such cases, the wife owes nothing because the consideration effectively returns to the husband. Finally, it is reported that a pledge or surety for the khul' consideration is valid, and one person can act as agent for both parties in khul'.

Key Terms
التتارخانية (al-TatarKhaniyya): A Hanafi legal work by 'Alam al-Din al-TatarKhani.
القنية (al-Quniya): A Hanafi legal compilation by 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Bukhari.
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The consideration given by the wife in khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first ruling (khul' with two wives for a slave), why is the value of the slave divided according to the named amounts rather than the mahr of the like?
A) Because the mahr of the like is unknown.
B) Because the value represents the price of their bada' (sexual rights) and increase over the named is disliked.
C) Because the husband cannot afford more.
D) Because the slave is a common asset.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi jurisprudence, when a man khala' his two wives with a single object, the consideration is divided according to the amounts specified in the contract, and ambiguous allocation results in the wives being divorced without payment.

Conditional Khul' and Its Validity According to al-Quniya
Rulings on conditional khul' from al-Quniya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify valid conditions in khul' and apply the Hanafi rule that khul' is broader than sale.

Core Idea
In khul', conditions on the husband's performance are valid, but if the condition is integral, non-fulfillment prevents the divorce.

This lesson explores several scenarios from al-Quniya regarding conditional khul'. According to Abu Hanifa, khul' is more flexible than sale, so conditions like delivering rice or a bond are valid, and the place of delivery need not be specified. However, if the condition is made a prerequisite (e.g., delivery of a garment before the divorce), then failure to fulfill the condition prevents the divorce from taking effect. These rulings highlight the importance of the parties' intentions and the conditions attached to the consideration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first case: khul' for mahr on condition of rice delivery.
A woman khala' herself for her mahr on condition that the husband gives her a specific quantity of white rice. The ruling is that it is valid and place of delivery need not be specified.
Principle: khul' is broader than sale.
2
Note the principle from Abu Hanifa.
Khul' is more flexible than sale, so conditions that would require specification in sale are overlooked in khul'.
3
Examine the al-Bazz case: khul' for a garment on condition of delivery.
The husband makes the delivery of the garment a condition for the divorce. The garment perishes before delivery. Since the condition is integral, the divorce does not take effect.
If the condition is made a prerequisite, its fulfillment is necessary.
4
Analyze the case of the bond (qabala).
A woman gifts her mahr to her brother, who then lends it to the husband. She khala' herself on condition she delivers the bond the next day. She fails, but the divorce does not take effect.
Similar to the garment case: condition not fulfilled.
5
Discuss conditions for document or return of cloths.
If she khala' with condition that the husband write a document or return her cloths, it is said she does not become unlawful unless the document is written and cloths returned in the session.
The condition must be fulfilled in the same session.

Khul' When the Consideration Belongs to the Husband and Other Rulings
Rulings when the khul' consideration belongs to the husband, and other miscellaneous rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the object of khul' is revealed to belong to the husband, and identify the validity of pledge, guarantee, and agency in khul'.

Core Idea
If the consideration for khul' is found to belong to the husband, the wife owes nothing because the consideration effectively returns to him.

This lesson covers several miscellaneous rulings from various sources on khul'. The central theme is that if the object given as consideration is later discovered to belong to the husband, the wife owes nothing. This principle applies to slaves, dirhams, and dinars. Additionally, the lesson addresses the validity of pledge and guarantee for the khul' consideration, and the permissibility of delegating khul' to a third party or even having one person act for both sides.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case: khul' for a slave that turns out to be the husband's.
A woman khala' herself for a slave, then it is discovered (by mutual confession) that the slave belongs to the husband. The ruling: she owes nothing.
Because the consideration is effectively returned to the husband.
2
Extend to dirhams and dinars.
If the khul' was for dirhams or dinars that turn out to belong to the husband, the same ruling applies: nothing is due.
General principle: if the consideration belongs to the husband, it is as if no consideration was given.
3
Examine the case of khul' for a debt.
If she khala' herself for what she owes him (debt), and he accepts, the divorce occurs, the debt is void, and no payment is due.
4
Consider the validity of pledge and guarantee.
It is valid to use a pledge (rahn) or surety (kafala) for the khul' consideration.
From al-Khaniyya.
5
Consider delegation of khul'.
A woman can delegate the khul' to her husband, or a slave to his master; the delegate may perform khul' without their presence. One person can act on both sides.
From al-Mujtaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو خلع امرأتيه على عبد قسمت قيمته على مسميهما في العقد لأنه قيمة بضعيهما لا على مهر مثليهما لأن الزيادة على المسمى مكروهة في الخلع والزيادة في بدل الخلع باطلة لأنها زادت بعد هلاك المعقود عليه فصار كما لو زاد في بدل الصلح عن دم العمد فإنها لا تصح .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : إذا قال لامرأتيه إحداكما طالق بألف درهم والأخرى بمائة دينار فقبلتا طلقتا بغير شيء. وروى ابن سماعة عن محمد : إذا قال لامرأتيه إحداكما طالق بألف فقبلتا ومات فعلى كل واحدة منهما خمسمائة ولا ميراث اهـ. وفي القنية : اختلعت نفسها بالمهر بشرط أن الزوج يعطيها كذا مناً من الأرز الأبيض وخالعها به ينبغي أي يصح ولا يشترط بيان مكان الإيفاء عند أبي حنيفة لأن الخلع أوسع من البيع ففي بت : خالعها على ثوب بشرط أن تسلم إليه الثوب فقبلت فهلك الثوب قبل التسليم لم تبن لأنه يجعل نفس التسليم شرطاً . مخ: وهبت مهرها لأخيها فأخذ أخوها منه المهر قبالة ثم اختلعت نفسها منه بشرط أن تسلم له القبالة غداً فقبل ولم تسلم إليه القبالة غداً لا تحرم. ولو اختلعت بشرط الصك أو قالت بشرط أن يرد عليها أقمشتها فقيل لا تحرم ويشترط كتابة الصك ورد الأقمشة في المجلس خلعتك على عبدي وقف على قبولها ولم يجب شيء. خلعتك بمالي عليك من الدين وقبلت ينبغي أن يقع الطلاق ولا يجب شيء ويبطل الدين. ادعت مهرها على زوجها فأنكره ثم اختلعت نفسها بمهرها وقبل ثم تبين بالشهود أنها كان امرأته قبل الخلع فليس له شيء ولو اختلعت على عبد ثم تبين أنه عبد الزوج ولا ذلك إلا بالتصادق فينبغي أن لا يلزمها شيء لأن ما هو بدل الخلع يسلم له كما لو علم أنه عبده. وسئل لو كان الخلع على دراهم أو دنانير ثم تبين أنها للزوج لم يجب شيء .اهـ. وفي الخانية : ويجوز الرهن والكفالة ببدل الخلع. وفي المجتبى : فوضت الخلع إلى زوجها أو العبد إلى المولى ففعل بغير حضرتهما جاز والواحد يتولى الخلع من الجانبين.
And if he khala' his two wives with a slave, its value is divided according to the names given in the contract because it is the value of their sexual rights, not according to their dowers of the like, because increase over what is named is disliked in khul', and increase in the consideration for khul' is void because it increased after destruction of the object of contract, so it is like if one increased in the consideration for blood money of intentional killing, it is not valid. End quote. In al-TatarKhaniyya: If he said to his two wives, 'One of you is divorced for one thousand dirhams and the other for one hundred dinars,' and they accepted, they are divorced for nothing. And Ibn Sama'a narrated from Muhammad: If he said to his two wives, 'One of you is divorced for one thousand,' and they accepted and he dies, upon each is five hundred, and no inheritance. End quote. In al-Quniya: She khala' herself for the mahr on condition that the husband gives her so many mans of white rice, and he khala' her with it, it is proper, i.e., valid, and specification of place of delivery is not required according to Abu Hanifa because khul' is broader than sale. In al-Bazz: He khala' her for a garment on condition that she deliver the garment to him, she accepted, then the garment perished before delivery, she does not become separate because he made the delivery itself a condition. Different: She gifted her mahr to her brother, then her brother took from him the mahr as a loan or bond, then she khala' herself from him on condition that she deliver the bond to him tomorrow, he accepted, and she did not deliver the bond tomorrow, she does not become unlawful. And if she khala' with a condition of a document or she said with condition that he return her cloths, it is said she does not become unlawful, and writing the document and returning the cloths in the session is required. 'I khala' you for my slave that is a waqf on her acceptance, and nothing is due.' 'I khala' you for what is due to me from you of debt, and she accepted, it is proper that divorce occurs and nothing is due, and the debt is void. She claimed her mahr from her husband, he denied it, then she khala' herself for her mahr and he accepted, then it became clear by witnesses that she was his wife before the khul', so he has nothing. And if she khala' for a slave, then it became clear that it was the husband's slave, and that is only known by mutual confession, then it is proper that nothing is due from her because what is the consideration for khul' yields to him as if he knew it was his slave. And he was asked: If the khul' was for dirhams or dinars, then it became clear that they were the husband's, nothing is due. End quote. In al-Khaniyya: Pledge and guarantee for the consideration of khul' are valid. In al-Mujtaba: She delegated the khul' to her husband or the slave to the master, and he did it without their presence, it is valid, and one person can conduct the khul' on both sides.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage consolidates multiple rulings from various Hanafi texts on khul'. First, if a man divorces both his wives in return for a single slave, the value of the slave is divided according to the amounts specified in the contract for each wife, not according to their typical mahr, because any increase over what is named is disliked in khul' and an increase after the destruction of the subject matter is void. Then, from al-TatarKhaniyya: if a man says to his two wives 'one of you is divorced for 1000 dirhams and the other for 100 dinars' and they both accept, they are both divorced without any payment because the allocation is invalid. In another narration from Muhammad, if he says 'one of you is divorced for 1000' and both accept, then the husband dies, each owes 500 and there is no inheritance between them. From al-Quniya: if a woman khala' herself for her mahr on condition that the husband gives her a certain amount of rice, it is valid and the place of delivery need not be specified according to Abu Hanifa because khul' is more flexible than sale. However, if the khul' is conditioned on the husband doing something (like delivering a garment), and the condition is not fulfilled, the divorce does not take effect. Other rulings include khul' with a condition of a written document or return of cloths, khul' against a debt, and cases where the object of khul' turns out to belong to the husband. In such cases, the wife owes nothing because the consideration effectively returns to the husband. Finally, it is reported that a pledge or surety for the khul' consideration is valid, and one person can act as agent for both parties in khul'.

Key Terms
التتارخانية (al-TatarKhaniyya): A Hanafi legal work by 'Alam al-Din al-TatarKhani.
القنية (al-Quniya): A Hanafi legal compilation by 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Bukhari.
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The consideration given by the wife in khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a woman khala' herself for her mahr and later it is proven by witnesses that she was not his wife at the time, what is the ruling?
A) The khul' is invalid and she must return the mahr.
B) The husband has nothing.
C) She must pay the mahr again.
D) The marriage is revived.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, if the object of khul' turns out to belong to the husband, the wife owes no consideration, and the divorce remains valid.

Talaq — Divorce

Khul' and Talaq with Impermissible Consideration: Ruling and Compensation
Ruling with proof for khul'/talaq with impermissible compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when khul' or talaq is contracted with an impermissible item (wine, pig, carrion) and explain why no compensation is due.

Core Idea
Khul' with impermissible consideration is valid; divorce occurs but husband gets nothing.

What happens if a husband divorces his wife in exchange for a bottle of wine? Is the divorce valid? Does he get the wine? The Hanafi school addresses this with a nuanced ruling: the divorce takes effect, but the husband receives no compensation. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this rule and examines a difference of opinion within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine whether the passage is about khul' (divorce initiated by wife with compensation) or talaq (husband-initiated divorce). Note the ruling: the divorce occurs, but it is bain (irrevocable) in khul', revocable in other talaq, and the husband receives nothing.
The term 'majjānan' (gratuitously) indicates no financial obligation.
2
Analyze the Legal Reasoning (Talil)
The passage explains why the husband gets nothing: the wife did not deceive him, and the sexual act is not valued when leaving marriage. Since the consideration is void, only the wording of khul' remains effective, causing bainunah.
This is a reasoning-based ruling, not a direct textual proof.
3
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Identify Zafar's position: he holds that the wife must return the mahr. Compare with the majority view (Abu Hanifa and others) that no compensation is due.
This dispute is recorded in al-Muhit and al-Bazzaziyya.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The passage indicates that the fatwa is given according to the view that talaq does occur without compensation. This is the operative ruling for practice.
The passage quotes al-Bazzaziyya: 'and by it fatwa is given'.

He divorces her with wine or pig or carrion, it falls as bain (irrevocable) in khul', and revocable in other than khul', gratuitously, like 'khala'ni on what is in my hand' while there is nothing in her hand, and if she increased from property or dirhams, she returns her mahr or three?? the invalid. He said: (For if he khala' or divorces her with wine or pig or carrion, it falls as bain in khul', revocable in other, gratuitously) because khul' for what is not permissible is valid because it is not nullified by a corrupt condition, and nothing is due to him because she did not deceive him, and the sexual act is not valued in principle at the time of exit; it is only valued by naming property. And in al-Mujtaba: Wealth is only obligated by commitment, consumption of wealth, or ownership, and none of that occurred. Since the consideration became void, the effective factor in khul' is its wording, which necessitates bainunah because it is from the kinayah expressions that necessitate cutting the marital connection, and in the second (talaq) it is explicit and is revocable, so his saying 'gratuitously' applies to both issues. And in al-Misbah: I did it gratis meaning without compensation. Ibn Faris said: al-majan is giving something without price. And al-Farabi said: This is for you gratis i.e., without consideration. End quote. And Zafar obligated upon her return of the mahr as in al-Muhit. It is conditioned that she named something prohibited, because if she named something permissible for him, like 'khala'ni on this ring' and it turned out to be wine, she may return the mahr taken if the husband did not know it was wine, but if he knew, he gets nothing. And in al-Muhit: If he khala' her with a slave and it turned out to be free, he returns the mahr according to the two, and according to Abu Yusuf, its value if it had been a slave because it is known in marriage. And it is conditioned to khul' and talaq, because kitaba (contract of manumission) for wine or pig is void, and for carrion? or he becomes free if he pays in the first with obligation of his value because the master's property is valued, and he does not become free in the second, and marriage with an entire slave is valid with obligation of mahr al-mithl because the sexual act has value at the time of consummation. Then know that even though the consideration is not obligatory in khul' and talaq, they do not occur except with her acceptance. Hence it is said in al-Bazzaziyya: If she said to him 'khala'ni with property or on property' and she did not mention its amount, it is not completed in the apparent narration without her acceptance. And if the consideration is not due, does the talaq occur? It is said it occurs and that is the fatwa, and it is said it does not occur and that is more similar to the evidence. End quote. His saying: (like 'khala'ni on what is in my hand' while there is nothing in her hand) means the irrevocable divorce occurs with nothing upon her due to lack of naming something by which she would be deceiving him. And he indicated that if he said to her 'I khala' you on what is in my hand' while there is nothing in his hand, he also gets nothing, as there is no difference between them. If there was a jewel in his hand belonging to her, she accepted, it becomes his even if she did not know that, because she harmed herself when she accepted the khul' before knowing what was in his hand. And if he bought from her in this manner, it would be valid and she would have no option, so khul' is more appropriate. This is in al-Mabsut. And he indicated that if she said 'khala'ni on what is in my house' or 'on what is in my house from something' while there is nothing in her house, the khul' is from both sides. It will come at the end of the chapter from al-Bazzaziyya that one cannot be an agent from her side, whether the consideration is named or not, it is valid. And in al-TatarKhaniyya from al-Kubra: One person conducts khul' from both sides if it is khul', and it is compensation if the consideration is mentioned; in one narration that is the chosen view. No. Muhammad that.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage deals with khul' or talaq where the consideration is something impermissible like wine, pig, or carrion. The ruling is that the divorce occurs as bain (irrevocable) in the case of khul', and as revocable in the case of talaq other than khul', and the husband gets no compensation (gratuitously). The reasoning is that khul' with an impermissible item is still valid because it is not voided by a corrupt condition, and the husband does not deserve any payment because the wife did not deceive him (she didn't promise something that appeared valuable but turned out to be worthless). The sexual act is not considered valuable in itself when leaving marriage; it only becomes valued by the naming of a valid consideration. Since the consideration is void, only the wording of khul' remains effective, which is a kinayah (indirect expression) that necessitates bainunah. For explicit divorce (talaq), it is revocable. There is also a discussion of Zafar's view that she must return the mahr. The condition is that she named something prohibited; if she named something permissible but it turned out to be wine, she can take back the mahr if the husband was unaware of the fact; otherwise, the husband gets nothing. Additional rulings include cases where the consideration turns out to be a free person, etc. The passage also addresses that the acceptance of the wife is necessary even if the consideration is not due. There is a difference of opinion on whether talaq occurs when no consideration is due: the preferred view is that it does occur. The 'khala'ni on what is in my hand' scenario: if the wife says this and there is nothing in her hand, the divorce occurs without any payment because no specific consideration was named that would make her liable. If there was a jewel in the husband's hand belonging to the wife, and she accepted without knowing, the jewel becomes his, and she has no option, similar to a sale. Finally, the passage mentions that one person can act as agent for both parties in khul' if it is considered a compensation, but not from the wife's side according to al-Bazzaziyya.

Key Terms
مجاناً (majjānan): Gratis, without any compensation or payment.
بائن (bā'in): Irrevocable divorce; the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage contract.
كنايات (kināyāt): Indirect expressions that imply divorce but require intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband divorces his wife in exchange for a pig (khul'), what is the ruling?
A) The divorce is invalid because pig is not valid property.
B) The divorce is valid and the husband gets the pig or its value.
C) The divorce is valid (bain) and the husband gets nothing.
D) The divorce is valid but the wife must pay her mahr.

Key Takeaway
Khul' or talaq with an impermissible consideration is valid, but the husband receives no compensation because the consideration is void and the divorce itself is the effective exchange.

Ruling on Khul' with Prohibited Items and Unspecified Consideration
Expanding rulings on khul' with prohibited items and unspecified consideration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khul' with prohibited items, distinguish between ba'in and raj'i in such cases, and apply the rule about unspecified consideration like 'what is in my hand'.

Core Idea
Khul' with haram consideration is valid but no compensation is due; the divorce is ba'in for khul', raj'i for explicit talaq.

This passage from 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' explains a set of nuanced rulings regarding khul' and talaq when the wife offers prohibited items like wine, pig, or carrion, or when she says 'divorce me for what is in my hand' without specifying. The core principle is that the divorce itself is valid even if the condition about consideration is corrupt, but the compensation is not due if the woman did not deceive the husband. The type of divorce—ba'in or raj'i—depends on the wording used. Let's break down these rulings step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what is being ruled: khul' or talaq initiated by the wife in exchange for a prohibited item (wine, pig, carrion) or an unspecified consideration. The ruling states the divorce is valid, the husband receives no compensation (majjaanan), and the divorce is ba'in if it is khul', raj'i if it is explicit talaq.
The word 'majjaanan' means without compensation, and it applies to both scenarios.
2
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The text explains why the divorce is valid despite the corrupt condition: because the vulva (bud') is not valuable at the time of dissolution; it only becomes valuable by naming a consideration. Also, no compensation is due because the woman did not deceive the husband and no wealth was committed, consumed, or owned.
This is based on the principle that a condition that is fasid (corrupt) does not invalidate the contract itself; it only affects the obligation.
3
Distinguish between khul' and explicit talaq
In khul', the wording is kinayah (indirect), which severs the marriage immediately, making it ba'in. In explicit talaq (using the word 'talaq'), it is raj'i (revocable) because the intention is clear and allows for reconciliation.
This distinction is crucial for understanding whether the husband can take her back during 'iddah without a new contract.
4
Note the intra-madhhab disagreement
Imam Zufar held that the wife must return the mahr (dower) if she obtained khul' with a prohibited item, contrary to the majority of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad who say no compensation is due. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
The text also mentions that if the wife named a permissible item that turned out to be prohibited, she can retrieve the mahr if the husband was unaware, but if he knew, nothing is due.
5
Apply to unspecified consideration cases
The passage extends the same principle to cases like 'divorce me for what is in my hand' when there is nothing in her hand: the divorce occurs as ba'in without compensation. The text also discusses similar scenarios like 'what is in my house' or 'what is in the belly of my slave-girl'.
In these cases, since no specific consideration is named, the woman does not become a 'deceiver' (gharra) and the divorce is valid without compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن خالعها أو طلقها بخمر أو خنزير أو ميتة وقع بائن في الخلع رجعي في غيره مجاناً) لأن الخلع على ما لا يحل صحيح لأنه لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد ولا يجب له شيء لأنها لم تغره والبضع غير متقوم في الأصل حالة الخروج وإنما يتقوم بتسمية المال. وفي المجتبى : وإنما يلزم المال بالالتزام أو باستهلاك المال أو بملكه ولم يوجد، ولما بطل العوض كان العامل في الخلع لفظه وهو يوجب البينونة لأنه من الكنايات الموجبة لقطع وصلة النكاح، وفي الثاني الصريح وهو رجعي فقوله «مجاناً عائد إلى المسألتين. وفي المصباح: فعلته مجاناً أي بغير عوض قال ابن فارس: المجان عطية الشيء بلا ثمن. وقال الفارابي : هذا لك مجاناً أي بلا بدل اهـ وأوجب زفر عليها رد المهر كما في المحيط. قيد بكونها سمت محرماً لأنها لو سمت له حلالاً كخالعني على هذا الحل فإذا هو خمر فلها أن ترد المهر المأخوذ إن لم يعلم الزوج بكونه خمراً، وإن علم به فلا شيء له وفي المحيط : لو خلعها على عبد فإذا هو حر رجع بالمهر عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف بقيمته لو كان عبداً لما عرف في النكاح. وقيد بالخلع والطلاق لأن الكتابة على خمر أو خنزير فاسدة وعلى ميتة أو فيعتق إن أداه في الأولى مع وجوب قيمة نفسه لأن ملك المولى متقوم ولا يعتق في الثانية، والنكاح بالكل صحيح مع وجوب مهر المثل لتقوم البضع عند الدخول. ثم اعلم أن البدل وإن لم يجب في الخلع والطلاق فلا يقعان إلا بقبولها ولذا قال في البزازية : لو قالت له خالعني بمال أو على مال ولم تذكر قدره لا يتم في ظاهر الرواية بلا قبولها. وإذا لم يجب البدل هل يقع الطلاق؟ قيل يقع وبه يفتى، وقيل لا يقع وهو الأشبه بالدليل اهـ. قوله : (كخالعني على ما في يدي ولا شيء في يدها أي يقع الطلاق البائن من غير شيء عليها لعدم تسمية شيء تصير به غارة له وأشار إلى أنه لو قال لها خالعتك على ما في يدي ولا شيء في يده إنه لا شيء له أيضاً إذ لا فرق بينهما، فلو كان في يده جوهرة لها فقبلت فهي له وإن لم تكن علمت ذلك لأنها هي التي أضرت بنفسها حين قبلت الخلع قبل أن تعلم ما في يده، ولو اشترى منها بهذه الصفة كان جائزاً ولا خيار لها فالخلع أولى؛ كذا في المبسوط. وأشار إلى أنها لو قالت خالعني على ما في بيتي أو ما في بيتي من شيء ولا شيء في بيتها الخلع من الجانبين أنها كمسألة الكتاب لأن الشيء يصدق على غير المال؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وكذا لو قالت على ما في يدي من شيء أو على ما في بطن جاريتي ولم تلد لأقل من ستة أشهر؛ كذا في المجتبى. وفي المحيط : لو اختلعت على ما في بطن جاريتها أو غنمها أو ما في نخلها صح وله ما في بطنها، وإن لم يكن فلا شيء له، ولو حدث بعده في بطونها فللمرأة لأن ما في بطنها اسم للموجود للحال. ولو اختلعت على حمل جاريتها وليس في بطنها حمل ترد المهر لأنها غرته حيث أطمعته فيما له قيمة لأن الحمل مال متقوم ولكن في وجوده احتمال وتوهم ويصح الخلع بعوض موهوم بخلاف ما في البطن لأنه قد يكون مالاً وقد لا يكون كريح أو ما يحويه البطن .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : لو طلقها على أن تبريه عن كفالة نفس فلان فالطلاق رجعي، ولو طلقها على أن تبريه عن الألف التي كفلها لها عن فلان فالطلاق بائن
He said: (If she divorces him or he divorces her with wine, or a pig, or an animal that died without slaughter (maytah), then it occurs as ba'in in khul' and raj'i in other than it, without compensation) because khul' for something that is not permissible is valid because it is not invalidated by a corrupt condition, and nothing is due to him because she did not deceive him, and the vulva is not a valuable consideration in principle at the time of dissolution; it only becomes valuable by naming a consideration. In al-Mujtaba: Wealth becomes obligatory only by commitment, or by consuming wealth, or by ownership, and none of these occurred. When the consideration is void, the operative factor in khul' is the wording, which necessitates ba'in (irreversibility) because it is among the kinaayat (indirect expressions) that necessitate severing the marital tie. In the second [case, i.e., talaq with explicit wording], it is raj'i (revocable). So his saying 'without compensation' applies to both issues. In al-Misbah: I did it 'majjaanan' (for free), i.e., without compensation. Ibn Faris said: al-majaan is giving a thing without price. al-Farabi said: This is for you 'majjaanan', i.e., without exchange. Zufar made the return of the mahr obligatory for her as in al-Muhit. It is conditioned that she named a prohibited item because if she named a permissible thing to him, like 'divorce me for this honey', and it turned out to be wine, then she can return the taken mahr if the husband did not know it was wine. If he knew, then nothing is due to him. In al-Muhit: If he divorced her in exchange for a slave, and it turned out to be free, then the mahr is returned according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]; according to Abu Yusuf, its value if it had been a slave, according to what is known in marriage. It is restricted to khul' and talaq because kitabah (contract of emancipation) for wine or pig is void, and for maytah, he is freed if he pays it in the first case with the obligation of his own value because the master's ownership is valuable, and he is not freed in the second. Marriage for all of that is valid with the obligation of mahr al-mithl (proper dowry) because the vulva is valuable at the time of consummation. Then know that even though the consideration is not obligatory in khul' and talaq, they do not occur except with her acceptance. Hence in al-Bazzaziyyah: If she said 'divorce me for wealth' or 'for wealth' without mentioning its amount, it is not completed in the apparent transmission without her acceptance. If the consideration is not obligatory, does the talaq occur? It was said it does occur, and it is given as fatwa; it was said it does not occur, and that is more akin to evidence. He said: (like 'divorce me for what is in my hand' when there is nothing in her hand, meaning the ba'in talaq occurs without anything due from her due to not naming something by which she would become his deceiver. He pointed out that if he said to her 'I divorce you for what is in my hand' when there is nothing in his hand, nothing is due to him either, as there is no difference between them. If there was a jewel in his hand that belongs to her and she accepted, it becomes his even if she did not know that, because she harmed herself when she accepted the khul' before knowing what is in his hand. If she bought from him with this description, it would be permissible and she has no option (khiyar); so khul' is more appropriate. This is in al-Mabsut. He pointed out that if she said 'divorce me for what is in my house' or 'for what is in my house of something' when there is nothing in her house, it is khul' from both sides. It is like the issue of the book because 'something' applies to other than wealth; as in Fath al-Qadir. Similarly, if she said 'for what is in my hand of something' or 'for what is in the belly of my slave-girl' and she has not given birth for less than six months; as in al-Mujtaba. In al-Muhit: If she divorced herself for what is in the belly of her slave-girl or her sheep or what is in her palm trees, it is valid and he gets what is in her belly, and if there is nothing, nothing is due to him. If later something occurs in their bellies, it belongs to the woman because 'what is in her belly' is a term for what exists at the moment. If she divorced herself for the pregnancy of her slave-girl and there is no pregnancy in her belly, she returns the mahr because she deceived him by making him desire something of value, for pregnancy is valuable property but its existence is probable and illusory. Khul' with illusory consideration is valid, unlike 'what is in the belly' because it may be wealth or may not be, like wind or what the belly contains. In al-Tatarakhaniyyah: If he divorces her on condition that she releases him from the guarantee of someone's person, the talaq is raj'i. If he divorces her on condition that she releases him from the thousand dirhams for which he had stood guarantee for her regarding someone, the talaq is ba'in.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling of khul' and talaq with prohibited or unspecified consideration. The author explains that khul' with a prohibited item like wine, pig, or carrion is valid despite the corrupt condition, but no compensation is due because the woman did not deceive the husband and the marital right (bud') is not valuable at the time of dissolution. The talaq is ba'in in khul' because khul' is a kinayah expression severing the marriage, but if it is an explicit talaq (with the word 'talaq'), it is raj'i. The word 'majjaanan' (for free) applies to both cases. Zufar's opposing view (that mahr must be returned) is noted. The text then details scenarios where the woman specifies a prohibited item without knowing it, leading to her right to recover the mahr if the husband was unaware. It also extends the same principle to cases like 'what is in my hand' where nothing exists, leading to talaq without compensation. The commentary emphasizes the role of acceptance, the rule that the contract is valid despite a fasid condition, and the distinction between ba'in and raj'i based on the type of wording used.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): A form of divorce initiated by the wife in return for consideration paid to the husband.
بائن (ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that severs the marriage immediately without the possibility of revocation during the 'iddah.
رجعي (raj'i): A revocable divorce where the husband can take back his wife during the 'iddah without a new contract.
مجاناً (majjaanan): Without any compensation, for free.
غرة (gharra): Deception; the woman who deceives the husband by implying a valuable consideration that does not exist.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A corrupt condition that does not invalidate the contract but may affect the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband divorces his wife in exchange for a pig (khinzir), what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The talaq is invalid because the consideration is haram.
B) The talaq is ba'in and no compensation is due to the husband.
C) The talaq is raj'i and compensation is due.
D) The talaq is ba'in and the wife must return the mahr.

Key Takeaway
Khul' and talaq with prohibited or unspecified consideration are valid, but no compensation is due unless the wife deliberately deceived the husband about the consideration's existence or value.

Specifying Mal or Dirhams in Khul': Returning Mahr or Three Dirhams
Explaining the consequences when a wife specifies 'mal' or 'darahim' in khul' but possesses nothing of the kind.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the compensation a wife must pay when she specifies 'mal' or 'darahim' in khul' but possesses nothing of the kind.

Core Idea
When a wife names a category in khul', the minimum of that category becomes due if nothing exists.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding khul' (divorce initiated by the wife). When the wife specifies the consideration as 'mal' or 'darahim', but she has none, the law imposes a substitute to prevent the husband from losing the inducement. The ruling hinges on whether the specification creates a definite expectation, and the linguistic analysis of the term 'darahim' as a plural requiring a minimum of three.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two forms of specification
Identify whether the wife said 'on what is in my hand of mal (wealth)' or 'of darahim (dirhams)'. 'Mal' is an open category; 'darahim' is a specific countable noun.
The ruling differs based on the word used.
2
Apply the ruling to each
If she specified 'mal' and has none, she returns the mahr she received. If she specified 'darahim' and has none, she pays three dirhams.
The compensation is wajib (obligatory).
3
Trace the linguistic reasoning for 'darahim'
The source argues that 'darahim' is a plural with no upper limit, so the minimum (three) becomes obligatory, by analogy to acknowledgments or bequests of dirhams. Additionally, the preposition 'min' here is explanatory (li al-bayan), not partitive, so it does not reduce the obligation.
This addresses a potential objection that 'min' implies a portion.
4
Consider the exception for knowledge
If the husband knew that there was nothing of the specified category, no compensation is due because he was not deceived.
This exception is based on the principle that deception (taghrir) is absent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن زادت من مال أو من دراهم ردت مهرها أو ثلاثة دراهم) يعني ردت مهرها فيما إذا قالت خالعني على ما في يدي من مال ولم يكن في يدها شيء وردت ثلاثة دراهم فيما إذا قالت خالعني على ما في يدي من دارهم ولم يكن في يدها شيء لأنها في الأولى لما سمت مالاً لم يكن الزوج راضياً بالزوال إلا بالعوض ولا وجه إلى إيجاب المسمى وقيمته للجهالة ولا إلى قيمة البضع أعني مهر المثل لأنه غير متقوم حالة الخروج فتعين إيجاب ما قام به على الزوج ؛ كذا في الهداية. وقيده في الخلاصة بعدم العلم فقال : لو خالعها على ما في هذا البيت من المتاع وعلم أنه لا متاع في هذا البيت وقع الطلاق ولا يلزمها شيء وذكر اليد مثال والبيت والصندوق وبطن الجارية والغنم كاليد. وقوله «من مال مثال أيضاً والمتاع والحمل للبطن كالمال فإذا قالت على ما في بطن جاريتي أو غنمي من حمل ردت المهر. وفي المحيط لو خالعها بما لها عليه من المهر ثم تبين أنه لم يبق عليه شيء من المهر لزومها رد المهر لأنه طلقها بطمع ما نص عليه فلا يقع مجاناً، فإن علم أنه لا الزوج لها عليه وأن لا متاع في البيت في مسألة على ما في البيت من متاع لا يلزمها شيء لأنها لم تطمعه فلم يصر مغروراً اهـ. وفي الثاني ذكرت الجمع ولا غاية لأقصاه وأدناه ثلاثة فوجب الأدنى كما لو أقر بدراهم أو أوصى بدراهم وأورد عليه أن «من» للتبعيض فينبغي وجوب درهم أو درهمين وأجيب بأنها هنا للبيان لأن الأصل أن كل موضع تم الكلام بنفسه ولكنه اشتمل على ضرب إبهام فهي للبيان وإلا فللتبعيض، وقولها خالعني على ما في يدي كلام تام بنفسه حتى جاز الاقتصار عليه ولا فرق في الحكم بين ذكر الجمع منكرا أو معرفاً. وأورد عليه إذا كان معرفاً أنه ينبغي وجوب واحد فقط لما عرف أن الجمع المحلي كالمفرد المحلي كما لو حلف لا يشتري العبيد أو لا النساء . يتزوج وأجيب بأنه إنما ينصرف إلى الجنس إذا عرى عن قرينة العهد كما في المثالين وقد وجدت مهر
He said: (And if she adds from wealth (mal) or from dirhams, she returns her mahr or three dirhams) meaning she returns her mahr when she says 'divorce me for what is in my hand of wealth' and there is nothing in her hand; and she returns three dirhams when she says 'divorce me for what is in my hand of dirhams' and there is nothing in her hand, because in the first case, when she named wealth, the husband was not content with dissolution except in exchange, and there is no way to necessitate the named object and its value due to ignorance, nor to necessitate the value of the vulva, meaning the proper mahr, because it is not valuable at the time of dissolution, so it is determined to necessitate what is established upon the husband. This is from al-Hidayah. In al-Khulasa, it is restricted by ignorance: if he divorces her for what is in this house of furniture and he knows there is no furniture in this house, the talaq occurs and nothing is due from her. He mentioned 'hand' as an example; house, box, belly of a slave-girl, and sheep are like the hand. His saying 'from wealth' is also an example; furniture and pregnancy of the belly are like wealth, so if she says 'for what is in the belly of my slave-girl or my sheep of pregnancy', she returns the mahr. In al-Muhit: If he divorced her for the mahr that she owes him and then it becomes clear that nothing of the mahr remains upon him, she must return the mahr because he divorced her with the desire for what was stated, so it does not occur for free. If he knows that there is no mahr owed to him and that there is no furniture in the house, in the issue of 'for what is in the house of furniture', nothing is due from her because she did not make him desire, so he is not deceived. In the second case, she mentioned a plural (darahim) and there is no upper limit; its minimum is three, so the minimum becomes obligatory, just as if one acknowledged dirhams or bequeathed dirhams. It was objected that 'min' indicates partitive, so one or two dirhams should be obligatory. The answer is that here it is for explanation (li al-bayan) because the principle is that wherever the speech is complete by itself but includes a type of ambiguity, 'min' is for explanation; otherwise it is for partitive. Her saying 'divorce me for what is in my hand' is complete speech by itself such that it is permissible to limit to it, and there is no difference in the ruling between mentioning the plural as indefinite or definite. It was objected that if it is definite, it should necessitate only one because it is known that the definite plural is like the definite singular, as when one swears not to buy the slaves or marry the women. The answer is that it applies to the genus when it is free from a context of covenant, as in the two examples, and the mahr has been found.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when a wife specifies the consideration in khul' as 'mal' (wealth) or 'darahim' (dirhams) but has nothing of the kind. If she says 'what is in my hand of mal' and there is no mal, she must return the mahr she received, because the husband was induced by the prospect of a specific category of wealth. If she says 'what is in my hand of darahim' and there is none, she must pay three dirhams, the minimum of a plural noun. The reasoning is that the husband's consent was based on the named category, not on a specific amount; 'darahim' is a plural with no upper limit, so the lowest number (three) is imposed. The text also discusses the grammatical role of 'min': here it is for explanation (li al-bayan) because the sentence 'khal'ani 'ala ma fi yadi' is complete but ambiguous, and the added word clarifies; if it were partitive, it would necessitate only part of what is in the hand. If the husband knows there is nothing, no compensation is due because he is not deceived. The ruling applies analogously to other containers like house, box, belly of a slave-girl, or sheep.

Key Terms
مال (mal): Wealth, property; in this context, any valuable asset other than dirhams specifically.
دراهم (darahim): Dirhams, silver coins; a specific currency, whose plural implies at least three.
من للبيان (min li al-bayan): The preposition 'min' used for explanation (bayan) rather than partitive (tab'id).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife says 'I divorce you for what is in my hand of dirhams' and she has nothing, what must she pay?
A) Nothing
B) The mahr
C) Three dirhams
D) One dirham

Key Takeaway
In khul', when a wife specifies a category she does not possess, the compensation is determined by the nature of the category: unspecified 'mal' triggers return of the mahr; specified 'darahim' triggers minimum three dirhams.

Khul' with Compensation of What Is in the Belly
Ruling on khul' with uncertain compensation and the distinction between 'ma fi al-batn' and 'haml'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khul' when the compensation is specified as 'what is in the belly' and distinguish it from when the compensation is specified as 'pregnancy' (haml).

Core Idea
Khul' is valid even with uncertain compensation; deception (ghurur) triggers return of mahr.

In Hanafi law, khul' allows a wife to divorce her husband by offering him compensation. But what if she offers something uncertain, like 'what is in the belly'? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the ruling: the contract is valid, but the outcome depends on whether the specified item exists at the time. The key distinction is between 'what is in the belly' (ma fi al-batn) and 'pregnancy' (haml), each carrying different consequences when the compensation is absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling being discussed? It is the validity of khul' when the compensation is an uncertain item like 'what is in the belly' of a slave-girl, sheep, or palm tree.
The act is khul' (divorce initiated by wife with compensation). The ruling is that it is valid (sahih).
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites from al-Muhit and al-Mujtaba. The proof is that 'a thing can be true for something other than property,' meaning the compensation does not need to be definite property; it can be speculative.
The proof is based on linguistic and juristic reasoning, not a direct text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
'What is in the belly' (ma fi al-batn) refers only to the actual contents at the time of contract. If nothing exists, the husband gets nothing. In contrast, 'pregnancy' (haml) is considered valuable property, so if it is nonexistent, the wife must return the mahr due to deception.
The logical link: the term 'ma fi al-batn' is ambiguous and does not imply a specific property; 'haml' implies a valuable asset.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools require the compensation to be definitely existing for the contract to be valid. The Hanafi school allows conjectural consideration.
The cross-madhhab difference is mentioned; the passage does not elaborate on the other side.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The ruling from later Hanafi works (fatawa mutakhkhirin) is that khul' is valid; the wife's liability depends on whether she caused deception.
The mufta bihi is that the contract stands, but if she specified 'pregnancy' and it was absent, she must return the mahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنها كمسألة الكتاب لأن الشيء يصدق على غير المال؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وكذا لو قالت على ما في يدي من شيء أو على ما في بطن جاريتي ولم تلد لأقل من ستة أشهر؛ كذا في المجتبى. وفي المحيط : لو اختلعت على ما في بطن جاريتها أو غنمها أو ما في نخلها صح وله ما في بطنها، وإن لم يكن فلا شيء له، ولو حدث بعده في بطونها فللمرأة لأن ما في بطنها اسم للموجود للحال. ولو اختلعت على حمل جاريتها وليس في بطنها حمل ترد المهر لأنها غرته حيث أطمعته فيما له قيمة لأن الحمل مال متقوم ولكن في وجوده احتمال وتوهم ويصح الخلع بعوض موهوم بخلاف ما في البطن لأنه قد يكون مالاً وقد لا يكون كريح أو ما يحويه البطن .اهـ.
That it is like the issue of the book because a thing can be true for something other than property; thus in Fath al-Qadir. Similarly, if she said 'on what is in my hand of something' or 'on what is in the belly of my slave-girl' and she did not give birth for less than six months; thus in al-Mujtaba. In al-Muhit: If she made khul' on what is in the belly of her slave-girl or her sheep or what is in her palm tree, it is valid and he gets what is in her belly, and if there is nothing then nothing for him, and if it occurs later in her bellies then it is for the woman because 'what is in her belly' is a name for what exists at the present moment. And if she made khul' on the pregnancy of her slave-girl and there is no pregnancy in her belly, she returns the mahr because she deceived him by making him hopeful of something of value, because the pregnancy is valuable property but its existence is probable and conjectural, and khul' with a conjectural consideration is valid, unlike what is in the belly because it may be property and may not, like wind or what the belly contains. End.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof explaining the consequences when a wife makes khul' with compensation that is uncertain or nonexistent. The author first establishes that the ruling is analogous to the main issue of the book (referring to Kanz al-Daqaiq) because the term 'thing' can apply to non-property. Then he cites al-Mujtaba: if she says 'on what is in my hand of something' or 'on what is in the belly of my slave-girl' and the slave-girl has not given birth in less than six months (indicating pregnancy is possible), the rule applies. From al-Muhit: if she makes khul' on what is in the belly of her slave-girl, sheep, or palm tree, the khul' is valid and the husband takes what is in the belly. If nothing is there, he gets nothing. If the belly later contains something, it belongs to the wife because 'what is in the belly' refers only to what exists at the time. However, if she specified 'pregnancy' (haml) and there is no pregnancy, she must return the mahr because she deceived him by making him desire something of value. Pregnancy is considered valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) but its existence is uncertain; thus khul' with a conjectural consideration is valid, unlike 'what is in the belly' which may be nothing but wind. The distinction is that 'haml' implies an actual property, while 'ma fi al-batn' is ambiguous. The ruling is from later fatawa works (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife with compensation given to the husband; the divorce becomes ba'in.
غرور (ghurur): Deception causing the husband to agree to khul' based on a false expectation of valuable compensation.
ما في البطن (ma fi al-batn): Literally 'what is in the belly'; refers to the actual contents at the time of contract, not a future pregnancy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a wife makes khul' on 'what is in the belly of her slave-girl' and the slave-girl has no pregnancy, what is the ruling?
A) The khul' is invalid and no divorce occurs.
B) The khul' is valid, and the husband gets nothing.
C) The khul' is valid, and the wife must return the mahr.
D) The khul' is valid, and the husband takes the slave-girl.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, khul' with compensation of 'what is in the belly' is valid even if empty, but specifying 'pregnancy' where none exists constitutes deception requiring return of mahr.

Talaq on Condition of Release from Suretyship
Distinguishes talaq raj'i from ba'in based on type of kafalah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for talaq conditional on release from suretyship and distinguish between kafalah bi al-nafs and kafalah bi al-mal.

Core Idea
A divorce conditional on release from a person-suretyship (non-financial) is raj'i; conditional on release from a debt-suretyship (financial) is ba'in.

In this lesson we examine a subtle distinction from the Hanafi fatawa literature. The nature of the surety—whether it guarantees a person's appearance or a financial debt—determines the type of divorce that occurs when the wife agrees to release her husband from that suretyship. Understanding this difference is crucial because it affects the wife's post-divorce status and the possibility of reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Name the conditions and the resulting talaq type: (1) release from suretyship for a person → raj'i; (2) release from a specific debt → ba'in.
The condition is the wife's act of releasing the husband from his suretyship obligation.
2
Classify the suretyship type
Determine whether the suretyship is for a person (kafalah bi al-nafs) or for a debt (kafalah bi al-mal). The passage explicitly distinguishes between 'kafalah nafs' and 'kafalah mal'.
Only financial suretyship can serve as a valid compensation.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle on compensation
In Hanafi law, a divorce becomes ba'in when the wife provides financial compensation (e.g., in khula). Here, release from a financial surety is considered valuable, making the divorce ba'in. Release from a personal surety is not financial, so the divorce remains raj'i.
This principle is consistent with the general rule: al-iwad (consideration) makes talaq ba'in.
4
Note the authority
The ruling is from al-Tatarkhaniyyah, a later fatwa compilation. It is consistent with earlier Hanafi usul and is the mufta bihi position.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التتارخانية : لو طلقها على أن تبريه عن كفالة نفس فلان فالطلاق رجعي، ولو طلقها على أن تبريه عن الألف التي كفلها لها عن فلان فالطلاق بائن
In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: If he divorces her on condition that she release him from suretyship for the person of so-and-so, the divorce is raj'i. And if he divorces her on condition that she release him from the thousand (dirhams) for which he stood surety for her from so-and-so, the divorce is ba'in.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from al-Tatarkhaniyyah, a later fatawa compilation. It distinguishes between two scenarios of talaq conditional on release. If the husband divorces his wife on condition that she release him from a suretyship (kafalah) that he undertook for the person of a third party (i.e., he guaranteed the person's appearance, not a debt), then the divorce is raj'i (revocable) because the suretyship is not a financial obligation that can be the basis of a valid compensation. In contrast, if the condition is that she release him from a specific debt of one thousand dirhams that he guaranteed for her (e.g., he was surety for her debt to someone else), then the divorce is ba'in (irrevocable) because the release from debt is a valuable consideration. The key is the nature of the suretyship: a surety for a person (kafalah bi al-nafs) is not financial, so it cannot be a proper compensation, making the divorce raj'i. A surety for a debt (kafalah bi al-mal) is financial, so it serves as compensation, making the divorce ba'in. Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Key Terms
كفالة (kafalah): Suretyship; a contract where one person guarantees the debt or appearance of another.
طلاق رجعي (talaq raj'i): Revocable divorce where husband can take wife back without a new marriage within the iddah.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): Irrevocable divorce where husband cannot remarry without a new contract and mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband divorces his wife on condition that she release him from suretyship for a person (kafalah bi al-nafs), what is the type of divorce?
A) Ba'in (irrevocable) because it involves a condition.
B) Raj'i (revocable) because the suretyship is not financial.
C) Invalid because suretyship cannot be a condition for divorce.
D) Ba'in if the condition is met; otherwise raj'i.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a divorce conditional on release from a personal surety is revocable (raj'i), while release from a financial surety results in an irrevocable divorce (ba'in).

Khul' with Empty Hand: Returning Mahr or Three Dirhams
Ruling on khul' compensation when wife's hand is empty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on khul' compensation when the wife specifies property vs dirhams and her hand is empty, and identify the condition of the husband's knowledge.

Core Idea
If the wife promises non-existent property in khul', she returns the mahr; if she promises dirhams, she pays three dirhams.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a practical scenario in khul': the wife offers something she does not possess. The ruling hinges on how she specifies the compensation—'mal' (property) or 'dirhams'—and whether the husband was aware of the emptiness. We will unpack the reasoning, including linguistic principles and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
Identify whether the wife said 'mal' or 'dirhams'. This determines the compensation owed if her hand is empty.
If she said 'mal', she returns the mahr. If she said 'dirhams', she returns three dirhams.
2
Understand the reasoning for each
For 'mal', the named thing is unknown, so the mahr she took is returned. For 'dirhams', the plural imposes a minimum of three, analogized to confession or bequest.
The vulva (buda') is not considered valuable at the time of exit, so mahr al-mithl is not imposed.
3
Apply the qualification from al-Khulasa
If the husband knew the hand was empty, no compensation is required because he was not deceived.
Knowledge nullifies the claim of deception (ghurur).
4
Analyze the linguistic objections
Answer the objection about 'min' being partitive: here it is for explanation (li al-bayan) because the sentence is complete but ambiguous. The definite plural refers to a covenant (ahd) due to 'in my hand'.
This distinguishes khul' from other contexts like oaths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن زادت من مال أو من دراهم ردت مهرها أو ثلاثة دراهم) يعني ردت مهرها فيما إذا قالت خالعني على ما في يدي من مال ولم يكن في يدها شيء وردت ثلاثة دراهم فيما إذا قالت خالعني على ما في يدي من دارهم ولم يكن في يدها شيء لأنها في الأولى لما سمت مالاً لم يكن الزوج راضياً بالزوال إلا بالعوض ولا وجه إلى إيجاب المسمى وقيمته للجهالة ولا إلى قيمة البضع أعني مهر المثل لأنه غير متقوم حالة الخروج فتعين إيجاب ما قام به على الزوج ؛ كذا في الهداية. وقيده في الخلاصة بعدم العلم فقال : لو خالعها على ما في هذا البيت من المتاع وعلم أنه لا متاع في هذا البيت وقع الطلاق ولا يلزمها شيء وذكر اليد مثال والبيت والصندوق وبطن الجارية والغنم كاليد. وقوله «من مال مثال أيضاً والمتاع والحمل للبطن كالمال فإذا قالت على ما في بطن جاريتي أو غنمي من حمل ردت المهر. وفي المحيط لو خالعها بما لها عليه من المهر ثم تبين أنه لم يبق عليه شيء من المهر لزومها رد المهر لأنه طلقها بطمع ما نص عليه فلا يقع مجاناً، فإن علم أنه لا الزوج لها عليه وأن لا متاع في البيت في مسألة على ما في البيت من متاع لا يلزمها شيء لأنها لم تطمعه فلم يصر مغروراً اهـ. وفي الثاني ذكرت الجمع ولا غاية لأقصاه وأدناه ثلاثة فوجب الأدنى كما لو أقر بدراهم أو أوصى بدراهم وأورد عليه أن «من» للتبعيض فينبغي وجوب درهم أو درهمين وأجيب بأنها هنا للبيان لأن الأصل أن كل موضع تم الكلام بنفسه ولكنه اشتمل على ضرب إبهام فهي للبيان وإلا فللتبعيض، وقولها خالعني على ما في يدي كلام تام بنفسه حتى جاز الاقتصار عليه ولا فرق في الحكم بين ذكر الجمع منكرا أو معرفاً. وأورد عليه إذا كان معرفاً أنه ينبغي وجوب واحد فقط لما عرف أن الجمع المحلي كالمفرد المحلي كما لو حلف لا يشتري العبيد أو لا النساء . يتزوج وأجيب بأنه إنما ينصرف إلى الجنس إذا عرى عن قرينة العهد كما في المثالين وقد وجدت القرينة هنا على العهد وهو قولها على ما في يدي؛ كذا في الكافي. وأوضحه في فتح القدير فقال : لأن قولها على ما في يدي أفاد كون المسمى مظروفاً بيدها وهو عام يص على الدراهم وغيرها فصار بالدراهم عهد في الجملة من حيث هو مما صدقات لفظ ما وهو مبهم وقعت «من» بياناً له ومدخولها هو المبين لخصوص المظروف والدراهم مثال، والمراد أنها بينت المبهم بجمع كالدنانير وينبغي أن يكون قولها على ما في هذا البيت من الشياه أو الخيل أو البغال أو الحمير كذلك يلزمها ثلاثة من المسمى ثم رأيت في المعراج : لكن زاد الثياب وفيه نظر للجهالة المتفاحشة وقيد بقوله ولا شيء في يدها» لأنه لو كان في يدها مال متقوم كان له قليلاً كان أو كثيراً ولا يلزمها رد المهر في الأولى، وأما في الثانية فلا بد أن يكون في يدها مما سمته، فلو كان في يدها أو درهمان لزمها تكملة الثلاثة ؛ كذا في الخانية والمبسوط . وبهذا علم أن في کلام المصنف مسامحة لأن عدم وجود شيء في يدها شرط لرد المهر في الأولى، وعدم وجود الثلاثة شرط في الثانية، وكلامه لا يفيده. وأفاد بقوله ردت المهر أنه مقبوض فيدل على أنه لو لم يكن مقبوضاً برىء منه ولا شيء عليها كما ذكره العمادي في فصوله وفي الجوهرة ثم إذا وجب الرجوع بالمهر له وكانت قد أبرأته لم يرجع عليها بشيء لأن عين ما يستحقه قد سلم له بالبراءة فلو رجع عليها لأجل الهبة وهي لا توجب على الواهب ضماناً .اهـ. وفي البزازية: والحاصل أنه إذا يرجع ما ليس بمتقوم لا يجب شيء، وإن سمى موجوداً معلوماً يجب المسمى، وإن سمى مجهولاً جهالة مستدركة فكذلك وإن فحشت الجهالة وتمكن الخطر بأن خالعها على ما يثمر نخلها العام أو على ما في البيت من المتاع ولم يكن فيه شيء بطلت التسمية وردت ما سمى قبضت اهـ . قيد بالخلع لأن السيد لو أعتق عبده على ما في يده من الدراهم وليس في يده شيء يجب عليه قيمة نفسه لأن منافع البضع غير متقومة حالة الخروج فلا يشترط كون المسمى معلوماً بخلاف العبد فإنه متقوم في نفسه، وبخلاف النكاح حيث يجب مهر المثل لأنه متقوم حالة الدخول ؛ كذا في البدائع. ودلت المسألة الأولى على أنه لو خالعها على عبد بعينه مثلاً وقد كان ميتاً قبل الخلع أنه يرجع عليها بالمهر الذي أخذته منه للغرور بخلاف ما لو مات بعده حيث تجب قيمته كما لو استحق وظهور حريته كموته قبل الخلع فيرجع عليها بالمهر
His statement: (And if she adds from property or from dirhams, she returns her mahr or three dirhams) means she returns her mahr in the case where she said 'make khul' with me on what is in my hand of property' and there was nothing in her hand, and she returns three dirhams in the case where she said 'make khul' with me on what is in my hand of dirhams' and there was nothing in her hand. Because in the first, when she specified property, the husband was not satisfied with the dissolution except for compensation, and there is no way to impose the named thing and its value due to ignorance, nor to impose the value of the vulva, i.e., dower, because it is not valuable at the time of exit, so specifying what was established on him became necessary; thus in al-Hidayah. Al-Khulasa qualified it with lack of knowledge, saying: If she made khul' with him on what is in this house of goods and he knew there are no goods in this house, the divorce falls and nothing is required of her. He mentioned the hand as an example, and the house, chest, belly of slave-girl, and sheep are like the hand. And his statement 'from property' is also an example, and goods and pregnancy in the belly are like property. So if she says 'on what is in the belly of my slave-girl or my sheep from pregnancy', she returns the mahr. In al-Muhit: If she made khul' with him on the mahr he owed her, then it becomes clear that nothing remained of the mahr, she must return the mahr because he divorced her with the hope of what was specified, so it does not occur gratuitously. If he knew that he had no debt to her and that there were no goods in the house in the matter of 'on what is in the house of goods', nothing is required of her because she did not make him hopeful, so he was not deceived. End. In the second, she mentioned the plural and there is no maximum and its minimum is three, so the minimum is required, just as if he admitted to dirhams or bequeathed dirhams. An objection was raised that 'min' is partitive, so one or two dirhams should be required. The answer is that here it is for explanation because the principle is that every place where the speech is complete by itself but contains a kind of ambiguity, then 'min' is for explanation; otherwise it is partitive. And her statement 'make khul' with me on what is in my hand' is complete speech by itself, so it is permissible to limit to it. And there is no difference in the ruling between mentioning the plural with indefinite or definite. An objection was raised that if it is definite, only one should be required because the definite plural is like the definite singular, as if he swore not to buy the slaves or the women. The answer is that it refers to the genus only if devoid of a stipulation of covenant, as in the two examples, and here the stipulation of covenant exists, which is her saying 'on what is in my hand'; thus in al-Kafi. And al-Fath al-Qadir clarified: Because her saying 'on what is in my hand' indicates that the named thing is contained in her hand, and it is general covering dirhams and others, so by dirhams it becomes a covenant in general insofar as it is among what the word 'what' is true of, and it is ambiguous, and 'min' is a clarification of it, and its object is that which clarifies the specific container, and dirhams are an example. And the intent is that she clarified the ambiguous with a plural, like dinars. And it should be that her saying 'on what is in this house from sheep, horses, mules, or donkeys' likewise requires three of the named. Then I saw in al-Mi'raj: but he added clothes, and there is consideration due to extreme ignorance. And he qualified with his saying 'and there is nothing in her hand' because if there was in her hand valuable property, even a little or a lot, it is for him, and she does not have to return the mahr in the first case. As for the second, she must have in her hand what she named, so if she had one or two dirhams, she must complete the three; thus in al-Khaniyyah and al-Mabsut. By this it is known that in the author's speech there is looseness because the absence of anything in her hand is a condition for returning the mahr in the first, and the absence of three is a condition in the second, and his speech does not indicate that. And his statement 'she returns the mahr' indicates that it is received, so it indicates that if it was not received, she is released from it and nothing is required of her, as al-Imadi mentioned in his chapters and in al-Jawharah. Then when the recovery of the mahr is required for him and she had discharged him from it, he does not recover anything from her because the very thing he deserves has been delivered to him by the discharge, so if he recovered from her due to a gift, and the gift does not necessitate a guarantee from the donor. End. In al-Bazzaziyyah: The conclusion is that if the husband returns what is not valuable, nothing is required; if he named an existing known thing, the named thing is required; if he named something unknown that can be resolved, similarly; and if the ignorance is extreme and risk is possible, such as khul' on what her palm tree will produce this year or on what is in the house of goods and there is nothing, the specification becomes invalid and she returns what she received. End. It is qualified by khul' because if a master freed his slave on what is in his hand of dirhams and there is nothing in his hand, he must pay his value, because the benefits of the vulva are not valuable at the time of exit, so it is not required that the named thing be known, unlike the slave for he is valuable in himself, and unlike marriage where the dower is required because it is valuable at the time of entry; thus in al-Bada'i. And the first issue indicates that if he made khul' with her on a specific slave, for example, and it had died before the khul', he recovers from her the mahr he took from her due to deception, unlike if it died after, where its value is required, just as if it is subject to prior right or his freedom becomes apparent, it is like its death before khul', so he recovers from her the mahr.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This is a commentary (expansion probe) on the matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The matn states: 'If she adds from property or from dirhams, she returns her mahr or three dirhams.' The commentator explains the two cases: If the wife says 'make khul' on what is in my hand of property (mal)' and her hand is empty, she must return the mahr she received. If she says 'of dirhams' and her hand is empty, she must return three dirhams. The reasoning from al-Hidayah is that in the first case, 'mal' is vague; the husband did not agree without compensation, and it is impossible to impose the named thing (unknown) or its value (unknown) or the value of the vulva (mahr al-mithl) because it is not valued at the time of exit; so the only option is to impose what was established on him (i.e., the mahr she got). In the second case, 'dirhams' is a known genus, but the plural indicates a minimum of three, similar to confession or bequest. The commentary then addresses objections about the word 'min' (whether it indicates partitive or explanatory) and about whether the plural definite requires three or one. It concludes that 'min' is for explanation because the sentence is complete but ambiguous, and the definite plural here is not for genus but for covenant indicated by 'in my hand'. A qualification from al-Khulasa: if the wife knew there was nothing, then no compensation is required because she did not deceive. The passage also discusses the condition that the mahr was actually received; if not, she is discharged. Further, if the husband was released from the obligation (ibra), he cannot recover. From al-Bazzaziyyah: a summary of scenarios: if the compensation is not valuable, nothing; if known existing, the named; if unknown but resolvable, likewise; if extremely unknown, specification invalid and she returns what she took. The commentator then distinguishes khul' from freeing a slave: in khul', the compensation can be unknown because the vulva is not valuable, unlike a slave. Finally, an example with a specific slave: if it died before khul', she returns mahr due to deception; if after, she pays its value. Authority weight: The matn is from Kanz al-Daqaiq (a later work), but the commentary cites al-Hidayah and others which are from the established madhhab. The rulings are mufta bihi.

Key Terms
مال (mal): Property in a general sense; here it is distinguished from dirhams specifically.
غرور (ghurur): Deception; here, when the wife makes the husband think she has something valuable, he divorces based on that hope.
جمع محلي (jamm' muhalla): A plural noun with the definite article (al-); its legal effect in commands and statements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife says 'make khul' with me on what is in my hand of dirhams' but she has nothing, how much must she pay according to the Hanafi school?
A) Nothing, because there is nothing.
B) One dirham, because it is the minimum of singularity.
C) Three dirhams, because the plural minimum is three.
D) Mahr al-mithl, because the compensation is unknown.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi khul', the compensation is determined by the type of specification: 'mal' leads to returning the mahr; 'dirhams' leads to three dirhams, and the husband's knowledge of emptiness cancels the obligation.
